Free Trade Agreement  between the United Mexican States and the Republics of El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras

PREAMBLE
The United Mexican States, the Republic of El Salvador, the Republic of Guatemala and the Republic of Honduras.
RESOLVED TO:
STRENGTHEN the bonds of friendship and the existing spirit of cooperation between their peoples:
ACCELERATE and promote the revitalization of American integration schemes;
ACHIEVE a better balance in your business relationships;
CONTRIBUTE to harmonious development, the expansion of world trade and the expansion of international cooperation;
PROMOTE a more extensive and secure market for the goods produced and the reciprocal exchange of services in their territories;
INCREASE the competitiveness of the services sector, to consolidate the competitiveness of the countries in the free trade zone;
REDUCE the provisions in your reciprocal trade;
ESTABLISH a legal framework with clear and mutually beneficial rules for the promotion and protection of investments, as well as to facilitate the commercial exchange of their goods and services;
ENSURE a predictable commercial framework for the planning of productive activities and investment;
DEVELOP the provisions of the Marrakesh Agreement Establishing the World Trade Organization (WTO Agreement), as well as other bilateral and multilateral integration and cooperation instruments;
STRENGTHEN the competitiveness of their companies in world markets;
PROTECT intellectual property rights;
CREATE employment opportunities and improve living standards in their respective territories;  PROMOTE economic development consistent with the protection and conservation of the environment, as well as sustainable development;
PRESERVE its ability to safeguard the public welfare; Y
PROMOTE the dynamic participation of the different economic agents, particularly the private sector, in efforts aimed at deepening their economic relations;
CELEBRATE THIS FREE TRADE AGREEMENT
Chapter I INITIAL PROVISIONS
Article 1-01 Establishment of the free trade zone. The Parties establish a free trade area in accordance with the provisions of Article XXIV of the GATT 1994 and Article V of the GATS.
Article 1-02 Objectives.
1. The objectives of this treaty, specifically developed through its principles and rules, are the following:
a) stimulate the expansion and diversification of trade in goods and services between the Parties;
b) promote conditions of free competition within the free trade zone;
c) eliminate barriers to trade and facilitate the circulation of originating goods and services between the Parties;
d) remove barriers to the movement of capital and business persons between the territories of the Parties;
e) increase investment opportunities in the territories of the Parties;
f) protect and enforce, adequately and effectively, intellectual property rights in the territory of the Parties;
g) establish guidelines for further cooperation between the Parties, aimed at expanding and improving the benefits of this treaty; Y
h) create effective procedures for the application and compliance of this treaty, for its joint administration and for the settlement of disputes.
2. The Parties shall interpret and apply the provisions of this Agreement in light of the objectives set out in paragraph 1 and in accordance with the applicable rules of international law.
Article 1-03 Relationship with other international treaties and agreements.
1. The Parties confirm the rights and obligations in force between them under the WTO Agreement and other treaties and agreements to which they are party.
2. In case of inconsistency between the provisions of the treaties and agreements referred to in paragraph 1 and the provisions of this treaty, the latter shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 1-04 Scope of application.
The provisions of this treaty apply between Mexico and El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras. This treaty does not apply between El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras.
Article 1-05 Observance of the treaty.
Each Party shall ensure, in accordance with its constitutional norms, compliance with the provisions of this treaty in its territory, at the federal or central, state or departmental and municipal level, except in cases where this treaty provides otherwise.
Article 1-06 Succession of treaties.
Any reference to any other international treaty or agreement shall be understood to be made in the same terms to a successor treaty or agreement to which the Parties are party.
Article 1-07 Annexes.
The annexes to this treaty constitute an integral part of it.
Chapter II GENERAL DEFINITIONS
Article 2-0 Definitions of General Application.
For the purposes of this treaty, unless otherwise provided, it shall be understood as:
TRIPS Agreement : the Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights, which is part of the WTO Agreement;
GATS : the General Agreement on Trade in Services, which is part of the WTO Agreement;
WTO Agreement: the Marrakesh Agreement Establishing the World Trade Organization, dated April 15, 1994;
customs duty : any import tax, duty or tribute and any charge of any kind applied in connection with the importation of goods, including any form of surcharge or additional charge on imports, except:
a) any charge equivalent to an internal tax established in accordance with Article III:2 of the GATT 1994, with respect to like goods, direct competitors or substitutes of the Party, or with respect to goods from which it has been manufactured or produced all or part of the imported good;
b) any countervailing duty;
c) any duty or other charge related to importation, proportional to the cost of the services rendered; Y
d) any premium offered or collected on imported goods, derived from any bidding system, regarding the administration of quantitative restrictions on imports or tariffs-quota or tariff preference quotas;
good : products or merchandise as understood in the GATT 1994, whether originating or not;
good of a Party : national products as understood in the GATT 1994, those goods that the Parties agree upon, and includes originating goods. A good of a Party may incorporate materials from other countries;
originating good or originating material : a good or a material that qualifies as originating in accordance with the provisions of Chapter VI;
Customs Valuation Code : the Agreement Relating to the Application of Article VII of the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade of 1994, including its interpretative notes, which is part of the Agreement on the WTO;
Commission : the Administrative Commission established in accordance with article 18-01; countervailing duty: "countervailing duty" as defined in Chapter IX; days: calendar or calendar days;
business : an entity incorporated or organized under applicable law, whether or not for profit and privately or government owned, including companies, foundations, partnerships, trusts, shares, sole proprietorships, joint ventures, or other associations;
State enterprise : an enterprise that is owned or controlled by a Party through equity participation;
enterprise of a Party : an enterprise incorporated or organized under the laws of a Party;
existing : in force at the entry into force of this treaty;
tariff fraction : the breakdown of a Harmonized System tariff classification code to more than six digits;
GATT 1994 : the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade of 1994, which is part of the WTO Agreement;
measure : any law, regulation, procedure, provision or administrative practice, among others;
national : a natural person who has the nationality of a Party in accordance with its applicable law;  Party : any State for which this treaty has entered into force;  Exporting Party : the Party from whose territory a good or service is exported;  Importing Party : the Party into whose territory a good or service is imported;
heading : a Harmonized System tariff classification code at the four-digit level;
person : a physical or natural person, or a company;
person of a Party : a national or company of a Party;
Tariff Reduction Program : the one established in paragraph 5 of article 3-04 and in paragraph 1 of article 4-04;
Secretariat : the Secretariat established in accordance with article 18-02;
SAC : the Central American Tariff System used by the member countries of the General Treaty of Central American Economic Integration, based on the Harmonized System of Designation and Coding of Goods;  Harmonized System : the Harmonized Commodity Description and Coding System in force, including its general rules and its section, chapter and subheading legal notes, in the manner in which the Parties have adopted it in their respective legislations; subheading: a Harmonized System tariff classification code at the six-digit level;
territory : for each Party, as defined in Annex 2-01.
Annex 2-01 Country Specific Definitions
For the purposes of this treaty, unless otherwise provided, it shall be understood as:
territory :
a) with respect to Mexico:
i) the states of the Federation and the Federal District;
ii) islands, including reefs and cays in adjacent seas;
iii) the islands of Guadalupe and Revillagigedo, located in the Pacific Ocean;
iv) the continental platform and the submarine bases of the islands, cays and reefs;
v) the waters of the territorial seas, to the extent and terms established by international law, and internal maritime waters;
vi) the space located on the national territory, with the extension and modalities established by international law itself; Y
vii) any area beyond the territorial seas of Mexico within which Mexico may exercise rights over the seabed and subsoil and over the natural resources they contain, in accordance with international law, including the United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea, as well as with its internal legislation; Y
b) with respect to El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras: the terrestrial, maritime and air space of each Party, as well as their exclusive economic zones and their continental shelves, over which they exercise sovereign rights and jurisdiction, in accordance with their legislation and the law international.
Chapter III
NATIONAL TREATMENT AND MARKET ACCESS OF GOODS
Article 3-01
Definitions .
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
industrial goods : a good that is not considered as agricultural, according to the definition of chapter IV;
consumed :
a) actually consumed; either
b) processed or manufactured in such a way that it gives rise to a substantial change in the value, form or use of a good or to the production of another good;
material : "material" as defined in Chapter VI;
samples without commercial value :
a) raw materials and goods whose dimensions, quantities, weight, volume or presentation are such as to indicate, without a doubt, that they are not usable for anything other than demonstration or proof;
b) the objects of common materials fixed on cards, supports or clearly presented as samples according to the uses of the trade;
c) raw materials and goods, as well as the leftovers in these raw materials or goods, which have been rendered useless for anything other than demonstration, by laceration, perforation, placement of indelible marks or any other effective means to avoid any possibility to be commercialized; Y
d) Goods that cannot be conditioned in the form of samples without commercial value, according to the provisions of subparagraphs a) to c), consisting of:
i) non-consumable goods, with a unit value not greater than 10 United States dollars, which are made up of unique specimens of each series or quality; Y
ii) consumable goods with a unit value of no more than 10 United States dollars, even composed totally or partially of specimens of the same type or quality, provided that the quantity and manner of presentation of said samples exclude any possibility of commercialization .
Article 3-02 Scope of application .
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, this Chapter applies to trade in goods between the Parties.
Article 3-03 National Treatment .
1. Each Party shall grant national treatment to the goods of another Party, in accordance with Article III of the GATT 1994, including its interpretative notes. For this purpose, Article III of the GATT 1994 and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this treaty and are an integral part thereof.
2. The provisions of paragraph 1 mean, with respect to a state, department or municipality, a treatment no less favorable than the most favorable treatment that that state, department or municipality grants to any similar goods, direct competitors or substitutes, as the case may be. of the Party of which they are members.
3. Paragraphs 1 and 2 do not apply to the measures indicated in annex 3-03 and 3-09.
Article 3-04 Tariff relief .
1. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, neither Party may increase any existing customs duty, or adopt any new customs duty, on originating goods subject to the Tariff Elimination Program.1 ,2
2. Notwithstanding any other provision of this Agreement, with respect to goods excluded from the Tariff Elimination Program, any Party may maintain or adopt a prohibition or restriction, or a customs duty on the importation of those goods, in accordance with its rights and obligations derived from the WTO Agreement.
3. Once a year from the entry into force of this treaty, the Parties will examine, through the Committee, the possibility of incorporating the goods excluded from it into the Tariff Reduction Program. The agreements through which these goods are incorporated into the Tariff Elimination Program will be adopted by the Parties in accordance with their legal procedures.
4. Paragraph 1 is not intended to prevent a Party from creating a new tariff item, provided that the customs duty applicable to the corresponding originating goods is not greater than that applicable to the item item itemized.
5. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, each Party shall eliminate its customs duties on originating goods, in accordance with the provisions of Annex 3-04(5).3  6. At the request of any of the Parties, consultations will be held to examine the possibility of accelerating the elimination of customs duties provided for in the Tariff Elimination Program.
7. Once approved by the Parties, in accordance with their legal procedures, the agreement adopted based on paragraph 6, regarding the accelerated elimination of the customs duty on an originating good, shall prevail over any customs duty or category of relief applicable in accordance with the Tariff Elimination Program for that good.
8. The Parties agree to set customs duties on industrial goods contained in the Tariff Elimination Program in terms of ad-valorem taxes.
Article 3-05 Customs duty refund programs on exported goods, customs duty deferral programs, and customs duty exemption programs applied to exported goods.
1. Regarding refunds and exemption from customs duties, the Parties shall retain their rights and obligations in accordance with their legislation and the WTO Agreement.
2. When 25% of the domestic industry of a Party considers itself affected by the refund and tariff exemption mechanisms established in another Party, they shall hold consultations in order to reach a mutually satisfactory solution.
Article 3-06 Temporary importation of goods .
1. Each Party shall authorize the temporary importation without payment of customs duty of the goods listed below and that are imported from the territory of another Party into its territory, regardless of their origin and that are available in the territory of that Party. similar goods, direct competitors or substitutes:
a) professional equipment necessary for the exercise of the activity, trade or profession of a business person;
b) equipment for the press or for the broadcast of radio or television signals and cinematographic equipment;
c) goods for sporting purposes or intended for exhibition or demonstration, including components, auxiliary devices and accessories; Y
d) commercial samples and publicity films.
2. Except as otherwise provided in this agreement, the Parties may subject the temporary importation without payment of customs duty, of a good of the type indicated in subparagraphs a), b) or c) of paragraph 1 to any of the following conditions, without the possibility of adopting additional conditions, when:
a) the good is imported by a national or resident of another Party;
b) the property is used exclusively by the visiting person, or under his personal supervision, in the performance of his activity, trade or profession;
c) the good is not subject to sale, lease or assignment in any other way while it remains in its territory under the temporary importation regime;
d) the good is accompanied by a bond or guarantee that does not exceed 110% of the charges that would be owed, as the case may be, for the final entry or importation, or by another form of guarantee, refundable at the time of re-exportation of the good , except that no bond or guarantee may be required for customs duties on an originating good;
e) the good is susceptible to identification by any reasonable means established by the customs legislation of each Party;
f) the good is re-exported upon the departure of that person or within the period corresponding to the purpose of temporary importation;
g) the good is imported in quantities not greater than what is reasonable according to the intended use and in accordance with the customs legislation of each Party;
h) the good does not undergo any transformation or modification during the authorized import term, except for wear and tear due to normal use of the good; Y
i) the good complies with the sanitary and phytosanitary measures and with the applicable standardization measures, in accordance with the provisions of chapters V and XV, respectively.
3. Except as otherwise provided in this agreement, the Parties may subject the temporary importation without payment of the customs duty plus other charges that are charged due to importation, of a good of the type indicated in literal d) of paragraph 1, to any of the following conditions, without additional conditions being able to be adopted when:
a) the good is imported only for the purposes of placing orders for goods or services that are supplied from the territory of another Party or from a non-Party country;
b) the property is not subject to sale, lease or assignment in any other way, and is used only for demonstration or exhibition while it remains in its territory;
c) the good is accompanied by a bond or guarantee that does not exceed 110% of the charges that would be owed in its case for the definitive entry or importation, or of another form of guarantee, refundable at the time of export of the good, except that no bond or guarantee may be required for customs duties on an originating good;
d) the good is susceptible to identification by any reasonable means established by the customs legislation of each Party;
e) the good is re-exported within a term that reasonably corresponds to the purpose of temporary importation, in accordance with the terms established by the customs legislation of each Party;
f) the good is imported in quantities not greater than what is reasonable according to the intended use and in accordance with the customs legislation of each Party;
g) the good does not undergo any transformation or modification during the authorized import period, except for wear and tear due to the normal use of the good; Y
h) the good complies with the sanitary and phytosanitary measures and with the applicable standardization measures, in accordance with the provisions of chapters V and XV, respectively.
4. When a good is temporarily imported and does not comply with any of the conditions that a Party imposes in accordance with paragraphs 2 and 3, that Party may apply the customs duties and any other charges that would be due for final entry or importation. of the same.
Article 3-07 Free import of customs duty for samples without commercial value.
Each Party shall authorize the free import of samples with no commercial value from the territory of another Party.
Article 3-08 Customs valuation .
1. Upon the entry into force of this treaty, the customs value of an imported good shall be determined in accordance with the principles of the Customs Valuation Code.
2. Pursuant to Article 13 of the Customs Valuation Code, if in the course of determining the customs value of imported goods it is necessary to delay the final determination of that value, the importer may remove them from customs if, when so required, provide a deposit or other form of security provided by the law of the Party. This form will cover the payment of the taxes to which the assets would ultimately be subject.
3. Each Party shall establish the appropriate documentation to prove that the customs value is correct, which shall not be greater than what can reasonably be requested to comply with Article VII of the GATT 1994.
4. When a Party uses or applies estimated prices, it shall establish exemption mechanisms from the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3. Likewise, it shall establish the measures that facilitate the administration of said scheme.
5. Before a Party adopts or modifies the estimated price referred to in this article, it shall communicate to the other Parties the description of the good, its tariff fraction, and the estimated price that it intends to establish.
6. The Parties shall hold consultations with each other, so that the foregoing does not hinder trade.
7. The Parties understand that the estimated price referred to in paragraph 4 will serve only as a reference for valuation cases, and may not be considered as the base price for the determination of the internal taxes of each Party or for the application of duties or customs duties.
Article 3-09 Import and export restrictions.
1. Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, no Party may adopt or maintain any prohibition or restriction on the import of any good of another Party or on the export or sale for export of any good destined for the territory of another Party, except as provided for in Article XI of the GATT 1994, including its interpretative notes. For this purpose, Article XI of the GATT 1994 and its interpretative notes are incorporated into this treaty and are an integral part thereof.
2. The Parties understand that the rights and obligations of the GATT 1994 incorporated in paragraph 1, prohibit export price requirements and, except as permitted for the application of resolutions and commitments regarding countervailing duties, import price requirements. .
3. The Parties understand that the rights and obligations incorporated in paragraph 1 prohibit, among others, but not limited to:
a) quantitative restrictions on imports, according to the parameters of paragraph 1;
b) prices or minimum values;
c) voluntary export restraints when they do not result from an agreement consistent with the Agreement on the Application of Article VI of the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade of 1994, which forms part of the WTO Agreement;
d) the granting of import licenses with the condition that the importer acquires national production;
e) the granting of import licenses on the condition that the importer exports; Y
f) the granting of import licenses on the condition that the good to be imported includes a certain percentage of content from the importing Party.
4. In cases where a Party adopts or maintains a prohibition or restriction on the import or export of goods from or to a non-Party, nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to prevent it from:
a) limit or prohibit the importation of the goods of the non-Party country, from the territory of another Party; either
b) require as a condition for the export of those goods from the Party to the territory of another Party, that they not be re-exported to the non-Party country, directly or indirectly, without being consumed in the territory of another Party.
5. In the event that a Party adopts or maintains a prohibition or restriction on the import of a good from a non-Party country, at the request of any of them, the Parties shall consult in order to avoid interference or undue distortion in the mechanisms pricing, marketing and distribution in another Party.
6. Paragraphs 1 to 4 do not apply to the measures set out in Annex 3-03 and 3-09.
Article 3-10 Registration of importers.
If, as a result of the application and administration of a registry of importers, a Party considers that the access of a good of that Party to the territory of the Party that applies the measure is hindered or prevented, both Parties shall hold consultations in order to reach a mutually satisfactory solution.
Article 3-11 Customs measures.
Each Party shall ensure that the application, administration, and publication of customs measures are in accordance with the provisions of this Agreement, its legislation, and the WTO Agreement.
Article 3-12 Establishment of specific customs.
1. When a Party contemplates the establishment of limitations on the customs clearance of certain types of goods to specific customs, it will consult with the other Parties to avoid that they could affect its interests in accordance with this treaty.
2. The Party that establishes such limitations will allow the entry of the goods into its territory, through any of the legally established border posts, so that the goods reach the specific customs office for the respective clearance, provided they comply with the corresponding customs formalities. .
Article 3-13 Customs processing fees.
No Party shall increase or establish any customs duty for the service rendered by customs and shall eliminate such duties on originating goods upon the entry into force of this Agreement.
Article 3-14 Export taxes.
1. Except as provided in this Article and in Annex 3-14, no Party shall adopt or maintain any tax, customs duty, or charge on the export of any good destined for consumption in the territory of another Party, unless they are adopted or keep on said good when it is destined for internal consumption.
2. For the purposes of this paragraph, "temporarily" shall be understood to mean up to one year, or a longer period agreed by the Parties. Notwithstanding paragraph 1, each Party may adopt or maintain a tax, levy or charge on exports to the territory of another Party if such tax, levy or charge is applied temporarily for:
a) alleviate a critical shortage of a food item; either
b) ensure to a national transformation industry the supply of the essential quantities of raw materials during the periods in which the national price is maintained at a level lower than the world price in execution of a governmental stabilization plan, provided that such taxes, liens or charges:
i) do not have the consequence of increasing the exports of that national industry;
ii) do not have the effect of increasing the protection granted to said national industry;
iii) do not go against the provisions of this treaty relating to non-discrimination; Y
iv) are sustained only for the period necessary to maintain the integrity of the stabilization plan.
3. The Parties may hold consultations in relation to the application of the provisions of this article, tending to the application of measures that seek to avoid unwanted effects in the application of a domestic food aid program.
Article 3-15 Country of Origin Marking.
Annex 3-15 applies to measures related to country of origin marking.
Article 3-16 Distinctive products.
Regarding distinctive products, the Parties shall be subject to the provisions of Annex 3-16.
Article 3-17 Publication and notification.
1. Neither Party shall apply before its official publication any measure of a general nature adopted by that Party that has the effect of increasing a customs duty or other charge on the importation of goods of another Party, or that imposes a new or more onerous measure, restriction or prohibition for imports, or that establishes or increases non-tariff type restrictions and prohibitions on imports of goods from another Party or for transfers of funds related to them.
2. Each Party shall identify, in terms of the tariff fractions and the nomenclature that corresponds to them in accordance with their respective rates, the measures, restrictions or prohibitions on the import or export of goods for reasons of national security, public health, preservation of the flora or fauna, the environment, sanitary and phytosanitary regulations, standards, labels, technical regulations, international commitments, public order requirements or any other regulations.
Article 3-18 Committee on Trade in Goods.
1. The Parties establish the Committee on Trade in Goods, made up of a principal representative and an alternate designated by each Party. The representatives designated by the Parties must be officials in charge of handling matters related to this chapter.
2. The Committee will be integrated upon the entry into force of the treaty and at the request of any Party, it will hold its first meeting within a period not exceeding 60 days after its integration. The Committee will meet ordinarily once a year, and extraordinarily at the request of any Party.
3. Except in the case of extraordinary meetings, for ordinary meetings the Committee will be successively chaired by each Party, with the Party holding the presidency making the call at least 30 days in advance and proposing the agenda of the topics. to treat. It will also have the role of rapporteur.
4. When one of the Parties considers that another Party contravenes the provisions of may request in writing an extraordinary meeting of the Committee, which must be notified to the other Parties. The request must contain the specific measure and provision that the Party considers to be in violation of the treaty. The extraordinary meeting may be held when attended by at least the representatives of the requesting Party and the requested Party and it will take place in the country to which the request for consultations was made. The results derived from the extraordinary meeting do not prejudge, nor will they affect the rights of any Party that did not participate in said meeting.
5. Unless the Parties agree otherwise, the extraordinary meeting may be considered consultations under Article 19-05. Likewise, in the event that a Party does not respond within the five days following the date on which the request for the extraordinary meeting was received, it does not hold or does not intend to hold the extraordinary meeting within a Within a period of no more than 15 days, or another mutually agreed period, counted from the date of receipt of the request, said Party may request a meeting of the Commission, in accordance with Article 19-06.
Article 3-19 Levels of temporary flexibility.
Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 3-04, preferential tariff treatment shall be granted in accordance with Annex 3-19.
Annex 3-03 and 3-09 Exceptions to articles 3-03 and 3-09 
Section A Measures of El Salvador
1. Notwithstanding the provisions of article 3-09, El Salvador, consistent with its obligations in the WTO, may adopt prohibitions or restrictions on the importation of the following goods:
a) used and retreaded tires included in tariff heading 40.12;
b) Used vehicles, automobiles, tractors, cycles and other land vehicles, together with their parts and accessories included in Chapter 87;
c) used clothing items included in tariff headings 63.09 and 63.10; Y
d) sacks (bags) and sacks used for packaging, made of jute or other textile fibers, classified in tariff subheading 6305.10.
Section B Guatemala Measures
1. Notwithstanding what is established in Article 3-09, Guatemala may adopt or maintain measures related to the export of round or carved logs and sawn wood with dimensions greater than eleven centimeters thick, in accordance with the provisions of the Forest Law, Legislative Decree number 101-96.
2. Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 3-09, Guatemala may adopt or maintain measures related to the export of coffee, in accordance with the provisions of the Coffee Law, Legislative Decree number 19-69.
3. Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 3-09, Guatemala may adopt or maintain import price requirements for the importation of used goods described in the following headings and subheadings:  (Descriptions are provided for reference purposes.)
Annex 3-14 Export Taxes
The provisions of paragraph 1 of article 3-14 will not apply to Honduras for bananas, which will be progressively deducted until reaching 0.04 United States dollars per box exported, subjecting the rest of the tariff universe to the provisions of this article.
Annex 3 -15 Country of Origin Marking
1. For the purposes of this annex, it shall be understood as:
final buyer : the last person who, in the territory of the importing Party, acquires a good in the form in which it is imported. This buyer is not necessarily the final user of the good;
container : a container, packaging, packaging or wrapping, among others;
common container : the container in which the good will usually arrive at the final purchaser; legible: capable of being read easily;
Sufficient permanence : that the mark will remain on the good until it reaches the final purchaser, unless it is intentionally removed;
customs value : the value of a good for the purpose of imposing import taxes on an imported good; Y
visible : that can be seen with the ordinary handling of the good or container.
2. Each Party shall apply the provisions relating to country of origin marking in accordance with Article IX of the GATT 1994.
3. Each Party may require that a good from another Party imported into its territory bear a country of origin mark that indicates the name of the latter to the final buyer of the good.
4. Each Party may require, among its general consumer information measures, that an imported good bear the country of origin mark in the manner prescribed for goods of the importing Party.
5. Each Party, when adopting, maintaining and applying any country of origin marking measure, shall minimize the difficulties and costs that such measure may cause to the trade and industry of another Party.
6. Each Party:
a) accept any reasonable method of marking a good of another Party, such as the use of adhesive or pressure labels, tags or paint, which ensures that the mark is visible, legible and of sufficient permanence; Y
b) exempt from the country of origin marking requirement of a good of another Party that:
i) is not capable of being marked;
ii) cannot be marked prior to export to the territory of another Party without damaging it;
iii) cannot be marked except at a cost that is substantial in relation to its customs value, so as to discourage its export to the territory of another Party;
iv) cannot be marked without material impairment of its operation or substantial deterioration of its appearance;
v) is in a container marked in such a way as to reasonably indicate the origin of the good to the final buyer;
vi) is raw material;
vii) will be produced in the territory of the importing Party, by the importer or on its behalf, in such a way that the good becomes the good of the importing Party;
viii) due to its nature or the circumstances of its importation, the final buyer can reasonably know its country of origin, even if it is not marked;
ix) has been produced 20 years or more before importation;
x) has been imported without the required marking and cannot be subsequently marked except at a cost that is substantial in relation to its customs value, provided that the omission of marking was not for the purpose of circumventing the country of origin marking requirements ;
xi) is in transit, in guarantee or at the disposal of the customs authority, for purposes of temporary importation without payment of customs duties; either
xii) is an original work of art.
7. With the exception of the goods described in subparagraphs vi), vii), viii), ix), xi), and xii), of subparagraph b) of paragraph 6, a Party may provide that when a good is exempt from the requirement country of origin marking, in accordance with subparagraph b) of paragraph 6, the common outer container is marked so as to indicate the country of origin of the good it contains.
8. Each Party shall provide that:
a) a common container that is imported empty, disposable or not, will not require the marking of its country of origin, but the container in which it is imported may be required to be marked with the country of origin of its content; Y
b) a full common container, disposable or not, will not require the marking of its country of origin, but may be required to be marked with the name of the country of origin of its contents, unless its contents are already marked and the container can be easily opened for inspection, or the marking of the contents is clearly visible through the container.
9. Whenever administratively and legally feasible, each Party shall allow the importer to mark a good of another Party after importing it, but before releasing it from the control or custody of customs authorities, unless the importer has committed repeated violations of the country of origin marking requirements of the Party and has been previously notified in writing that the good must be marked prior to importation.
10. Each Party shall provide that, except for importers who have been notified in accordance with paragraph 8, no special assessment or penalty shall be imposed for failure to comply with that Party's country of origin marking requirements, unless that the goods are withdrawn from the control or custody of the customs authorities without having been adequately marked, or they have been affixed marks that lead to error.
11. The Parties shall cooperate and consult with each other on matters related to this Annex, including additional exemptions from the country of origin marking requirement.
Exhibit 3-16 Distinctive Products
El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras will recognize tequila and mezcal as distinctive products of Mexico for the purposes of standards and labeling. Consequently, El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras will not allow the sale of any product such as tequila or mezcal, unless they have been made in Mexico in accordance with their laws and regulations, related to the production of tequila and mezcal.
Annex 3-19 Levels of Temporary Flexibility between Mexico and El Salvador and Guatemala
1. Mexico will grant to the threads and fabrics classified in Chapters 52, 54 to 56 and 58 to 60 of the Harmonized System, produced in the territory of El Salvador or Guatemala in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 4 and imported into their territory, the preferential tariff treatment established in the Tariff Elimination Program corresponding to originating goods up to the amounts and terms specified below:
a) for Guatemala: 7,500,000 United States dollars per year for a period of four years from the entry into force of the treaty; Y
b) for El Salvador: 2,500,000 United States dollars per year for a period of four years from the entry into force of the treaty.
2. Mexico will grant artificial or synthetic fiber sweaters classified in subheading 6110.30 of the Harmonized System; to pantyhose-stockings classified under heading 61.15 of the Harmonized System and to 100% viscose rayon tablecloths, classified under subheading 6302.53 of the Harmonized System, produced in the territory of El Salvador or Guatemala in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 4 and imported into its territory, the preferential tariff treatment established in the Tariff Elimination Program corresponding to originating goods up to the amounts and terms specified below:
a) for Guatemala: 500,000 United States dollars per year for a period of four years from the entry into force of the treaty; Y
b) for El Salvador: 500,000 United States dollars per year for a period of four years from the entry into force of the treaty.
3. Guatemala will grant threads and fabrics classified in chapters 52, 54 to 56 and 58 to 60 of the Harmonized System, produced in the territory of Mexico in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 4 and imported into its territory, the preferential tariff treatment established in the Tariff Reduction Program corresponding to original goods up to 7,500,000 United States dollars per year or its equivalent in quetzales for a period of four years from the entry into force of the treaty.
4. For the purposes of the amounts established in this annex, the applicable rules of origin will be those that appear in annex 6-26.
5. The annual amounts established in this annex will be allocated as follows:
a) in the case of El Salvador, they may not be assigned to assets classified in a certain heading, in an amount that exceeds 25% of the total annual amount, except for heading 55.13, which will not exceed 45%;
b) in the case of Guatemala, they may not be assigned to assets classified in a certain heading, in an amount that exceeds 20% of the total annual amount, except for heading 52.08 which will not exceed 45%; Y
c) For imports from Guatemala from Mexico, they may not be assigned to goods classified in a certain heading, in an amount that exceeds 25% of the total annual amount.
6. The Party into whose territory the goods indicated in this annex are imported, shall administer the amounts indicated therein in accordance with its legislation.
7. The assets indicated in this annex and in annex 6-26 will be subject to the provisions of chapter VII.
Chapter IV  AGRICULTURAL SECTOR
Article 4-01 Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
MFN tariff : the most favored nation tariff;
agricultural good : a good classified in any of the following chapters, headings or subheadings of the Harmonized System:
(Descriptions are provided for reference purposes)
export subsidies: those subsidies or subsidies contingent on export performance, including those listed in Article 9 of the Agreement on Agriculture, which is part of the WTO Agreement;  Customs rate for imports under quota : the customs duty that is paid within the volume negotiated as a quota; and  tariff rate for non-quota imports : the tariff rate applied to quantities in excess of the amount specified in a quota tariff.
Article 4-02 Scope of application .
1. This Chapter applies to measures adopted or maintained by any Party related to trade in agricultural goods.
2. In the event of any inconsistency between the provisions of this chapter and any other provision of this treaty, the provisions of this chapter shall control to the extent of the inconsistency.
Article 4-03 International obligations.
A Party, before adopting a measure pursuant to an intergovernmental agreement on goods, in accordance with subparagraph h) of Article XX of the GATT 1994 that may affect trade in agricultural goods between the Parties, must consult through the Committee on Agricultural Trade, established in Article 4-10, with another Party, to avoid the annulment or impairment of a concession granted by that Party in its list of the Tariff Elimination Program.
Article 4-04 Access to markets.
1. Notwithstanding the provisions of Article 4-02 and unless otherwise provided in this Agreement, the Parties shall progressively eliminate their customs duties on originating agricultural goods, in accordance with the provisions of Annex 3-04(5).
2. The Parties, at the request of any of them, will carry out consultations through the Committee, to examine the possibility of accelerating the elimination of customs duties provided for in the Tariff Elimination Program.
3. Once approved by the Parties, in accordance with their legal procedures, the agreement on the accelerated elimination of the customs duty on an originating good that is reached between the Parties, shall prevail over any customs duty or category of relief indicated in accordance with the Tariff Reduction Program for that good.
4. Notwithstanding any other provision of this Agreement, with respect to goods excluded from the Tariff Elimination Program, any Party may maintain or adopt a prohibition or restriction, or a customs duty on the importation of those goods, in accordance with its rights and obligations derived from the WTO Agreement.
5. Once a year from the entry into force of this agreement, the Parties will examine, through the Committee, the possibility of incorporating the goods excluded from it into the Tariff Reduction Program. The agreements through which these goods are incorporated into the Tariff Elimination Program will be adopted by the Parties in accordance with their legal procedures.
Article 4-05 Non-tariff measures.
Except as otherwise provided in this Agreement, neither Party shall adopt or maintain prohibitions or restrictions on the import and export of any agricultural good, or measures of the type set forth in Article 4.2 of the Agreement on Agriculture, which forms part of the Agreement. Agreement on the WTO, it has been prescribed that they be converted into ordinary customs duties, such as minimum import prices or values, discretionary import licensing regimes, quantitative restrictions on imports and similar measures applied at the border that do not are customs duties proper, in agricultural trade between the Parties.
Article 4-06 Internal aid.
1. The Parties recognize that domestic support measures can be important for their agricultural sectors, but that they can also distort trade and affect production. In this regard, the Parties will apply domestic support as established in the multilateral agricultural negotiations within the framework of the WTO Agreement and when a Party decides to support its agricultural producers, it will strive to move towards domestic support measures that:
a) have minimal or no distorting effects on trade or production; Y
b) are in full compliance with the provisions of Annex 2 of the Agreement on Agriculture, which is part of the WTO Agreement.
2. To guarantee transparency, the Committee will analyze, at least once a year, the status of all domestic support measures in the Parties, as well as any modification to these measures, seeking to assess compliance with the provisions of paragraph 1. Likewise, the Parties will exchange public information in a timely manner or at the request of the Party.
3. The application of any type of domestic support measures on an agricultural good, to the extent that they cause or threaten to cause damage to the production or trade of the other Party, may be subject to an investigation regarding unfair practices. of international trade and, where appropriate, be subject to the application of countervailing duties in accordance with Chapter IX.
Article 4-07 Domestic Food Aid.
1. The Party that establishes a domestic food aid program, in accordance with paragraph 4 of Annex 2 of the Agreement on Agriculture, which is part of the Agreement on the WTO, shall ensure, through the instruments it deems necessary, that the benefits of this program are received only by consumers of that Party.
2. At the request of a Party, consultations will be held to ensure compliance with the provisions of paragraph 1.
3. If no agreement is reached, the Parties shall refer to paragraph 3 of Article 4-06.
Article 4-08 Export subsidies.
Five years from the entry into force of this agreement, neither Party may maintain or adopt export subsidies on agricultural goods in their reciprocal trade.
Article 4-09 Special agricultural safeguard.
The Parties, with respect to the special agricultural safeguard, shall be subject to the provisions of Annex 4-09.
Article 4-10 Committee on Agricultural Trade.
1. The Parties establish the Committee on Agricultural Trade, made up of representatives of each of them, in accordance with Annex 4-10. The term for the integration of the Committee will not be greater than 90 days from the entry into force of this treaty and will be chaired by a representative of the country hosting the meeting.
2. The Committee may invite representatives of the private or academic sectors and officials of regional and sub-regional organizations to participate, depending on the topic dealt with in the meeting.
3. The Committee will ordinarily meet twice a year and extraordinarily as many times as necessary at the request of a Party. The resolutions of the Committee will be taken by consensus.
4. For the purpose of ordinary meetings, the host Party will convene the other Parties 30 days in advance, and they must acknowledge receipt thereof. For extraordinary meetings, the call time will depend on the urgency of the topic to be discussed.
5. The functions of the Committee include:
a) monitor compliance, application and correct interpretation of the provisions of this chapter;
b) serve as a discussion forum for the Parties to consult and resolve on aspects related to this chapter in coordination with the other committees, subcommittees, working groups or any other instance established in the treaty;
c) make pertinent recommendations to the Commission on matters within its competence;
d) coordinate the exchange of information on trade in agricultural goods between the Parties;
e) carry out an annual assessment of trade in agricultural goods between the Parties and present a report to the Commission;
f) promote cooperation for the application and administration of this chapter; Y
g) Any other functions entrusted to it by the Commission.
Article 4-11 Trade in sugar.
The Parties agree to establish a Sugar Analysis Committee, in accordance with Annex 4-11.
Annex 4-09 Special Agricultural Safeguard
Section A Special Agricultural Safeguard between El Salvador and Mexico
1. El Salvador, notwithstanding what is established in its List contained in annex 3-04(5), may adopt or maintain a bilateral special agricultural safeguard (SAE) in the form of a quota, on an agricultural good listed in this annex, with based on the following:
a) the tariff rate for imports under quota will be the result of applying the Tariff Reduction Program for the good in question, in accordance with the provisions of annex 3-04(5); Y
b) the tariff rate for non-quota imports will be the lower of the base rate and the prevailing MFN rate at the time of importation. 
2. No Party may, with respect to the same good, apply at the same time an SAE and a bilateral safeguard contemplated in Chapter VIII.  3. The application period of an SAE will be until the end of the calendar year.  4. This mechanism will be applied until the end of the Tariff Elimination Program.  5. The amount of the quota for the following goods will be:
Section B Special Agricultural Safeguard between Guatemala and Mexico
1. Guatemala may apply to the goods contained in literal a) of the appendix to this section, as of the second year of validity of the treaty, at the request of the interested party, a special agricultural safeguard (SAE) when all of the following three conditions are met:
a) the volume of imports of a good from Mexico has a weighted average share of Guatemala's total imports of that good in the last three calendar years, greater than that described in the appendix to this section;
b) Guatemala's imports from Mexico of the good in question have exceeded 10% of their average annual growth rate of the last three calendar years; Y
c) the average annual growth rate of the last three calendar years of Guatemala's imports from Mexico in said good is greater than 5%.
2. Mexico may apply for the goods contained in literal b) of the appendix to this section, from the second year of validity of the treaty, at the request of the interested party, an SAE when all of the following three conditions are met:
a) the volume of imports of a good from Guatemala has a weighted average share of total imports from Mexico of that good in the last three calendar years, greater than 5%;
b) the imports that Mexico makes from all over the world of the good in question have exceeded 10% of its average annual growth of the last three calendar years; Y
c) the average annual growth of the last three calendar years of imports that Mexico makes from all over the world of the good in question is greater than 5%.
3. The application of the SAE will consist of an increase in the tariff resulting from applying the Tariff Elimination Program, at the lower tariff between the MFN in force at the time of importation and the base rate indicated for said good in the Tariff Elimination Program.
4. The application of the SAE will not be subject to any compensation.
5. The duration of the SAE will be up to 12 months, extendable for up to 12 more months. The importing Party shall notify the other Party of its intention to extend said measure at least 30 days prior to its expiration.
6. Once an SAE has been applied, the importing Party may apply it again until a period equal to the duration of the measure in accordance with paragraph 5 has elapsed. This new measure may not last longer than 12 months.
7. Once the mechanism described in paragraphs 5 and 6 has been applied, neither Party may apply it again. Consequently, no Party may apply a SAE to a good in the appendix to this section for more than 24 months if the first time this mechanism was activated there was no extension pursuant to paragraph 5 or for more than 36 months if the SAE was applied. again according to paragraph 6.
8. A Party may apply an SAE during the reduction period established in the Tariff Reduction Program for each good, and up to three years after the respective reduction has ended.
9. Notwithstanding what is established in paragraphs 7 and 8, a Party may adopt and apply an SAE for the goods included in the appendix to this section, with the consent of the other.
10. A Party may not simultaneously adopt and apply an SAE and a bilateral safeguard, in accordance with Chapter VIII, with respect to the same good.
11. The SAE adopted by the importing Party will take effect from the day the measure is published in the dissemination body provided for in the legislation of the importing Party, incorporating the pertinent information that justifies its implementation.
12. Notwithstanding the application of the SAE, the Parties may hold consultations to exchange information and to try to reach mutually beneficial agreements.
13. Goods excluded from the Tariff Reduction Program will have the right to use this mechanism when they are incorporated into it. The terms for the application of the SAE to these assets will be reviewed on a case-by-case basis.
Section C  Special Agricultural Safeguard between Honduras and Mexico
1. Honduras may apply for the goods contained in literal a) of the appendix to this section, as of the second year of validity of the treaty, at the request of the interested party, a special agricultural safeguard (SAE) when all of the following three conditions are met:
a) the volume of imports of a good from Mexico has a weighted average participation greater than 30% of the total imports of Honduras of that good in the last three calendar years;
b) Honduras imports from Mexico of the good in question have exceeded 10% of their average annual growth rate of the last three calendar years; Y
c) the average annual growth rate of the last three calendar years of imports of Honduras from Mexico in said good is greater than 5%.
2. Mexico may apply for the goods contained in literal b) of the appendix to this section, from the second year of validity of the treaty, at the request of the interested party, an SAE when all of the following three conditions are met:
a) the volume of imports of a good from Honduras has a weighted average participation greater than 3% of the total imports of that good from Mexico in the last three calendar years;
b) the imports that Mexico makes from all over the world of the good in question have exceeded 10% of its average annual growth rate of the last three calendar years; Y
c) the average annual growth rate of the last three calendar years of the imports that Mexico makes from all over the world of the good in question is greater than 5%.
3. The application of the SAE will consist of an increase in the tariff resulting from applying the Tariff Elimination Program, at the lower tariff between the MFN in force at the time of importation or the base rate indicated for said good in the Tariff Elimination Program.
4. The application of the SAE measure will not be subject to any compensation.
5. The duration of the SAE will be up to 12 months, extendable for up to 12 more months. The importing Party shall notify the other Party of its intention to extend said measure at least 30 days prior to its expiration.
6. Once an SAE measure has been applied, the importing Party may apply it again until a period equal to the duration of the measure has elapsed in accordance with paragraph 5. This new measure may not last longer than 12 months.
7. Once the mechanism described in paragraphs 5 and 6 has been applied, neither Party may apply it again. Consequently, no Party may apply a SAE to a good in the appendix to this section for more than 24 months if the first time this mechanism was activated there was no extension pursuant to paragraph 5 or for more than 36 months if the SAE was applied. again according to paragraph 6.
8. A Party may apply an SAE during the reduction period established in the Tariff Reduction Program for each good, and up to three years after the respective reduction has ended.
9. Notwithstanding what is established in paragraphs 7 and 8, a Party may adopt and apply an SAE for the goods included in the appendix to this section, with the consent of the other.
10. A Party may not simultaneously adopt and apply an SAE and a bilateral safeguard, in accordance with Chapter VIII, with respect to the same good.
11. The SAE adopted by the importing Party will take effect from the day the measure is published in the dissemination body provided for in the legislation of the importing Party, incorporating the pertinent information that justifies its implementation.
12. Notwithstanding the application of the SAE, the Parties may hold consultations to exchange information and to try to reach mutually beneficial agreements.
13. Goods excluded from the Tariff Reduction Program will have the right to use this mechanism when they are incorporated into it. The terms for the application of the SAE to these assets will be reviewed on a case-by-case basis.
Annex 4-10 Committee on Agricultural Trade
Pursuant to Article 4-10, the Committee on Agricultural Trade will be made up of:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;
b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;
c) in the case of Honduras: the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or its successor; Y
d) in the case of Mexico: the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development and the Ministry of Agriculture, Livestock and Rural Development, or their successors.
Annex 4-11 Sugar trade between Guatemala and Mexico
1. The Parties agree to establish a Sugar Analysis Committee made up of representatives of each of them.
2. The Committee will review, on a case-by-case basis, to determine the preferential conditions of trade in sugar, when a Party requests preferential access to the good in a particular year. In the event that a Party has been an exporter of sugar in a particular year, in the following year there will be no concession of preferential access for the other Party.
3. For the goods specified in paragraphs 4 and 5, the Parties maintain their rights and obligations under the WTO Agreement with respect to tariff and non-tariff measures, except as otherwise agreed by the Committee.
4. For the purposes of this annex, sugar will be understood, for imports to Mexico, as the following subheadings or tariff fractions described in the Mexican General Import Tax Tariff: 1701.11.01, 1701.11.99, 1701.12.01, 1701.12. 99, 1701.91, 1701.99.01 (except those containing flavorings), and 1701.99.99.
5. For the purposes of this annex, sugar shall be understood, for imports to Guatemala, as the following subheadings or tariff fractions described in the SAC: 1701.11.00, 1701.12.00, 1701.91.00, and 1701.99.00 (except those containing flavorings).
Chapter V SANITARY AND PHYTOSANITARY MEASURES
Article 5-01 Definitions.
1. For the purposes of this chapter, the Parties shall apply as a reference the definitions and terms established:
a) in the Agreement on the Application of Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures, which is part of the Agreement on the WTO (Agreement on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures);
b) by the International Office of Epizootics (OIE);
c) in the International Plant Protection Convention; Y
d) by the Codex Alimentarius Commission.
2. Additionally, for the purposes of this chapter, the Parties will understand by:
food additive : any substance that by itself is not normally consumed as food, nor is it used as a basic ingredient in food, whether or not it has nutritional value, and whose addition to food in its production, manufacturing, processing, preparation, treatment phase , packaging, packaging, transport or storage, results (or can reasonably be expected to result) directly or indirectly by itself or its by-products, a component of the food or affects its characteristics. This definition does not include "contaminants" or substances added to food to maintain or improve nutritional qualities;
food : any processed, semi-processed or raw substance intended for human consumption, including beverages, chewing gum and any other substances used in the manufacture, preparation or treatment of food, but does not include cosmetics, tobacco, nor substances used solely as medicines;  pollutant: any substance or living organism not intentionally added to food, which is present in said food as a result of production (including operations carried out in agriculture, animal husbandry and veterinary medicine), manufacturing, processing, preparation, treatment, packaging, packaging, transportation or storage of said food or as a result of environmental contamination. This term includes physical contaminants;  food safety : quality that ensures that food does not present any risk to human health;  approval procedure: any registration, certification, notification or any other mandatory administrative procedure to approve the use of an additive or establish a tolerance of a contaminant for defined purposes or under agreed conditions in a food, drink or feed, prior to allowing its use or commercialization when any of these contains the additive or contaminant;  control or inspection procedure: any procedure used, directly or indirectly, to determine whether a sanitary or phytosanitary measure is being met, including sampling, testing, inspection, verification, monitoring, auditing, accreditation, or other procedures that involve the physical examination of a good, the packaging of the good, or equipment or facilities directly related to the production, marketing or use of a good, but does not mean an approval procedure;  pesticide: any substance intended to prevent, destroy, attract, repel or control any pest, including unwanted species of plants or animals, during the production, storage, transport, distribution and processing of food, agricultural products or animal feed, or that may administered to animals to combat ectoparasites. The term includes substances intended for use as plant growth regulators, defoliants, desiccants, agents to reduce fruit density or sprout inhibitors and substances applied to crops before or after harvest to protect the product against deterioration during storage and transport. The term does not normally include fertilizers, nutrients of vegetable or animal origin, feed additives or drugs for animals; Y  pesticide residue : any specified substance present in food, agricultural products, or animal feed as a consequence of the use of a pesticide. The term includes any derivative of a pesticide, such as conversion products, metabolites and reaction products, and impurities considered to be of toxicological importance.
Article 5-02 Scope of application.
1. This Chapter is applicable to all sanitary and phytosanitary measures that may directly or indirectly affect trade in goods between the Parties.
2. The framework of rules and disciplines that regulate the adoption and compliance with said measures will be compatible with the Agreement on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures.
3. The Parties shall consider as competent authorities those that have the legal responsibility to guarantee compliance with the sanitary and phytosanitary requirements contemplated in this chapter.
Article 5-03 Rights and obligations.
1. Each Party may establish, adopt, maintain or apply any sanitary or phytosanitary measure that regulates the protection of life, human or animal health and plant health, including food safety and the importation of any good from the territory of the Parties, when they do not comply with the applicable requirements, or do not satisfy the approval procedures defined in these measures.
2. Each Party may establish, adopt, maintain or apply sanitary and phytosanitary measures that represent a higher level of protection than that which would be achieved by means of those based on an international standard, guideline or recommendation, provided that there is scientific justification to justify it.
3. Each Party shall ensure that its sanitary or phytosanitary measures:
a) are based on scientific principles, taking into account, where appropriate, both relevant factors and different geographical and technological conditions;
b) are maintained only when there is a scientific basis to support them; Y
c) are based on a risk assessment appropriate to the circumstances.
4. Each Party shall ensure that its sanitary or phytosanitary measures do not arbitrarily or unjustifiably discriminate between its goods and similar goods of another Party, or between the goods of the latter and similar goods of any other non-Party, when sanitary conditions exist. or similar or identical phytosanitary.
5. The sanitary or phytosanitary measures of each Party shall not constitute a disguised restriction on trade, nor shall they have the object or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade between the Parties. In this sense, they will ensure that their measures are put into practice only to the degree necessary to achieve their adequate level of protection, taking into account technical, economic and scientific feasibility.  6. Each Party shall have the right to set its appropriate levels to protect life, human or animal health, and plant health, in accordance with the provisions of Article 5-06.
7. Each Party shall ensure that any non-governmental body that it relies on for the development or application of a sanitary or phytosanitary measure acts in a manner consistent with this Chapter.
8. In order to expeditiously apply sanitary and phytosanitary measures in the territory of the Parties and thus facilitate trade flows, the general procedures for the adoption and application of said measures shall be governed by the provisions of Annex 5. -03.
Article 5-04 International standards and harmonization.
1. Each Party shall use, as a frame of reference, the international standards, guidelines or recommendations, for the establishment of its sanitary and phytosanitary measures, except when these do not constitute an effective or adequate means to protect life, human or animal health and plant health, due to factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure nature, or for scientifically justified reasons or because the level of protection considered appropriate is not obtained.
2. The sanitary or phytosanitary measure of a Party that conforms to an international standard, guideline or recommendation shall be presumed compatible with paragraphs 1 to 5 of Article 5-03.
3. When a Party has reason to believe that a sanitary or phytosanitary measure of another Party affects or may adversely affect its exports, and the measure is not based on relevant international standards, guidelines or recommendations, it may request that Party to inform it by written and within a period not exceeding 30 days, on the reasons for the measure.
4. In order to promote the development and periodic review of international standards, guidelines and recommendations, as well as to achieve a greater degree of harmonization, each Party shall participate, according to its possibilities, in the competent international standardization organizations, in particular the Codex Alimentarius Commission, the International Office of Epizootics and the International Convention for the Protection of Plants.
5. The Parties shall develop criteria and procedures for the harmonization of methods for sampling, diagnosis, inspection and certification of animals, plants, their products and by-products, as well as matters relating to food safety.
Article 5-05 Equivalence.
1. Without reducing the level of protection of life, human or animal health and plant health established in their legislation and in order to facilitate trade, the Parties shall recognize the equivalence of their respective sanitary or phytosanitary measures, without prejudice to the rights conferred on them by this chapter and taking into account the guidelines and recommendations of the competent international standardization organizations.
2. The importing Party will accept a sanitary or phytosanitary measure established, applied or maintained by the exporting Party as equivalent, even when it differs from its own, provided that it objectively demonstrates with scientific information and with risk assessment methods based on agreed international standards. by them, that the measure achieves the appropriate level of protection required by the importing Party.
3. For the purposes of establishing the equivalence between the measures, access for inspections, tests and other applicable procedures will be provided to the importing Party that requests it.
4. Each Party will accept the results of the sanitary and phytosanitary control procedures that are carried out in the territory of another Party, as long as they satisfactorily guarantee that the good complies with the sanitary or phytosanitary measures that are established or maintained in the territory of that part.
5. Upon request, a Party shall consult with another Party, aimed at the recognition of the equivalence of specific sanitary or phytosanitary measures.
6. When developing a sanitary or phytosanitary measure, each Party shall consider the sanitary or phytosanitary measures, in force in or proposed by the other Parties.
Article 5-06 Risk assessment and adequate level of sanitary and phytosanitary protection.
1. Each Party shall ensure that its sanitary and phytosanitary measures are based on an assessment, appropriate to the circumstances, of the existing risks to life, human or animal health, and plant health, taking into account risk assessment techniques. prepared by the competent standardization organizations agreed by the Parties.
2. When carrying out a risk assessment on a good, including food additives and physical, chemical and biological contaminants, each Party shall take into account the following factors:
a) available scientific and technical information;
b) the existence of pests and diseases that must be taken into account, including the existence of areas free or of low prevalence of pests and diseases recognized by the Parties;
c) the epidemiology of risky diseases and pests;
d) the critical control points in the production, handling, packaging, packing and transportation processes;
e) ecological conditions and other environmental conditions to be considered;
f) relevant methods of inspection, sampling and testing; Y
g) the quarantine measures and applicable treatments that satisfy the importing country in terms of risk mitigation.
3. In addition to paragraph 2, when establishing the appropriate level of protection, each Party shall take into account the risk associated with the introduction, establishment and spread of a pest or disease; and when evaluating the risk, it will also take into account, when appropriate, the following economic factors:
a) the loss of production or sales in the event of the entry, establishment or spread of a pest or disease;
b) the costs of control or eradication of the pest or disease in its territory; Y
c) the cost-effectiveness of other possible methods to limit the risk.
4. In establishing its appropriate level of protection, each Party shall take into account the objective of minimizing negative effects on trade, and in order to achieve consistency in such levels of protection, shall avoid making arbitrary or unjustifiable distinctions that may cause discrimination or constitute a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties.
5. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3 and subparagraph c) of paragraph 3 of Article 5-03, when a Party carries out a risk assessment and concludes that the scientific knowledge or other available information is insufficient to complete the evaluation, it may provisionally adopt a sanitary or phytosanitary measure, basing it on the available information.
6. Once the exporting Party has submitted sufficient information to the importing Party to complete the risk assessment, both Parties shall agree on a time frame for the risk assessment to be completed and, where appropriate, immediately modify the provisional sanitary or phytosanitary measure.
7. When a Party is able to achieve its appropriate level of protection, through the gradual application of a sanitary or phytosanitary measure, it may, at the request of another Party and, in accordance with this Chapter, allow such gradual application or grant specific exceptions for the extent, during established periods, taking into account the export interests of the requesting Party.
Article 5-07 Recognition of areas free of pests or diseases and areas of low prevalence of pests or diseases.
1. Each Party shall ensure that its sanitary or phytosanitary measures are adapted to the sanitary or phytosanitary characteristics of the areas of origin and destination of the good, whether it is the entire territory of a Party, part of the territory of a Party, or of all or parts of the territories of several Parties.
2. When evaluating the sanitary or phytosanitary characteristics of an area, the Parties shall take into account, among others, the level of prevalence of specific diseases or pests, the existence of eradication or control programs, and the criteria or guidelines developed by the competent international organizations agreed by the Parties.
3. The Parties will recognize the concepts of free zones and zones of low prevalence of pests or diseases. The determination of such zones will be based on factors such as geographic location, ecosystems, epidemiological surveillance and the effectiveness of sanitary or phytosanitary controls.
4. The Party that declares an area of its territory free of a certain pest or disease must demonstrate said condition to another Party with scientific information and grant the assurance that it will remain as such, based on the protection measures adopted by the Parties. authorities responsible for sanitary and phytosanitary services.
5. The Party interested in obtaining recognition of a zone free of any pest or disease must make the request and provide the corresponding scientific and technical information to another Party.
6. The Party that receives the request for recognition indicated in paragraph 5, will pronounce itself within a term agreed with the requesting Party, being able to carry out verifications in the territory of the latter for inspection, tests and other procedures. In case of non-acceptance, it will indicate in writing the technical basis of its decision.
7. The Parties will establish agreements on specific requirements whose fulfillment allows a good produced in an area of low prevalence of pests or diseases to be imported if it achieves the required level of protection.  Article 5-08 Control, inspection and approval procedures.
1. The Parties, in accordance with this chapter, shall apply the provisions contained in Annex C of the Agreement on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures, with regard to control, inspection and approval procedures, including the approval systems of the use of additives or establishment of tolerances for contaminants in food products, beverages or feed.
2. When the importing Party requires carrying out a control or inspection procedure at the production stage, the exporting Party shall adopt, at the request of the importing Party, the measures that facilitate access to its territory and provide it with the necessary assistance to the execution of the control or inspection procedure.
3. To ensure the safety of food, beverages and feed, each Party may establish, in its approval procedures and in accordance with its current legislation, authorization requirements for the use of a food additive, or the establishment of a level of tolerance for a contaminant in them, before granting access to their market. When that Party so requires, it may adopt a relevant international standard, guideline or recommendation, as a basis for granting access to these goods, until a final determination is made.
Article 5-09 Transparency.
Each Party, when proposing the adoption or modification of a sanitary or phytosanitary measure applicable in its territory, shall notify through its competent authorities:
a) the adoptions and modifications of said measures and will provide the information on them, in accordance with the provisions of Annex B of the Agreement on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures and will make the pertinent adaptations;
b) additionally, it will notify:
i) changes or modifications to sanitary or phytosanitary measures that have a significant effect on trade between the Parties, at least 60 days before the entry into force of the new provision, to allow observations by either Party or persons interested. Emergency situations will be exempt from the term indicated above, in accordance with the provisions of Annex B of the Agreement on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures;
ii) changes that occur in the field of animal health, such as the appearance of exotic diseases and those on list A of the International Office of Epizootics, within 24 hours after the diagnostic detection of the problem;
iii) changes that occur in the phytosanitary field, such as the appearance of quarantine pests or spread of pests under official control, within 72 hours after their verification;
iv) findings of epidemiological importance and significant changes in relation to diseases and pests not included in subparagraphs ii) and iii) that may affect trade between the Parties, within a maximum period of 10 days; v) disease outbreaks in which the consumption of imported natural or processed foods is scientifically proven to be the cause; and vi) the causes or reasons why a good of the exporting Party is rejected, within a period of seven days;
c) The Parties shall use the notification and information centers established before the WTO Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures as a communication channel; Y
d) each Party will ensure that there is an information center, capable of responding to the reasonable requests of any Party, and will provide the relevant documentation, in accordance with the principles established in point 3 of Annex B of the Agreement on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures.
Article 5-10 Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures.
