Within 120 days from the date on which the 30-day period referred to in paragraph 21 ends or from the date on which the document referred to in paragraph 22 is notified, the competent authority shall issue a written resolution to the exporter or producer, whose good or goods have been subject to verification, in which it is determined whether or not the good qualifies as originating, which will include the conclusions of fact and the legal basis of the determination, a copy of which will be forwarded to the importer. For the issuance of said resolution, the authority must take into consideration the documents or records provided by the exporter or producer within the period of 30 days referred to in paragraph 21.
24. Each Party shall provide that when its competent authority determines that a certain good imported into its territory does not qualify as originating in accordance with the tariff classification or the value applied by that Party to one or more materials used in the production of the good, and This differs from the tariff classification or the value applied to the materials by the Party from whose territory the good has been exported, the decision of that Party will take effect until it notifies the importer of the good and the person who has completed and signed it in writing. the certificate of origin that protects it.
25. The resolution referred to in paragraph 24 will not be applicable to imports made prior to the date on which said resolution takes effect, when:
a) the competent authority of the importing Party has issued an advance judgment pursuant to Article 7-10, or the competent authority of either Party has issued any other ruling on the tariff classification or value of materials on which it is entitled to rely a person; Y
b) the anticipated criterion or resolution mentioned in literal a), is prior to the beginning of the verification of origin.
26. When the verification carried out by a Party establishes that the exporter or producer has falsely or unfoundedly certified or declared more than once that a good qualifies as originating, the importing Party shall suspend preferential tariff treatment to identical goods that that person exports or produces, until the same proves that it complies with the provisions of Chapter VI.
Article 7-8 Confidentiality.
1. Each Party shall maintain, in accordance with the provisions of its legislation, the confidentiality of the information obtained pursuant to this chapter and shall protect it from any disclosure that could harm the person who provides it.
2. The confidential information obtained in accordance with this chapter may only be made known to the authorities responsible for the administration and application of the determination of origin resolutions and customs and tax matters.
Article 7-9 Penalties.
Each Party shall establish or maintain criminal, civil or administrative sanctions for violations of its laws and regulations related to the provisions of this chapter.
Article 7-10 Advance Criteria.
1. Each Party shall provide that, through its competent authority, prior written criteria be granted expeditiously, prior to the importation of a good into its territory. The anticipated criteria will be issued by the competent authority of the territory of the importing Party, at the request of its importer or of the exporter or producer in the territory of another Party, based on the facts and circumstances stated by them, regarding the origin of the goods. .
2. The anticipated criteria do not constitute necessary and indispensable requirements for the importation of goods under preferential tariff treatment.
3. The anticipated criteria will deal with:
a) if the good qualifies as originating, in accordance with Chapter VI;
b) if the non-originating materials used in the production of a good comply with the corresponding change in tariff classification indicated in Annex 6-03;
c) if the good meets the regional content value requirement established in Chapter VI;
d) if the method applied by the exporter or producer in the territory of another Party, in accordance with the principles of the Customs Valuation Code, to calculate the transaction value of the good or of the materials used in the production of a good with respect to the which advance judgment is requested is adequate, to determine if the good meets the regional content value requirement in accordance with Chapter VI;
e) if the country of origin marking carried out or proposed for a good satisfies the provisions of article 3-15; Y
f) other matters that the Parties agree.
4. Each Party shall adopt or maintain procedures for the issuance of advance criteria upon official publication, including at least:
a) the information that is reasonably required to process the request;
b) the power of its competent authority to request, at any time, additional information from the person requesting the advance judgment during the application evaluation process;
c) a period of 120 days for its competent authority to issue the advance judgment, once it has obtained all the necessary information from the person requesting it; Y
d) the obligation to fully explain, founded and motivated, the reasons for the anticipated judgment when it is unfavorable for the applicant.
5. Each Party shall apply the advance criteria to imports into its territory, from the date of issuance of the criterion, or from a later date indicated therein, unless the advance criterion is modified or revoked in accordance with the provisions in paragraph 7.
6. Each Party shall grant to any person who requests an advance judgment, the same treatment, the same interpretation and application of the provisions of Chapter VI regarding the determination of origin, that it has granted to any other person to whom it has issued a judgment. anticipated, when the facts and circumstances are identical in all material respects.
7. The anticipated judgment may be modified or revoked by the competent authority in the following cases:
a) when the advance judgment was based on an error:
i) in fact;
ii) in the tariff classification of the good or materials subject to the criterion; either
iii) in the application of the regional content value requirement, in accordance with Chapter VI;
b) when it is not in accordance with an interpretation agreed between the Parties or a modification with respect to Article 3-15 or Chapter VI;
c) when the circumstances or facts that support it change; either
d) in order to comply with an administrative or judicial decision.
8. Each Party shall provide that any modification or revocation of an advance ruling takes effect on the date it is issued or on a later date established therein, and may not be applied to imports of a good made before those dates, unless unless the person to whom it has been issued has not acted in accordance with its terms and conditions.
9. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 8, the Party that issues the advance judgment shall postpone the effective date of the modification or revocation for a period of not less than 45 days, when the person to whom the advance judgment has been issued advance judgment has relied on that judgment in good faith.
10. Each Party shall provide that, when considering the regional value content of a good for which an advance judgment has been issued, its competent authority shall assess whether:
a) the exporter or producer complies with the terms and conditions of the advance judgment;
b) the exporter's or producer's operations are consistent with the circumstances and substantial facts that support that criterion; Y
c) the supporting data and calculations used in applying the criterion or method for calculating value or allocating cost are correct in all material respects.
11. Each Party shall provide that, when its competent authority determines that any of the requirements set forth in paragraph 10 has not been met, the competent authority may modify or revoke the advance judgment, as the circumstances warrant.
12. Each Party shall provide that, when its competent authority decides that the advance judgment has been based on incorrect information, the person to whom it was issued shall not be penalized, if he demonstrates that he acted with reasonable care and in good faith in stating the facts and circumstances that gave rise to the advance judgment.
13. Each Party shall provide that, when an advance judgment is issued to a person who has falsely stated or omitted material circumstances or facts on which the advance judgment is based, or has not acted in accordance with the terms and conditions thereof, the authority authority that issues the advance judgment can apply the measures established in the legislation of each Party.
14. Each Party shall provide that the holder of an advance judgment may not use it if there is a substantial change in the facts and circumstances on which the competent authority relied to issue it.
Article 7-11 Review and challenge.
1. Each Party shall grant rights to review and challenge resolutions for determination of origin and anticipated criteria provided for in its legislation for its importers, exporters or producers of another Party that:
a) fill out and sign a certificate or declaration of origin that covers a good that has been the subject of a determination of origin resolution, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 21 of article 7-07; either
b) have received early judgment in accordance with the provisions of article 7-10.
2. The rights referred to in paragraph 1 include:
a) access to at least one instance of administrative review, independent of the official or agency responsible for the resolution or advance judgment subject to review, in accordance with the legislation of each Party; Y
b) access to an instance of judicial review of the resolution or decision made in the last instance of administrative review, in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
Article 7-12 Committee of Origin
1. The Parties establish the Committee of Origin, made up of representatives of each of them. The term for its installation will be within 30 days from the entry into force of this treaty.
2. The Origin Committee will meet in ordinary session twice a year and in extraordinary session as many times as necessary at the request of any Party.
3. The functions of the Committee of Origin are:
a) prepare, no later than 90 days after the entry into force of the treaty, the corresponding regulation;
b) ensure the effective application and administration of chapters VI and VII;
c) address issues regarding the interpretation, application and administration of chapters VI and VII;
d) try to reach agreements on:
i) tariff classification and customs value matters related to origin determination resolutions;
ii) the modifications to the certificate or declaration of origin referred to in article 7-02; Y
iii) the notification made by the countries on changes in their nomenclature or internal provisions on rules of origin and customs procedures for handling the origin of merchandise that affect this treaty; Y
e) attend to any other matter agreed upon by the Parties.
4. Any Party that considers that chapters VI and VII need to be modified, due to changes in the development of production processes, cases in which a waiver is granted in accordance with article 6-23 or other matters, may submit to the Committee of Origin a modification proposal for your consideration and the reasons and studies that support it.
The Committee of Origin will submit a report to the Commission within a period of no more than 90 days, counted from the receipt of the proposal.
Annex 7-01 Competent Authorities
For the purposes of article 7-01, the competent authority will be:
a) in the case of El Salvador, the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;
b) in the case of Guatemala, the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;
c) in the case of Honduras, the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or its successor; Y
d) in the case of Mexico, the Ministry of Finance and Public Credit, or its successor.
Chapter VIII SAFEGUARD MEASURES
Article 8-01 Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
threat of serious harm : the clear imminence of serious harm, determined pursuant to paragraph 8 of Article 8-05, based on the facts and not merely on pleading, conjecture or remote possibility;
competent authority means the "competent authority" in accordance with Annex 8-01; directly competitive good: one that, not being similar to the one being compared, is essentially equivalent for commercial purposes because it is dedicated to the same use and is interchangeable with it;
originating good means an "originating good" of a Party, as set out in Chapter VI;  similar good : the good that, although it is not exactly the same as the good with which it is compared, has similar characteristics and composition, which allows it to fulfill the same functions and be commercially interchangeable with it;  Serious Injury: a general and significant impairment of a domestic industry, determined pursuant to paragraph 8 of Article 8-05; and  domestic industry: the group of producers of similar or directly competitive goods that operate within the territory of a Party or those whose joint production of similar or directly competitive goods constitutes a significant proportion of the total national production of those goods.
Article 8-02 General Provisions.
1. Except as provided in this chapter, the Parties shall be governed in accordance with their legislation and the provisions of Article XIX of the GATT 1994 and the Agreement on Safeguards, which is part of the WTO Agreement.
2. Each Party may apply to imports of goods originating in the territory of another Party carried out under the Tariff Elimination Program, safeguard measures, based on clear, strict criteria and with a defined temporality. Each Party may adopt bilateral or global safeguard measures.
Article 8-03 Bilateral safeguard measures.
1. Each Party may adopt and apply bilateral safeguard measures if, as a result of the reduction or elimination of a customs duty stipulated in this Agreement, the volume of imports of one or more goods benefiting from the Tariff Elimination Program increases by one pace and under such conditions as to cause serious injury or threat of serious injury to the domestic industry as follows:
a) each Party may maintain bilateral safeguard measures during and up to three years after the end of the Tariff Elimination Program. After this period, said Party may adopt and apply a bilateral safeguard measure against the same good, only with the consent of the affected Party;
b) bilateral safeguard measures may only be adopted when strictly necessary to counteract serious injury or threat of serious injury caused by imports of goods originating in the territory of another Party;
c) The bilateral safeguard measures will be of a tariff type and may consist of the suspension of future tax relief on the good in question. Likewise, they may consist of an increase in the customs duty applicable to the good to a level that does not exceed the lower of the current most favored nation customs duty applicable to that good on the day the bilateral safeguard measure is adopted, and the tariff most favored nation customs applicable on that good the day before the entry into force of this treaty;
d) The Parties may apply bilateral safeguard measures for a period of up to four years, extendable for a period of one year. The established deadlines will be determined at the stage of prior consultations, by mutual agreement, according to the needs of the affected national industry;
e) The Parties may adopt a bilateral safeguard only once for the same asset when the measure has lasted more than two years and has been extended;
f) The Parties may adopt a bilateral safeguard for the same good once more when the measure has lasted for more than two years, has not been extended, a period equal to that of the measure previously imposed has elapsed, and has the consent of the Party against whose property the measure will be applied;
g) The Parties may adopt a bilateral safeguard for the second time for the same asset when the measure has lasted up to two years and has been extended by one year provided that a period equal to the previously imposed measure has elapsed; Y
h) Upon concluding the application of the bilateral measure, the tariff rate that will apply to the good in question will be the one that corresponds to that date according to the Tariff Elimination Program.
2. The Party that decides to initiate a procedure that could result in the adoption of a bilateral safeguard measure, must notify the exporting Party in writing and, at the same time, request prior consultations in accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 4 to 7 of article 8-05.
3. Unless the Parties involved agree otherwise, the Party that intends to adopt a bilateral safeguard measure shall grant the Party affected by that measure, mutually agreed compensation, in accordance with the following:
a) the compensation will consist of additional tariff concessions, whose effects on the trade of the exporting Party are equivalent to the impact of the bilateral safeguard measure;
b) the compensation will be determined in the consultation stage referred to in paragraph 11 of article 8-05;
c) if the Parties do not reach an agreement regarding compensation, the Party that intends to adopt the bilateral safeguard measure shall be empowered to do so and the Party affected by it may impose tariff measures that have trade effects equivalent to those of the measure bilateral safeguard adopted; Y
d) The compensation referred to in this article may only be made with goods included in the Tariff Elimination Program.
4. In the case of a bilateral safeguard measure for perishable or seasonal agricultural goods, the investigation periods established for the adoption of the measure will be reduced by half unless the Parties by mutual agreement decide to reduce them further.
Article 8-04 Global Safeguard Measures.
1. The Parties retain their rights and obligations to apply global safeguard measures under Article XIX of the GATT 1994 and the Agreement on Safeguards, which is part of the WTO Agreement, except those referring to compensation or retaliation and exclusion of a measure global safeguard insofar as they are incompatible with the provisions of this article.
2. When a Party decides to adopt a global safeguard measure in accordance with paragraph 1, it may only apply it to another Party when it determines that imports of goods originating in that Party, considered individually, represent a substantial part of total imports and contribute materially to serious injury or threat of serious injury to the importing Party.
3. For this determination, the following criteria will be taken into account, among others:
a) imports of goods originating in another Party shall not be considered to be substantial if they are not included in the imports of the main supplying countries of the good subject to the procedure, whose exports together represent 80% of the total imports of that good in the importing Party;
b) normally it will not be considered that imports of goods originating in a Party contribute significantly to serious injury or threat of serious injury, if their growth rate during the period in which the detrimental increase occurred is substantially lower than the growth rate of total imports from all sources, during the same period; Y
c) In order to determine the significant contribution to the serious injury or threat of serious injury, changes in the Party's participation in total imports and their volume will be taken into account.
4. The Party that applies the global safeguard measure, and has initially excluded from it a good of another Party, shall have the right to include it, when the competent authority determines that a sudden increase in imports of such good reduces the effectiveness of the global safeguard measure.
5. In no case may the importing Party apply the global safeguard measures provided for in paragraph 2, without prior written notification to the other Party and without having carried out consultations. For this purpose, all procedural requirements set forth in this chapter shall be complied with.
6. The Party that intends to adopt a global safeguard measure shall grant the Party affected by that measure mutually agreed compensation, in the form of concessions that have trade effects equivalent to the impact of the global safeguard measure.
7. Unless otherwise agreed, the compensation referred to in paragraph 6 will be determined in the consultation stage referred to in paragraph 5.
8. If the Parties fail to agree on compensation, the Party proposing to take the global safeguard measure shall be empowered to do so and the affected Party may impose measures that have trade effects equivalent to those of the global safeguard measure. adopted.
9. A Party shall not apply a global safeguard measure against a good originating in another Party when imports from that Party do not exceed 3% of total imports of that good, provided that developing country members of the WTO with a share in imports less than 3% do not represent together more than 9% of total imports of the good in question.
Article 8-05 Procedure.
1. Each Party shall establish clear and strict procedures for the adoption and application of safeguard measures, in accordance with the provisions of this Chapter.
2. The application submitted to the competent authority must be supported by 25% of the national industry.
3. Within a period of 30 days, counted from the presentation of the application, the competent authority may reject it, or initiate the investigation if it has determined that it is supported by producers that represent at least 25% of the total production of like or directly competitive goods.
4. The Party that decides to initiate a procedure to adopt safeguard measures will publish the initiation thereof in the dissemination bodies provided for in its legislation. The day following the publication, it shall notify the exporting Party in writing and request, at the same time, prior consultations.
5. The notification referred to in the previous paragraph will be made through the competent authority by certified mail, specialized courier, telefax or any other means that ensures its reception. This will contain sufficient information to support the application of the safeguard measures, including:
a) the names and available addresses of domestic producers of similar or directly competitive goods representative of the domestic industry, their participation in the domestic industry of that good and the reasons that lead them to affirm that they are representative of that sector ;
b) a clear and complete description of the good subject to the procedure, the tariff position at a six-digit level, at least, and the current tariff treatment, as well as the description of the similar or directly competitive good;
c) the data on imports corresponding to each one of the three most recent years that constitute the basis that this good is imported in increasing quantities, either in absolute terms or relative to national production;
d) the data on the total national production of the similar or directly competitive good corresponding to the last three years;
e) the data that demonstrate serious injury or threat of serious injury caused by imports to the sector in question in accordance with the data referred to in subparagraphs c) and d);
f) a list and description of the presumed causes of serious damage, or threat of serious damage based on the information required in accordance with subparagraphs a) to e) and a summary of the grounds for alleging that the increase in imports of that either in absolute terms or relative to national production is the cause of it;
g) the criteria and objective information that demonstrates that the assumptions established in this chapter are met for the application of a safeguard measure to the other Party, when applicable; Y
h) Information on the tariff measures that are intended to be adopted and their duration.
6. The period for prior consultations will begin on the day after the exporting Party receives the notification requesting the initiation of prior consultations. This period will be 60 business days, unless the Parties agree on a shorter term.
7. During the prior consultation period, the exporting Party will make all the observations it deems pertinent, particularly on whether the proposed safeguard measures are appropriate.
8. For the purposes of determining serious damage or threat of serious damage, the competent authorities must have reliable information and will evaluate in detail, based on said information, all the factors of an objective and quantifiable nature that have any relationship with the branch of national production affected, in particular the pace and amount of the increase in imports of the good in question, in absolute and relative terms, the part of the domestic market absorbed by the increase in imports, significant changes in the level of sales , internal prices, production, productivity, use of installed capacity, market share, profits, losses and employment.
9. To determine whether the safeguard measures are appropriate, a direct causal relationship between the increase in imports of the good in question and the serious injury or threat of serious injury to the domestic industry will be demonstrated.
10. If there are factors other than increased imports from the other Party that simultaneously injure or threaten to injure a domestic industry, the serious injury or threat of serious injury caused by those factors may not be attributed to the mentioned imports.
11. If, as a result of this investigation, the competent authority determines, based on objective evidence, that the assumptions set forth in this chapter are met, the importing Party may initiate consultations with the other Party, to determine the compensation referred to in the Article 8-03, paragraph 3; and Article 8-04, paragraph 6.
12. The provisions of this article shall not prevent the Parties from meeting at any time to discuss compensation to the Party affected by the imposition of the safeguard measure.
13. The safeguard measures provided for in this chapter may only be adopted once the consultation period has concluded. The final resolution by means of which a safeguard measure is adopted and, where appropriate, the compensation measure, will be published in the corresponding official dissemination organs of the Party that adopts it, as appropriate, and will be notified to the other Party at day after publication.
14. The notification referred to in the preceding paragraph will be made through the competent authority by certified mail, specialized courier, telefax or any other means that ensures its receipt and will take effect the day after it is received by the Party. exporter. For this purpose, the exporting Party must acknowledge receipt of the notification, the day following its receipt.
15. The Parties are at no time obliged to reveal the information that has been provided confidentially, the disclosure of which contravenes their legal systems. Notwithstanding this, the importing Party that intends to adopt the safeguard measure shall provide the other Party with a non-confidential summary of the information that is confidential.
16. If the importing Party determines that the reasons that gave rise to the adoption of the safeguard measure still persist, it shall notify the competent authorities of the other Party of its intention to extend it, at least 60 business days prior to its expiration and it will provide the information that supports the decision, including the evidence that the causes that led to the adoption of the safeguard measure persist. The notification will be made in the terms provided in this chapter, and both the prior consultations on the extension and those related to the respective compensation must be carried out before the expiration of the safeguard measures initially adopted.
17. Each Party shall ensure that the final resolution adopting a safeguard measure is subject to review by administrative or judicial courts to the extent provided by its legislation. Negative resolutions on the existence of serious damage or threat of serious damage may not be modified except by this review procedure.
Annex 8-01 Competent Authority
For purposes of this chapter, the term "competent authority" shall mean:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Ministry of Economy or the one that is duly designated to act as competent authority;
b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy or the one that is duly designated to act as competent authority;
c) in the case of Honduras: the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce or the one that is duly designated to act as competent authority; Y
d) in the case of Mexico: the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development, or its successor.
Chapter IX UNFAIR INTERNATIONAL TRADE PRACTICES
Article 9-01 Definitions.
For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
WTO Agreements: the Agreement on the Implementation of Article VI of the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade of 1994 and the Agreement on Subsidies and Countervailing Measures, which are part of the WTO Agreement;
competent authority : the one indicated by each Party in Annex 9-01(1);
investigating authority : the one indicated by each Party in Annex 9-01(2);
price undertaking : a commitment by the exporter or exporting Party to revise its prices or to terminate dumped or subsidized exports that suspends or terminates an investigation, without imposing a countervailing duty; countervailing duties: "anti-dumping duties" or "countervailing duties", in accordance with the WTO Agreements; injury: material injury to a domestic industry, threat of material injury to a domestic industry, significant delay in the creation of a domestic industry, serious injury or threat of serious injury to an industry National Production;
investigation : an investigative procedure on unfair international trade practices carried out by the investigating authority; dissemination body: the one indicated by each Party in Annex 9-01(3);  interested party : as defined in the WTO Agreements, and includes the government of each Party whose assets are subject to the investigation;
unfair international trade practices: the importation of goods under dumped or subsidized conditions that cause damage to a domestic industry;
domestic industry : "domestic industry" as defined in the WTO Agreements; final resolution: a resolution of the competent authority that puts an end to an investigation and that decides if the imposition of definitive countervailing duties is appropriate;
initial resolution : a resolution of the competent authority formally declaring the initiation of the investigation; and preliminary resolution: a resolution of the competent authority that decides on the imposition of provisional countervailing duties.
Article 9-02 General principle.
The Parties reject any unfair international trade practice and recognize the need to eliminate domestic policies that cause trade distortions.  Article 9-03 Subsidies.
1. Except as provided in Article 4-08, neither Party shall grant subsidies for the export of goods to the territory of another Party.
2. Upon the entry into force of this Agreement, each Party shall eliminate all subsidies on the export of goods to the territory of another Party, except those permitted under the WTO Agreement.
3. When a Party maintains or grants subsidies after the entry into force of this Agreement and these cause damage to a domestic industry, the affected Party may initiate an investigation.
Article 9-04 Principles for the application of national legislation.
1. The investigation, establishment and application of countervailing duties will be based on national legislation in a manner compatible with the provisions of this chapter, the provisions and procedures established in Articles VI and XVI of the GATT 1994 and the Agreements of the WTO.
2. In the case of a regional proceeding, the Parties shall be governed by the provisions of Annex 9-04.
Article 9-05 Publication of resolutions.
1. The Parties will publish the initial, preliminary and final resolutions in their dissemination bodies.
2. The resolutions shall take legal effect from the day following their publication in the dissemination body of each Party.
Article 9-06 Withdrawal of the investigation.
1. The applicant may at any time withdraw from the investigation.
2. If a withdrawal request is submitted after the initiation of the investigation, the investigating authority will notify the interested parties, thereby concluding the investigation. Notwithstanding the foregoing, the investigating authority may only continue with the investigation if, within a period of 30 days from the notification, the national producers who expressly support its continuation represent at least 25% of the National Production.
Article 9-07 Notifications.
1. The Parties shall ensure that, during the investigation, the investigating authority notifies the competent authority of the exporting Party in writing the day after the corresponding resolution takes effect and the interested parties within three days after said resolution takes effect. , so that they present in their defense the arguments and evidence they consider pertinent.
2. With the notification referred to in paragraph 1, a copy of the respective publication of the dissemination body of the Party conducting the investigation shall be sent, as well as a copy of the public version of the request to initiate the investigation and its annexes. .
Article 9-08 Minimum content of resolutions.
The initial, preliminary or final resolutions will contain, when appropriate, at least the following:
a) name of the complainant;
b) description of the imported good subject to the investigation and its tariff classification;
c) the elements and evidence used to determine the possible existence or existence of an unfair international trade practice; Y
d) the legal reasoning, data, facts or circumstances on which the resolution in question is based and motivated, which appear in the respective file.
Article 9-09 Notification to the exporting government.
When the investigating authority considers that there is sufficient evidence to justify the initiation of an investigation regarding unfair international trade practices, it shall notify the competent authority of the other Party. Said notification must be made before the start of the investigation and will contain at least:
a) type of investigation;
b) name of the applicant;
c) description of the good under investigation and its tariff classification; Y
d) name of the exporters and importers of whom it is known.
Article 9-10 Conciliation hearing.
When an investigation is formally initiated and as long as a final resolution is not issued, without interrupting the process, ex officio or at the request of the interested party, conciliatory hearings may be promoted, in order to propose formulas for solving the case.
If the parties reach an agreement, it will be sanctioned by the competent authority in accordance with the legislation of each Party.
Article 9-11 Preliminary resolution.
1. In no case before 60 days have elapsed, counted from the date of publication of the initial resolution, the competent authority will issue a preliminary resolution in which it determines that:
a) it is appropriate to continue with the investigation and, where appropriate, the imposition of provisional countervailing duties and their amount; or  b) the investigation is terminated by virtue of the fact that a positive preliminary determination of the existence of an unfair international trade practice has not been reached, in which case it will have the character of a final resolution.
2. When the preliminary resolution determines the imposition of a provisional countervailing duty, in addition to the provisions of article 9-08, it will include the margin of dumping or subsidy and the elements taken for its determination, a description of the damage and the methodology followed to determine them.
Article 9-12 Guarantees.
Importers may guarantee the provisional measures by means of a bond or deposit in cash equal to the provisionally estimated amount of the countervailing duty.
Article 9-13 Clarifications.
1. Once a provisional or definitive compensatory quota has been established, any interested party may request the competent authority to decide whether or not a certain asset is subject to it or to clarify any aspect of the corresponding resolution.  2. The presentation of the request referred to in paragraph 1 will not interrupt the course of the investigation or suspend the application of the countervailing duty.
3. From the acceptance of the request referred to in paragraph 1, the interested party may guarantee the payment of the compensatory fee by means of a bond or cash deposit.
Article 9-14 Sending copies.
The investigating authority shall ensure that all known interested parties receive, in a timely manner, copies of each of the reports, documents, and evidence presented to it in the course of the investigation, except for confidential information. Such copies will be provided by the party submitting the information.
Article 9-15 Technical information meetings.
1. At the request of any of the interested parties, the investigating authority will hold technical information meetings to explain the methodology used, the technical reports, the spreadsheets and any other element on which the initial, preliminary or preliminary resolution has been based. definitive, except for confidential information.
2. The presentation of said request will be made within the five business days following the publication of the resolution. The meeting will take place within 10 business days from the date of submission of the application.
Article 9-16 Public hearing.
1. The investigating authority will hold, ex officio or at the request of the interested party, a public hearing that will have the objective of the interested parties presenting their position regarding the information and evidence presented before said authority, allowing it and the interested parties among themselves, request additional explanations or clarifications on a specific element of the investigation.
2. The holding of the public hearing will be notified at least 15 business days before it takes place.
3. No interested party will be obliged to attend the scheduled hearing and their absence will not be detrimental to their cause.
4. The investigating authority will give the interested parties the opportunity to present arguments within 10 business days following the public hearing.
The allegations will consist of the written presentation of conclusions regarding the information and arguments provided during the investigation.
Article 9-17 Access to confidential information.
1. The investigating authority will grant, only to the legal representatives of the interested parties, access to the confidential information provided by the other parties in the course of an investigation into unfair international trade practices, in accordance with this article.
2. For this purpose, the investigating authority will require that the interested party express their consent so that their information classified as confidential can be reviewed by the legal representatives of the other interested parties.
3. Only the legal representatives of the interested parties who meet the following requirements may have access to confidential information:
a) submit a written request and fill out the format provided for this purpose by the investigating authority, in which they state the reasons and motives for which they wish to have access and specifically indicate the information they intend to review;
b) that they have a good reputation and prove their independence from their client, for which the following will be impediments: being a partner, occupying a managerial or salaried position of the same or having been in the last year;
c) that prove with official documents that they are a lawyer authorized to practice said profession in the territory of the importing Party, or failing that, that they are assisted by one;
d) that they guarantee before the investigating authority, through any of the forms of surety existing in the legislation of each Party, the fulfillment of the confidentiality commitment. The amount of the security will be set in accordance with its legislation or, failing that, in accordance with what the investigating authority determines;
e) that they undertake to return the original versions and copies of the minutes or summaries that have been prepared for access to confidential information, within 10 days after the interested parties have been made aware of the resolution that puts an end to to the procedure; Y
f) be a resident in the territory of the importing Party.
4. The bond will be in force for the entire duration of the investigation and the appeals that are presented as a result of the resolution that put an end to the procedure.
5. Without prejudice to making the bond effective, the legal representative and officials of the investigating authority who violate the confidentiality commitment will be subject to the sanctions established by the legislation of each Party.
6. The authorization of access to confidential information is a personal and non-transferable right.
Article 9-18 Access to information contained in other files.
In accordance with the legislation of each Party, any person who has an interest will have access to the administrative files of any investigation related to unfair international trade practices in which a final resolution has been issued, except for confidential information.
Article 9-19 Rights and obligations of interested parties.
Each Party will ensure that the parties interested in the administrative investigation have the same rights and obligations that will be respected both during the procedure, and in the administrative and contentious or jurisdictional instances that are filed against the final resolutions.
Article 9-20 Amendments to national legislation.
When a Party decides to amend, add, repeal or abrogate its legislation on unfair international trade practices, it will notify the other Parties immediately after its publication in their respective dissemination body. Said reform, addition, repeal or abrogation will be compatible with the WTO Agreements.
Addendum 9-01(1) Competent Authority
For purposes of this chapter, the term "competent authority" shall mean:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Ministry of Economy or the one that is duly designated to act as competent authority;
b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy, or the one that is duly designated to act as competent authority;
c) in the case of Honduras: the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or the one that is duly designated to act as competent authority; Y
d) in the case of Mexico: the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development or its successor.
Exhibit 9-01(2) Investigating Authority
For the purposes of this chapter, the term "investigating authority" shall mean:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Directorate of Trade Policy of the Ministry of Economy or its successor;
b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy, or the one that is duly designated to act as investigative authority;
c) in the case of Honduras: the General Directorate for Economic Integration and Trade Policy of the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or its successor; Y
d) in the case of Mexico: the International Trade Practices Unit of the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development or its successor.
Annex 9-01(3) Dissemination Bodies
For the purposes of this chapter, "dissemination bodies" shall mean:
a) in the case of El Salvador: a newspaper with national circulation, without prejudice to its subsequent publication in the Official Gazette;
b) in the case of Guatemala: the Diario de Centroamérica;
c) in the case of Honduras: a newspaper with national circulation, without prejudice to its subsequent publication in the Official Gazette "La Gaceta"; Y
d) in the case of Mexico: Official Gazette of the Federation.
Annex 9-04 Regional Procedure
In the case of a regional procedure, Guatemala, El Salvador and Honduras will only adopt the recommendation of the Secretariat for Central American Economic Integration (SIECA) for the application of a compensatory quota, when it has observed during said procedure the provisions established in this treaty.
Chapter X CROSS- BORDER TRADE IN SERVICES
Article 10-01 Definitions.
1. For the purposes of this chapter, it shall be understood as:
cross-border trade in services: the supply of a service:
a) from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party;
b) in the territory of a Party to a consumer of services of another Party; Y
c) by a service provider of a Party through the presence of natural persons of a Party in the territory of another Party;
service consumer : any person who receives or uses a service;  enterprise of a Party : an enterprise constituted or organized in accordance with the applicable law of a Party and having its domicile in the territory of that Party and a branch located in the territory of a Party that carries on business activities therein;  federal or central, state or departmental governments : includes non-governmental organizations that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated by those governments;  measures that a Party adopts or maintains: those adopted or maintained by:
a) the federal, central, state or departmental and municipal governments, if applicable; Y
b) non-governmental organizations that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated to them by those governments;
natural person of another Party : national or resident of another Party;
legal person of another Party : the one constituted or organized under the laws of that other Party and that carries out or plans to carry out substantive commercial operations in the territory of that Party or of any other Party;
service provider : any person who provides a service;
service provider of a Party : a person of a Party who intends to provide or provides a service;
quantitative restrictions : a non-discriminatory measure that places limitations on:
a) the number of service providers, whether through a quota, monopoly or an economic necessity test, or by any other quantitative means; either
b) the operations of any service provider, whether through a quota, monopoly or an economic necessity test, or by any other quantitative means;
specialized air services : aerial mapping services, aerial surveying, aerial photography, forest fire control, firefighting, aerial advertising, glider towing, skydiving services, aerial construction services, air transportation of logs or logs , scenic flights, training flights, aerial inspection and surveillance, and aerial spraying; and  service supplied in the exercise of governmental powers : that supplied by a public institution, which is not supplied under commercial conditions or in competition with one or more service providers.
2. Any other definition not contained in paragraph 1 shall be taken from the definitions contained in the GATS.
Article 10-02 Scope of application and extension of obligations.
1. This Chapter applies to measures that a Party adopts or maintains on cross-border trade in services by service providers of another Party, including those relating to:
a) the production, distribution, marketing, sale and provision of a service;
b) the purchase, payment or use of a service;
c) access to, and use of:
i) distribution and transportation systems related to the provision of a service; either
ii) public telecommunications networks and services;
d) the presence in its territory of a service provider of another Party, including services provided by a company once it has been established in accordance with the agreed commitments; and  e) the granting of a bond or other form of financial guarantee, as a condition for the provision of a service.
2. This chapter does not apply to:
a) air services, including national and international air transport, with and without a fixed itinerary, as well as auxiliary activities in support of air services, except:
i) aircraft repair and maintenance services during the period in which an aircraft is withdrawn from service;
ii) specialized air services; Y
iii) computerized reservation systems;
b) financial services;
c) subsidies or grants provided by a Party or a State enterprise, including government-supported loans, guarantees and insurance; neither
d) government services or functions such as, and not limited to, law enforcement, rehabilitation services, income security or insurance, social security or insurance, social welfare, public education , public training, health and care for children.
3. Nothing in this chapter shall be construed to:
a) impose on a Party any obligation with respect to a national of another Party who intends to enter its labor market or who has permanent employment in its territory, nor confer any right on that national, with respect to such entry or employment; neither
b) impose any obligation or confer any right on a Party, with respect to government purchases made by a Party or a State enterprise.
4. With respect to non-governmental organizations, referred to in subparagraph b) of the definition of "measures that a Party adopts or maintains", that exercise regulatory, administrative or other powers of a governmental nature that have been delegated to them in accordance with national legislation, federal or central governments shall ensure that they take all reasonable measures within their power to ensure that such agencies comply with the provisions of this chapter.
5. The provisions of this chapter shall apply to the measures related to the services contemplated in the annexes, only to the extent and terms stipulated in those annexes.
Article 10-03 Most Favored Nation Treatment.
1. Each Party shall immediately and unconditionally grant to the services and service providers of another Party treatment no less favorable than that it grants to similar services and similar service providers of any other country.
2. The provisions of this Chapter shall not be construed in the sense of preventing a Party from conferring advantages to adjacent countries, in order to facilitate exchanges, limited to contiguous border areas, of services that are produced or consumed locally.
Article 10-04 National treatment.
1. Each Party shall grant to the services and service providers of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that granted to its similar services or similar service providers.
2. Each Party may comply with the provisions of paragraph 1 by granting to the services and service providers of another Party formally identical or formally different treatment to the one it grants to its similar services and similar service providers.
3. Formally identical or formally different treatment shall be deemed to be less favorable if it modifies the conditions of competition in favor of services or service providers of the Party as compared with similar services or service providers of the other Party.
4. Treatment accorded by a Party under paragraph 1 means, with respect to a state, treatment no less favorable than the most favorable treatment accorded by that state to like services and like service providers of the Party to which belong.
Article 10-05 Local presence.
No Party shall require a service provider of another Party to establish or maintain a representative office or other type of business, or to reside in its territory as a condition for the cross-border provision of a service.
Article 10-06 Reservations and exceptions.
1. No Party shall increase the degree of non-conformity of its existing measures with respect to Articles 10-03, 10-04 and 10-05, listed in Annex I. Any reform of any of these measures shall not decrease the degree of conformity of the measure as it was in force immediately before the reform.
2. The Parties do not have the obligation to register municipal measures.
3. Articles 10-03, 10-04 and 10-05 shall not apply to any measure that a Party adopts or maintains with respect to sectors, subsectors or activities, as indicated in its list in Annex II.
Article 10-07 Transparency.
1. In addition to the provisions of Article 17-02, each Party shall disclose in its official publishing bodies in accordance with its legislation, promptly and, except in emergency situations, no later than the date of its entry into force, all relevant laws, regulations, administrative guidelines, and other decisions, rulings, or actions of general application that relate to or affect the operation of this chapter, and have been put into effect by federal, central, and state governments or by a nongovernmental regulatory body . Likewise, international agreements that refer to or affect trade in services and to which a Party is a signatory will be published.
2. When the publication of the information referred to in paragraph 1 is not feasible or practical, it will be made available to the public in another way.
3. Each Party shall promptly inform the other Party, at least annually, of the establishment of new laws, regulations, or administrative guidelines that significantly affect trade in services covered by its specific commitments under this Chapter, or of changes it introduces in the existing ones.
4. Each Party shall respond promptly to any requests for specific information made by another Party about the measures referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2 The offices responsible for providing specific information to another Party that requests it on these matters, as well as on the that are subject to the notification obligation set forth in paragraph 3, will be listed in annex 10-07.
Article 10-08 Non-discriminatory quantitative restrictions.
1. Each Party shall indicate in its schedule in Annex V, within a period of six months from the date of entry into force of this Agreement, any quantitative restrictions that remain at the federal or central and state levels.
2. Each Party shall notify the other Parties of any quantitative restriction it adopts after the date of entry into force of this Agreement and shall indicate the restriction in its list in Annex V.
3. Each Party shall endeavor periodically, but in any case at least every two years, to negotiate the liberalization of the quantitative restrictions indicated in its schedule in Annex V, in accordance with the provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2.
Article 10-09 Future liberalization.
1. In order to achieve a level of progressive liberalization, the Commission will call negotiations every two years, aimed at:
a) eliminate the remaining restrictions registered in accordance with paragraph 1 of article 10-06; and
b) Gradually incorporate into Annex I sectors and activities that each Party has consigned in Annex II.
Article 10-10 Committee on Cross-Border Trade in Services and Investment.
1. The Parties establish a Committee on Cross-Border Trade in Services and Investment, made up of representatives of each Party, in accordance with Annex 10-07.
Where appropriate, the Committee may authorize the participation of representatives of other institutions.
2. The Committee shall meet at least once a year, or at any time at the request of any of the Parties, or of the Commission.
3. The Committee shall perform, among others, the following functions:
a) Oversee the execution and administration of Chapters X and XIV;
b) discuss matters on cross-border trade in services and investment that are submitted to it by the Parties;
c) facilitate the exchange of information between the Parties, as well as technical cooperation in the area of trade in services and investment; Y
d) examine issues of interest to the Parties related to trade in services and investment that are discussed in international forums.
Article 10-11 Procedures.
The Committee will establish procedures for:
a) that each Party notify another Party and include in its relevant annexes:
i) non-discriminatory quantitative restrictions, in accordance with article 10-08; Y
ii) the modifications to the measures referred to in article 10-06; Y
b) holding negotiations aimed at deepening the liberalization of services between the Parties, in accordance with Article 10-09.
Article 10-12 Granting of permits, authorizations and licenses.
In order to guarantee that any measure that a Party adopts or maintains in relation to the requirements and procedures for the granting of permits, authorizations and licenses to nationals of another Party does not constitute an unnecessary barrier to trade, each Party shall endeavor to guarantee that said measures:
a) are based on objective and transparent criteria, such as capacity, aptitude and competence to provide a service;
b) are not more burdensome than necessary to ensure the quality of a service; Y
c) do not constitute a disguised restriction on the cross-border provision of a service.
Article 10-13 Denial of benefits.
A Party may deny the benefits derived from this chapter to a service provider of another Party, after prior notification and consultation, when the Party determines that the service is being provided by a service provider that does not carry out substantive commercial operations in the territory of the Party. another Party and that, in accordance with the applicable law of that Party, is owned or controlled by persons of a non-Party.
Article 10-14 Technical cooperation.
The Parties shall establish, no later than one year after the entry into force of this Agreement, a system to provide service providers with information regarding their markets in relation to:
a) the commercial and technical aspects of the provision of services;
b) the possibility of obtaining technology in terms of services; Y
c) all those aspects that the Commission identifies regarding services.
Article 10-15 Other disciplines.
1. The Commission will determine the procedures for establishing the disciplines related to:
a) safeguard measures; Y
b) subsidies that may have distorting effects on trade in services.
2. For the purposes of paragraph 1, the work of the relevant international organizations will be taken into account.
Article 10-16 Relationship with multilateral agreements on services.
1. The Parties shall apply to each other the provisions contained in the multilateral agreements on services of which they are members.
2. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 1, in the event of any inconsistency between these agreements and this treaty, the latter shall prevail over the former, to the extent of the inconsistency.
Addendum on Professional Services
I. Definitions
For the purposes of this annex, it shall be understood as:
professional or professional : the natural person to whom a university degree or equivalent academic degree has been legally issued, once they have complied with higher education study plans and programs or have equivalent training or experience and who has the corresponding authorization to practice a specific profession;
professional services : those services that require a title or equivalent academic degree for their provision and whose exercise is authorized, regulated or restricted in each case by a Party, but does not include services provided by persons who practice a trade or to the crew of merchant ships and aircraft;
professional exercise : the habitual performance of any act, for consideration or free of charge, or the provision of any service specific to each profession that requires authorization, in accordance with the legislation of each Party, even if it is only a simple consultation or the ostentation of the character professional or professional;
higher education : academic training that culminates in obtaining a university degree and academic degree, awarded by an institution of higher education in accordance with the legislation of each Party;
recognition of titles or academic degrees : any acceptance by the competent authority (governmental or non-governmental) of a Party, of the official academic documentation, obtained by a professional or professional of another Party, in higher education institutions, in accordance with its legislation ; Y
authorization for professional practice : the professional license, registration or association granted to a professional or professional, by competent governmental or non-governmental institutions of a Party, to practice a profession that requires authorization, in accordance with its legislation.
II. Aim
The purpose of this annex is to establish the rules that the Parties will observe to harmonize, among them, the measures that will regulate the mutual recognition of titles or academic degrees for the provision of professional services, through the granting of authorization for professional practice.
III. Recognition of titles or academic degrees
When a Party recognizes unilaterally or by agreement with another country, academic titles or degrees, education, experience, licenses or certificates obtained in the territory of another Party or of any non-Party country:
a) the provisions of Article 10-03 shall not be interpreted in the sense of requiring that Party to recognize the titles or academic degrees, education, experience, licenses or certificates obtained in the territory of another Party; Y
b) the Party will provide another Party with the opportunity to demonstrate that the academic titles or degrees, education, experience, licenses or certificates obtained in the territory of that other Party may also be recognized, or to enter into an arrangement or agreement that has effect equivalents.
IV. Reciprocity
Each Party, within a period of one year from the date of entry into force of this treaty, shall examine the possibility of eliminating any requirement of nationality or permanent residence indicated in its list of Annex I that it maintains for the recognition of titles to professional service providers of another Party. Where a Party is unable to remove these requirements with respect to a particular sector, the other Party may, in the same sector and for as long as the Party maintains its requirement, maintain, as the sole remedy, an equivalent requirement. .
V. Committee on Professional Services
In order to follow up on and comply with the recommendations on mutual recognition of titles or academic degrees for professional practice agreed upon by the Parties, the Committee on Professional Services is hereby created, made up of the following governmental and non-governmental authorities and institutions:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the National Directorate of Higher Education of the Ministry of Education;
b) in the case of Guatemala: the University of San Carlos de Guatemala and the Assembly of Presidents of the Professional Colleges;
c) in the case of Honduras: the National Autonomous University of Honduras and the Federation of Professional University Colleges of Honduras; Y
d) in the case of Mexico: the General Directorate of Professions of the Ministry of Public Education. Notwithstanding the foregoing, each Party may incorporate other competent institutions or bodies into the Committee, as circumstances require. Each Party shall encourage the pertinent bodies to develop the mutually acceptable norms and criteria, referred to in item VI, as well as to submit to the Commission recommendations on mutual recognition of titles or academic degrees for professional practice.
The Committee will begin its activities within the six months following the entry into force of this treaty and will be convened by the Commission. In the first meeting, the members of the Committee will present proposals on the activities to be carried out to comply with this annex. The decisions adopted will be communicated to the Commission for follow-up.
SAW. Bases for the recognition of titles for professional practice
The Parties agree that the processes of mutual recognition of titles for the professional practice referred to in paragraph V will be based on improving the quality of professional services through the establishment of mutually acceptable standards and criteria for these processes, protecting at the same time to consumers and safeguarding the public interest.
The elaboration of norms and criteria referred to in the previous paragraph must consider the legislation of each Party and may be elaborated in relation to the following aspects: education, exams, experience, conduct and ethics; professional development and recertification; scope of action; local knowledge; supervision and consumer protection.
The Parties will provide detailed and necessary information for the mutual recognition of titles or academic degrees for professional practice, including what corresponds to academic courses, guides and study materials, payment of fees, exam dates, schedules, locations, affiliation to societies or professional colleges.
This information will include federal or central and state legislation, administrative guidelines and measures of general application and those developed by governmental and non-governmental bodies.
VII. Adoption of recommendations
Based on the recommendations received by the Parties and to the extent that these are compatible with the provisions of this treaty, the Commission will encourage the Parties so that their competent authorities adopt the recommendations presented in accordance with item VI and develop procedures. for the issuance of the corresponding authorization to the professional service providers of each Party.
VIII. Revision
The Parties shall periodically review, at least once a year, the application of the provisions of this Annex.
Annex 10-07 Information Centers
The offices in charge of providing specific information referred to in article 10-07 will be:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Directorate of Trade Policy of the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;  b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy or the one designated as an information center;
c) in the case of Honduras: the General Directorate for Economic Integration and Trade Policy of the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or its successor; and  d) in the case of Mexico: the General Directorate of International Services Negotiations of the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development, or its successor.
Annex 10-09 Land Transportation by Road
Six months after the entry into force of this treaty, Guatemala, Honduras and Mexico will begin negotiations in order to establish the conditions for the opening of land transport by road, within which the following aspects will be considered, among others:
a) removal of restrictions on cross-border trade; and  b) development of a work program to make the respective standardization measures of each Party compatible.
Annex 10-10 Committee on Cross-Border Trade in Services and Investment
In accordance with article 10-10, the Committee on Cross-Border Trade in Services and Investment will be composed of:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;  b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy, or its successor;  c) in the case of Honduras: the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or its successor; and  d) in the case of Mexico: the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development, or its successor.
Chapter XI FINANCIAL SERVICES
Article 11-01 Definitions.  For the purposes of this chapter, the following shall be understood as:  competent authority : the authorities of each Party indicated in Annex 11-01;  public entity : a central bank, monetary authority or any institution of a public nature in the financial system of a Party that is owned or controlled by the government of a Party, that performs governmental, regulatory or supervisory functions, excluding public entities principally engaged in the supply of financial services on commercial terms;  financial institution: any financial intermediary or a company that is authorized to provide financial services and is regulated or supervised as a financial institution under the laws of the Party in whose territory it was incorporated;  financial institution of another Party : a financial institution, incorporated in the territory of a Party, that is owned or controlled by persons of another Party;  investment :
a) shares and corporate quotas and any other form of participation, in any proportion, in a financial institution including the investment that it makes in a company that provides complementary or auxiliary services for the fulfillment of its corporate purpose, which grants the right to owner to participate in the income or profits thereof; and  b) a stake in a financial institution, including the investment that it makes in a company that provides complementary or auxiliary services for the fulfillment of its corporate purpose, which grants the owner the right to participate in the corporate assets of that financial institution in a sale; however, it will not be understood by investment:
a) pecuniary claims derived exclusively from:
i) commercial contracts for the sale of goods or services by a person in the territory of a Party to a company in the territory of another Party; or  ii) the granting of credit in connection with a commercial transaction, such as trade financing;
b) any other pecuniary claim that does not entail the types of rights provided in the literals of the definition of investment; or c) a loan granted by a financial institution or a debt security owned by a financial institution, except in the case of a loan granted to a financial institution or a debt security issued by a financial institution, which is treated as capital for regulatory effects by the Party in whose territory the financial institution is incorporated;
investment of an investor of a Party : the investment owned by, or under the direct or indirect control of, an investor of a Party, in the territory of another Party;  non-Party investment: the investment of an investor that is not an investor of a Party;  investor of a Party : a Party, a State enterprise of the Party, or a person of that Party that intends to make, makes or has made an investment in the territory of another Party;  Disputing Investor : A person who makes a claim pursuant to the provisions of Section B of Chapter XIV;  new financial service: a financial service not provided in the territory of a Party that is provided in the territory of another Party, including any new form of distribution of a financial service, or sale of a financial product that is not sold in the territory of a Party;  self-regulatory bodies : any non-governmental entity, including any stock or futures exchange, clearing house or any other association or organization that exercises its own or delegated regulatory or supervisory authority over financial institutions or cross-border financial service providers ;  person : a national or company of a Party, not including branches;  cross-border provision of financial services or cross-border trade in financial services: the provision of a financial service :
a) from the territory of one Party to the territory of another Party;  b) in the territory of a Party by a person of that Party to a person of another Party; or  c) by a person of a Party in the territory of another Party;
financial service provider of a Party : a person of a Party who is engaged in the business of providing any financial service in the territory of that Party;  cross-border financial service provider of a Party means a financial institution of a Party that seeks to provide or provides cross-border financial services; and  financial service : a service of a financial nature offered by a financial institution of a Party, which includes all insurance, reinsurance, banking services and other services involving financial intermediation, including related and auxiliary services of a financial nature.  Article 11-02 Scope of application and extension of obligations.  1. This Chapter applies to measures adopted or maintained by a Party relating to:
a) financial institutions of another Party;  b) cross-border trade in financial services; and  c) investors of another Party and investments of those investors in financial institutions in the territory of the Party, as well as investments of these in companies that provide them with complementary or auxiliary services for the fulfillment of their corporate purpose.
2. This chapter does not apply to:
a) Activities or services that are part of public retirement plans or public social security systems;  b) the use of financial resources owned by another Party; or  c) other financial activities or services on behalf of the Party or its public entities or with its guarantee.
3. In the event of any inconsistency between the provisions of this chapter and any other provision of this treaty, the provisions of this chapter shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.  4. Article 14-11 and Section B of Chapter XIV are incorporated into this Chapter.  Article 11-03 Self- regulated bodies.  When a Party requires that a financial institution or a cross-border financial service provider of another Party be a member of, participate in or have access to a self-regulatory body to offer a financial service in or to its territory, the Party shall ensure that such body complies with the obligations of this chapter.  Article 11-04 Right of establishment.  1. The Parties recognize the principle that investors of a Party should be allowed to establish a financial institution in the territory of another Party, through any of the modalities of establishment and operation that its legislation allows.
2. Each Party may impose, at the time of the establishment of a financial institution, terms and conditions that are consistent with Article 11-06.  Article 11-05 Cross-border trade.  1. Each Party shall permit persons located in its territory and its nationals, wherever located, to purchase financial services from cross-border financial service providers of another Party located in the territory of that other Party. This does not oblige a Party to allow such cross-border financial service providers to advertise or conduct business by any means in its territory. The Parties may define what is "advertise" and "do business" for purposes of this obligation.  2. When a Party allows the provision of cross-border financial services and without prejudice to other means of prudential regulation of cross-border trade in financial services, the Party may require the registration of cross-border financial service providers of another Party and of financial instruments.  Article 11-06 National treatment.  1. Each Party shall grant investors of another Party treatment no less favorable than it grants to its own similar investors with respect to the establishment, acquisition, expansion, administration, conduct, operation, sale or other forms of alienation of similar financial institutions and investments. in similar financial institutions in its territory.  2. Each Party shall accord to financial institutions of another Party and to investments of investors of another Party in financial institutions treatment no less favorable than it accords to its own similar financial institutions and to similar investments of its own similar investors in financial institutions. similar financial institutions regarding the establishment, acquisition, expansion, administration, management, operation, sale or other forms of alienation of financial institutions and investments.  3. When a Party allows the cross-border provision of a financial service pursuant to Article 11-05, it shall grant cross-border financial service providers of another Party treatment no less favorable than that it grants to its own similar financial service providers, with respect to the provision of such service.  4. The treatment accorded by a Party to financial institutions and cross-border financial service providers of another Party, whether identical or different from that accorded to its own similar institutions or similar service providers, is consistent with paragraphs 1 through 3, if it offers equal opportunity to compete.  5. Treatment by a Party does not provide equal opportunity to compete if it disadvantages similar financial institutions and similar cross-border financial service providers of another Party in their ability to provide financial services, compared with the ability of the Party's own financial institutions and financial service providers to provide those services.  Article 11-07 Most Favored Nation Treatment.  Each Party shall accord to financial institutions of another Party, to cross-border financial service providers of another Party, to investors of another Party, and to investments of such investors in financial institutions, treatment no less favorable than that accorded to financial institutions similar, to similar cross-border financial service providers, to similar investors and to investments of such investors in similar financial institutions of another Party or of another non-Party country.  Article 11-08 Recognition and harmonization.  1. When applying the measures included in this Chapter, a Party may recognize the prudential measures of another Party or of a non-Party. Such recognition may be:
a) granted unilaterally;  b) achieved through harmonization or other means; or  c) granted based on an agreement or arrangement with another Party or with a non-Party country.
2. The Party that grants recognition of prudential measures in accordance with paragraph 1 shall provide appropriate opportunities for any other Party to demonstrate that there are circumstances whereby equivalent regulations exist or will exist, supervision and enforcement of the regulation and, if appropriate, procedures for sharing information between the Parties.  3. Where a Party grants prudential measures recognition in accordance with paragraph 1 and the circumstances set forth in paragraph 2 exist, that Party shall provide appropriate opportunities for another Party to negotiate accession to the agreement or arrangement, or to negotiate an agreement or similar arrangement.  Article 11-09 Exceptions.  1. The provisions of this chapter shall not be construed as an impediment for a Party to adopt or maintain reasonable prudential measures of a financial nature, for reasons such as:
a) protect investors, depositors or other creditors, holders or beneficiaries of policies or creditors of fiduciary obligations in charge of a financial institution or a provider of cross-border financial services;  b) maintain the safety, soundness, integrity or financial responsibility of financial institutions or cross-border financial service providers; and  c) ensure the integrity and stability of the financial system of that Party.
2. The provisions of this chapter do not apply to non-discriminatory measures of general application adopted by a public entity in conducting monetary policies or credit policies, or exchange policies. This paragraph shall not affect the obligations of any Party under Article 11-17 or 14-07.  3.
