a) the disputing Party accepts the appointment of each member of a tribunal established under the ICSID Convention or the ICSID Additional Facility Rules; and  b) a disputing investor, whether on its own behalf or on behalf of a company, may submit a claim to arbitration or continue proceedings under the ICSID Convention, or the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, only on the condition that the investor contestant and, where appropriate, the company it represents, express their consent in writing on the appointment of each of the members of the court.
Article 14-29 Consolidation of proceedings.  1. A consolidation tribunal established pursuant to this article shall be established in accordance with the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules and shall proceed in accordance with the provisions of said rules, except as provided in this section.  2. When an accumulation tribunal determines that the claims submitted to arbitration in accordance with article 14-22 raise issues of fact and law in common, the accumulation tribunal, in the interest of their fair and efficient resolution, and having heard the disputing parties, may assume jurisdiction, process and resolve:
a) all or part of the demands, jointly; or  b) one or more of the demands in the understanding that this will contribute to the resolution of the others.
3. A disputing party seeking a consolidation order under paragraph 2 shall request the Secretary General to set up a consolidation tribunal and shall specify in its request:
a) the name of the disputing Party or of the disputing investors against whom the accumulation order is sought;  b) the nature of the accumulation order requested; and  c) the grounds on which the request is based.
4. Within a period of 60 days from the date of receipt of the request, the Secretary General will set up a consolidation tribunal made up of three arbitrators. The Secretary General shall appoint from the list of arbitrators referred to in Article 14-27, the president of the merger tribunal, who shall not be a national of the disputing Party or a national of the Party of the disputing investor. In the event that an available arbitrator is not found on the list to preside over the accumulation tribunal, the Secretary General shall designate, from the ICSID panel of arbitrators, the president of said tribunal, who shall not be a national of the disputing Party nor a national of the Party of the disputing investor. The Secretary General will appoint the other two members of the accumulation tribunal from the list of arbitrators referred to in Article 14-27 and, when they are not available on said list, will select them from the ICSID panel of arbitrators. If there are no arbitrators available on that panel, the Secretary General will make the remaining appointments at his discretion. One of the members shall be a national of the disputing Party and the other member of the consolidation tribunal shall be a national of a Party of the disputing investors.  5. When an accumulation tribunal has been established pursuant to this article, the disputing investor who has submitted a claim to arbitration pursuant to article 14-19, and has not been named in the application for accumulation made pursuant to paragraph 3, may apply in writing to the accumulation court to be included in an accumulation order made in accordance with paragraph 2, specifying in such application:
a) the name and domicile of the disputing investor and, where appropriate, the name or corporate name and domicile of the company;  b) the nature of the accumulation order requested; and  c) the grounds on which the request is based.
6. The accumulation court will provide, at the expense of the interested investor, a copy of the accumulation petition to the disputing investors that would be subject to the accumulation resolution.  7. A court will not have jurisdiction to decide a claim, or part of a claim, in respect of which a consolidation court has assumed jurisdiction. 8. At the request of a disputing party, a consolidation tribunal may, pending its decision under paragraph 2, order that the proceedings of a tribunal be stayed pending a decision on the merits of the consolidation. What is ordered by the accumulation court must be complied with by the court.  Article 14-30 Notifications.  1. Within a period of 15 days from the date of receipt, the disputing Party shall send the Secretariat a copy of:
a) a request for arbitration made pursuant to paragraph 1 of Article 36 of the ICSID Convention;  b) a notice of arbitration under the terms of Article 2 of Part C of the ICSID Additional Facility Rules; or  c) a notice of arbitration under the terms provided by the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules.
2. The disputing Party shall deliver to the Secretariat a copy of the request formulated in the terms of paragraph 3 of Article 14-29:
a) within 15 days from the receipt of the request, in the case of a request made by the disputing investor; or  b) within 15 days from the date of the request, in the case of a request made by the disputing Party.
3. The disputing Party shall deliver to the Secretariat a copy of a request made under the terms of paragraph 5 of Article 14-29 within a period of 15 days from the date of receipt of the request.  4. The Secretariat shall keep a public register of the documents referred to in paragraphs 1, 2 and 3.  5. The disputing Party shall deliver to the other Parties:
a) written notification of a claim that has been submitted to arbitration no later than 30 days after the date of submission of the claim to arbitration; and  b) copies of all pleadings submitted in the arbitration proceeding.
Article 14-31 Participation by a Party.  Upon written notice to the disputing parties, a Party may submit submissions to a tribunal established under this section on questions of interpretation of this treaty that are in dispute before that tribunal.   Article 14-32 Documentation.  1. A Party shall be entitled, at its own expense, to receive from a disputing party a copy of:
a) the evidence offered to a tribunal established pursuant to this section, and  b) the written arguments presented by the disputing parties.
2. A Party receiving information pursuant to paragraph 1 shall treat such information as if it were a disputing Party.  Article 14-33 Seat of the arbitration procedure.  Unless the disputing parties agree otherwise, a tribunal established pursuant to this section shall conduct arbitral proceedings in the territory of a Party that is a member of the New York Convention, which shall be selected in accordance with:
a) the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, if the arbitration is governed by those rules or by the ICSID Convention; or  b) the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules, if the arbitration is governed by those rules.
Article 14-34 Applicable law.  1. A tribunal established pursuant to this section shall decide disputes submitted to it in accordance with this treaty and the applicable provisions of international law.  2. The Commission's interpretation of a provision of this treaty shall be binding on a tribunal established pursuant to this section.  Article 14-35 Interpretation of annexes.  1. When a Party alleges as a defense that a measure allegedly in violation falls within the scope of a reservation or exception set forth in any of the annexes, at the request of the disputing Party, a tribunal established pursuant to this section shall request the Commission for an interpretation. on that matter. The Commission, within a period of 60 days from the delivery of the request, will present its interpretation in writing to said court.  2. The Commission's interpretation submitted pursuant to paragraph 1 shall be binding on a tribunal established pursuant to this section. If the Commission does not submit an interpretation within a period of 60 days, said court will decide on the matter.  Article 14-36 Expert Opinions.  Notwithstanding the appointment of other types of experts when authorized by the applicable arbitration rules, the tribunal established pursuant to this section, at the request of a disputing party, or on its own initiative unless the disputing parties do not agree, may appoint one or more experts to rule in writing on any issue raised by a disputing party in a proceeding, in accordance with the terms and conditions agreed upon by the disputing parties.  Article 14-37 Provisional or precautionary measures.  A tribunal established pursuant to this section may apply to domestic courts, or order disputing parties, provisional or injunctive relief to preserve the rights of the disputing party or to ensure that the jurisdiction of the tribunal established pursuant to this section is fully exercised. effects. That court may not order compliance or suspension of the measure allegedly in violation referred to in article 14-19.  Article 14-38 Final award.  1. When a tribunal established pursuant to this section renders a final award unfavorable to a Party, such tribunal may only order:
a) the payment of pecuniary damages and the corresponding interest; or  b) restitution of the property, in which case the award will provide that the disputing Party may pay pecuniary damages, plus applicable interest, instead of restitution.
2. A court established pursuant to this section may also order payment of costs in accordance with the applicable arbitration rules.  3. When the claim is made by an investor representing a company based on article 14-19:
a) the award that provides for the restitution of the property will provide that it be granted to the company; and  b) the award that awards pecuniary damages and corresponding interest will provide that the sum of money be paid to the company.
4. A tribunal established pursuant to this section may not order a Party to pay punitive damages.  5. The award will be rendered without prejudice to the rights that any person with a legal interest has regarding the reparation of the damages that he has suffered, in accordance with the applicable legislation.  Article 14-39 Finality and execution of the award.  1. The award rendered by a court established pursuant to this section shall be binding only for the disputing parties and only with respect to the specific case.  2. In accordance with paragraph 3 and the review procedure applicable to an interim award, a disputing party shall abide by and comply with the award without delay.  3. A disputing party may request enforcement of a final award provided that:
a) in the case of a final award rendered under the ICSID Convention:
i) 120 days have elapsed from the date the award was rendered without any disputing party requesting its clarification, revision, or annulment; or  ii) the clarification, review and annulment procedures have been completed; either
b) in the case of a final award under the ICSID Additional Facility Rules or the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules:
i) 90 days have elapsed from the date the award was rendered without any disputing party having initiated an interpretation, rectification, additional award or annulment procedure; or  ii) the procedures for interpretation, rectification or additional award have been concluded, or a judicial court of the disputing Party has resolved a request for annulment and this resolution is not susceptible to being challenged.
4. Each Party shall provide for the due enforcement of an award in its territory.  5. When a disputing Party fails to comply with or does not comply with a final award, the Commission, upon receipt of a request from a Party whose investor was a party to the arbitration proceeding, shall form an arbitral tribunal in accordance with Chapter XIX. The requesting Party may invoke such procedures to obtain:
a) a determination that the breach or contempt of the terms of the final award is contrary to the obligations of this treaty; and  b) a recommendation that the Party comply with and abide by the final award.
6. The disputing investor may resort to the enforcement of an arbitral award in accordance with the ICSID Convention, the New York Convention or the Inter-American Convention, regardless of whether or not the procedures contemplated in paragraph 5 have been initiated.  7. For purposes of the Article I of the New York Convention and Article I of the Inter-American Convention, it shall be considered that the claim submitted to arbitration pursuant to this section arises from a commercial relationship or operation.  Article 14-40 General Provisions.  Moment in which the claim is considered submitted to arbitration  1. A claim is deemed submitted to arbitration under the terms of this section when:
a) the request for arbitration under paragraph 1 of Article 36 of the ICSID Convention has been received by the Secretary-General;  b) the notice of arbitration, pursuant to Article 2 of Part C of the ICSID Additional Facility Rules, has been received by the Secretary-General; or  c) the notice of arbitration provided for in the UNCITRAL Arbitration Rules has been received by the disputing Party.
Delivery of documents  2. The delivery of the notification and other documents to a Party shall be made at the place designated by it, in accordance with Annex 14-40 (2). Payments under insurance or guarantee contracts  3. In an arbitration proceeding requested in accordance with the provisions of this section, a Party shall not adduce as a defense, counterclaim, right of compensation, or others, that the disputing investor received or will receive, according to with an insurance or guarantee contract, indemnity or other compensation for all or part of the alleged damages for which restitution is requested.  Publication of awards  4. The publication of awards will be made in accordance with the provisions of the rules of procedure.  Article 14-41 Exclusions.  The dispute settlement provisions of this section, and those of Chapter XIX shall not apply to resolutions adopted by a Party by virtue of paragraph 2, letter c) of Article 14-02, nor to the cases contained in Annex 14- 41.  Article 14-42 Subrogation.  In the event that a Party or the entity designated by it has granted any financial guarantee on non-commercial risks in relation to an investment made by its investors in the territory of another Party and from the moment the first Party or its designated entity has made any payment charged to the guarantee granted, said Party or the designated entity will be the direct beneficiary of all types of payments to which the investor could be a creditor. In the event of a dispute, only the investor may initiate or participate in proceedings before a court established pursuant to this section.  Article 14-41 Exclusions.  The dispute settlement provisions of this section, and those of Chapter XIX shall not apply to resolutions adopted by a Party by virtue of paragraph 2, letter c) of Article 14-02, nor to the cases contained in Annex 14- 41.  Article 14-42 Subrogation.  In the event that a Party or the entity designated by it has granted any financial guarantee on non-commercial risks in relation to an investment made by its investors in the territory of another Party and from the moment the first Party or its designated entity has made any payment charged to the guarantee granted, said Party or the designated entity will be the direct beneficiary of all types of payments to which the investor could be a creditor. In the event of a dispute, only the investor may initiate or participate in proceedings before a court established pursuant to this section.
Annex 14-11 Public Utility
For the purposes of literal a) of paragraph 1 of article 14-11, the following are understood to be included in the term of public utility:
a) in the case of El Salvador: public utility or social interest;  b) in the case of Guatemala: collective utility, social benefit or public interest;  c) in the case of Honduras: need or public interest; and  d) in the case of Mexico: public utility.
Exhibit 14-40(2) Service of Notices and other Documents
1. For the purposes of article 14-40 (2), the place for delivery of notices and other documents shall be:
a) in the case of El Salvador:  Directorate of Trade Policy, Ministry of Economy Alameda Juan Pablo II, Guadalupe Street, Building C-2, Floor 3, Government Center San Salvador, El Salvador  b) in the case of Guatemala:  Ministry of Economics 8th. Avenida 10-43 zone 1 Guatemala, Guatemala  c) in the case of Honduras:  General Directorate for Economic Integration and Trade Policy, Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce Avenida Jeréz, Edificio Larach, Floor 10 Tegucigalpa, MDC, Honduras  d ) in the case of Mexico:  General Directorate of Foreign Investment, Secretariat of Commerce and Industrial Development Insurgentes Sur 1940, Piso 8, Colonia Florida, CP 01030 México, DF
2. The Parties will communicate any change in the place designated for the delivery of notifications and other documents.
Annex 14-41 Exclusions
They will not be subject to the dispute resolution mechanisms provided in section B or chapter XIX:
a) in the case of Honduras: the resolutions adopted by the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce in application of articles 11 and 18 of the Foreign Investment Law regarding health, national security and preservation of the environment .  b) in the case of Mexico, the resolutions adopted by the National Foreign Investment Commission that prohibit or restrict the acquisition of an investment in the territory of the United Mexican States that is owned or controlled by its nationals, or by one or more investors from another Party, as well as the resolutions related to the provisions of Annex I, page IMF-4. 
 
CHAPTER XV MEASURES RELATING TO STANDARDIZATION
Article 15-01 Definitions.  For the purposes of this chapter, the Parties will use the terms presented in the current ISO/CEI Guide 2, "General terms and their definitions in relation to standardization and related activities"; however, the following shall be understood as:  TBT Agreement : the Agreement on Technical Barriers to Trade, which is part of the WTO Agreement;  hazardous waste: any material generated in the extraction, benefit, transformation, production, consumption, use, control or treatment processes, whose quality does not allow it to be used again and which, due to its corrosive, toxic, poisonous, reactive, radioactive, explosive, flammable characteristics, infectious or irritating biological, represent a danger to health or the environment;  risk assessment : the assessment of the potential damage to human, animal or plant health or safety, or the environment, could be caused by any good or service traded between the Parties;  make compatible: bring different standardization measures, approved by different standardization bodies, but with the same scope, to a level such that they are identical, equivalent or have the effect of allowing goods or services to be used interchangeably or for the same purpose, so that goods and services are allowed to be marketed between the Parties;  certification conformity mark : the mark protected, applied or issued in accordance with the rules of a certification system, which guarantees that the relevant product, process or service is in conformity with a standard or other specific normative document;  measures relating to standardization: standards, technical regulations or conformity assessment procedures;  standard : the document approved by a recognized institution that provides, for common and repeated use, rules, guidelines or characteristics for goods or related processes and production methods, or for related services or methods of operation, and the observance of which is not mandatory. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging, marking or labeling requirements applicable to, or dealing exclusively with, a good, service, process or method of production or operation;  international standard – a standard or other guide or recommendation, adopted by an international standard-setting body and made available to the public;  legitimate objectives: among others, the guarantee of safety or the protection of health or life, human, animal or plant, the guarantee of safety or protection of the environment, or the prevention of practices that may mislead or deceive consumers, including matters related to the identification of goods or services, considering, among other aspects, when appropriate, fundamental factors of a climatic, geographical, technological, infrastructure or scientific justification type;  standardization body : a body whose standardization activities are recognized by the government of each Party, respectively;  international standardization body: a standards body open to participation by relevant bodies from at least all parties to the TBT Agreement, including the International Organization for Standardization (ISO), the International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC), the Codex Alimentarius Commission, the Organization World Health Organization (WHO) and its dependent bodies, the International Organization of Legal Metrology (OIML), the International Bureau of Weights and Measures (BIPM) and the International Commission on Radiological Units and Measurements (ICUMR) or any other body that Parties designate;  approval procedure: any mandatory administrative process to obtain a registration, license, permit, or any other authorization, in order for a good or service to be marketed or used for defined purposes or in accordance with established conditions;  conformity assessment procedure : any procedure used, directly or indirectly, to determine whether the relevant requirements established by technical regulations or standards are met, including sampling, testing, inspection, evaluation, verification, assurance of conformity, accreditation, certification , registration or approval, used for those purposes;  administrative rejection: the actions taken by a public administration body of the importing Party, in the exercise of its powers, to prevent the entry into its territory of a shipment or the provision of a service, due to non-compliance with technical regulations or evaluation procedures of conformity;  technical regulation: the document that establishes the characteristics of the goods or their processes and related production methods, or the characteristics of the services or their related methods of operation, including the applicable administrative provisions, and whose observance is mandatory. It may also include or deal exclusively with terminology, symbols, packaging or labeling requirements applicable to a good, service, process or method of production or operation;  service : any service within the scope of this treaty, which is subject to measures relating to standardization or metrology; and  dangerous substances: those that threaten human, animal or plant life or health or the environment, and that are identified as such by national and international organizations.  Article 15-02 Scope of application.  1. This Chapter applies to measures related to standardization and metrology of the Parties, as well as to measures related to them that may directly or indirectly affect trade in goods or services between them.  2. This chapter does not apply to sanitary and phytosanitary measures.  Article 15-03 Confirmation of international rights and obligations.  The Parties confirm their current rights and obligations regarding measures related to standardization arising from the TBT Agreement and other international agreements to which the Parties are party, including agreements on health, the environment and its conservation, and consumer protection.  Article 15-04 Extension of obligations.  Each Party shall comply with the provisions of this chapter and shall adopt the necessary measures to guarantee its compliance by its federal or central and state or departmental and municipal government and shall adopt the measures in this regard that are within its power with respect to non-governmental organizations. standardization in its territory.  Article 15-05 Main rights and obligations.  1. Each Party may set the level of protection it considers appropriate to achieve its legitimate objectives.  2. Each Party may elaborate, adopt, apply and maintain the measures related to standardization that allow guaranteeing its level of protection of human, animal or plant life or health, or of the environment, or for the prevention of practices that may induce to error or deception of the consumer, as well as the measures that guarantee its application and compliance, including the relevant approval procedures.  3. Neither Party shall develop, adopt, apply or maintain standardization measures or approval procedures that have the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade between them. To this end, each Party shall ensure that measures related to standardization or approval procedures do not restrict trade, except as strictly necessary for the achievement of its legitimate objectives, taking into account the technical and economic possibilities, and the risks that it would create. its breach.  4. In connection with its measures relating to standardization, each Party shall grant to goods and services originating in the territory of the other Party national treatment and treatment no less favorable than that accorded to similar goods and similar services originating from any other non-Party country.  5. At the request of El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras, the Committee on Measures Related to Standardization will evaluate and recommend to the Commission for its resolution, actions on any matter related to measures related to standardization and approval procedures, taking into account their specific needs related to Article 12 of the TBT Agreement, so that its elaboration, adoption and application do not represent an obstacle to trade. These actions must be specific and with a defined temporality.  Article 15-06 Use of international standards.  1. Each Party shall use for the elaboration, development or application of its measures related to standardization, the international standards in force or imminent adoption, except when those international standards do not constitute an effective or adequate means to achieve its legitimate objectives, due to factors of a climatic, geographical, technological or infrastructure nature, or for scientifically proven reasons.  2. It shall be presumed that a standardization measure of a Party that conforms to an international standard is consistent with the provisions of paragraphs 3 and 4 of Article 15-05.  3. In the pursuit of its legitimate objectives and due to fundamental factors of a climatic, geographic, technological or infrastructure nature, or for scientifically proven reasons, each Party may adopt, apply or maintain any standardization measure that results in a level of higher protection than would have been obtained if the measure were based on an international standard.  Article 15-07 Risk assessment.  1. Each Party may carry out risk assessments in its territory, provided that this does not have the purpose or effect of creating unnecessary obstacles to trade between them. When making such assessments, they will take into account the risk assessment methods developed by international organizations and will ensure that their measures related to standardization are based on assessments of the risk to human, animal or plant life or health, or safety of the environment.  2. The Party that performs a risk assessment shall take into consideration all the pertinent scientific evidence, the available technical information, the intended end use, the processes or methods of production, operation, inspection, quality, sampling or testing, or the conditions environmental.  3. Having established the level of protection that it considers appropriate in accordance with paragraph 1 of Article 15-05, in conducting a risk assessment, each Party shall avoid arbitrary or unjustifiable distinctions between like goods and like services, if those distinctions:
a) have the effect of arbitrary or unjustifiable discrimination against goods or services of another Party;  b) constitute a disguised restriction on trade between the Parties; or  c) discriminate between similar goods or services for the same use, in accordance with the same conditions that pose the same level of risk and that grant similar benefits.
4. When the Party that carries out a risk assessment concludes that the scientific evidence or other information available is insufficient to complete the assessment, it may provisionally adopt a technical regulation, of the type established in paragraph 5 of Article 15. -12 based on available relevant information, in accordance with paragraph 2. Once sufficient information has been presented to it to complete the risk assessment, the Party shall complete its assessment as soon as possible, review and, where appropriate, reconsider the provisional technical regulation in the light of that assessment.  Article 15-08 Compatibility and equivalence.  1. The Parties will work together to strengthen the level of safety and protection of human, animal or plant life or health, or the level of safety and protection of the environment, and to prevent practices that may lead to misleading or misleading consumers.  2. Without prejudice to the rights conferred on them by this Chapter and taking into account international standardization activities, the Parties will make their respective measures related to standardization compatible to the greatest extent possible, without reducing the level of security and protection to health or human, animal or plant life, or the level of safety and protection of the environment, or the prevention of practices that may mislead or deceive consumers.  3. At the request of a Party, another Party shall take reasonable measures within its power to promote the compatibility of its specific standardization measures with the standardization measures of the requesting Party, taking into account the procedures and international activities in the matter.  4. The importing Party will accept as equivalent to its own technical regulation the one adopted or maintained by the exporting Party, when the latter proves to the satisfaction of the former that its technical regulation adequately meets the legitimate objectives of the importing Party. For purposes of this accreditation, the importing Party shall cooperate with the exporting Party. The importing Party shall communicate in writing to the exporting Party, at its request, the reasons for non-acceptance of a technical regulation.  5. To the extent possible, each Party shall accept the results of conformity assessment procedures that are carried out in the territory of another Party, provided that they offer a satisfactory guarantee, equivalent to that provided by the procedures that it provides. Accepting Party carries out or that are carried out in its territory and whose result it accepts, that the relevant good or service complies with the technical regulation or with the applicable standard adopted or maintained in the territory of the accepting Party.  6. Upon acceptance of the results of a conformity assessment procedure in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 5 and, in order to strengthen the confidence and reliability of the conformity assessment results of each of them, The Parties may consult on matters such as the technical capacity of conformity assessment bodies, taking into account the verified compliance with the relevant international standards through that means of accreditation.  Article 15-09 Conformity assessment.  1. Taking into account the differences in the conformity assessment procedures in their respective territories, the Parties will make their respective conformity assessment procedures compatible, to the greatest extent possible, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.  2. For the mutual benefit of the Parties, each Party shall accredit, approve, license or recognize conformity assessment bodies in the territory of another Party on terms no less favorable than those granted to those bodies in its territory.  3. For conformity assessment procedures, a Party may use the existing technical capacity and structure of accredited bodies pursuant to paragraph 2, established in the territory of another Party.  4. With regard to its conformity assessment procedures, each Party:
a) refrain from adopting, maintaining or applying stricter conformity assessment procedures than necessary, to ensure that the good or service complies with the applicable technical regulation or standard, taking into account the risks that non-conformity could create ;  b) initiate and complete those procedures in the most expeditious manner possible;  c) establish a non-discriminatory order for processing applications;  d) it will grant to the goods and services of another Party, national treatment and a treatment no less favorable than that which it grants to originating goods and similar services of any other non-Party country;  e) publish the normal duration of each of these procedures or communicate, at the request of the applicant, the approximate duration of the procedure;  f) ensure that the competent national body:
i) upon receipt of an application, promptly examine the documentation for completeness and accurately inform the applicant of any deficiencies, it being the applicant's responsibility to correct them within the appropriate period;  (ii) as soon as possible, provide the applicant with the accurate and complete results of the conformity assessment procedure so that any corrective action can be taken by the applicant;  iii) when the application is deficient and at the request of the applicant, continue the procedure to the extent possible; and  iv) inform the applicant of the reasons for any delay and, at his request, the status of his application;
g) require from the applicant only the information necessary to assess conformity and determine the appropriate cost of the assessment;  h) grant confidential information, regarding a good or service of another Party, that is presented or derived from the procedure, national treatment and a treatment that protects the commercial interests of the applicant;  i) ensure that any charge charged for assessing the conformity of an imported good or service is equitable with that charged for assessing the conformity of an identical or similar good or service of the importing Party, taking into account communication, transport and other related costs;  j) ensure, where possible, that the procedure is carried out at the production facility of the good and, where appropriate, a certification conformance mark is awarded;  k) will limit the procedure to what is necessary, to determine that a good or service that has been modified continues to comply with a technical regulation or standard, as long as it is a good or service that has been determined prior to its modification, which complies with the pertinent requirements established by that technical regulation or that standard;  l) will limit any requirement related to samples of a good to what is essential, and will prevent their selection and collection from causing unnecessary inconvenience to the applicant or his representative; Y  m) prevent the location of the facilities where the procedures are carried out from causing unnecessary inconvenience to the applicant or his representative.
5. Each Party will give favorable consideration to the request of any Party, to negotiate agreements on the mutual recognition of the results of the conformity assessment procedures.  Article 15-10 Approval procedures.  1. The Parties shall grant national treatment in their approval procedures.  2. Notwithstanding the foregoing, when specific application requirements are required within the approval procedures for imported goods or services that are not granted national treatment in said requirements, they must comply with the provisions of paragraph 3. of article 15-05.  3. When a Party considers that any specific application requirement demanded by another Party for imported goods or services in accordance with the preceding paragraph does not comply with the provisions of paragraph 3 of Article 15-05, it may submit it to the Approval Procedures Subcommittee. , based on the provisions of article 15-16. In order to achieve a mutually satisfactory solution to the dispute, the consultations must be carried out within 15 days following the date of submission of the request.  The Parties in consultation, by mutual agreement, may extend said term for up to 90 days.  4. Each Party, in relation to its approval procedures, shall ensure that:
a) refrain that the procedures and their application are not stricter than necessary, taking into account the risks that non-compliance could create;  b) initiate and complete that procedure in the most expeditious manner possible;  c) establish a non-discriminatory order for processing applications;  d) communicate, at the applicant's request, the approximate duration of the procedure;  e) that the competent national body:
i) upon receipt of an application, promptly examine the documentation for completeness and accurately inform the applicant of any deficiencies, it being the applicant's responsibility to correct them within the appropriate period;  (ii) as soon as possible, provide the applicant with the results of the approval procedure, accurately and completely, so that any corrective action can be taken by the applicant; and  iii) inform the applicant of the reasons for any delay and, at his request, the status of his application;
f) require the applicant only the information necessary to carry out the approval procedure and determine the cost thereof;  g) grant confidential information, regarding a good or service of another Party, that is submitted or derived from the approval procedure, national treatment and a treatment that protects the commercial interests of the applicant;  h) that any charge charged for the procedure is equitable with that charged for the procedure for an identical or similar good or service of the Party carrying out the approval procedure, taking into account communication costs, transport and other related; and  i) limit any requirement related to samples of an asset to the essentials.
5. The Parties will grant, in accordance with their legislation, the sanitary registry for the goods that require it.  Article 15-11 Metrological standards.  Each Party shall guarantee the traceability of its metrological standards in accordance with the recommendations of the BIPM and the OIML, as stipulated in this chapter.  Article 15-12 Notification, publication and delivery of information.  1. Each Party shall notify the other Parties of the measures related to standardization and metrology that it decides to establish before they enter into force and on the same day as their nationals.  2. Each Party shall notify the other Parties of the measures related to standardization and metrology that are no longer in force.  3. When, in accordance with its legislation, a Party proposes the adoption or modification of any measure related to standardization or metrology:
a) publish a notice and notify the other Parties in writing of its intention to adopt or modify that measure, in order to allow interested persons to know the content of the proposal, at least 60 days prior to its adoption; or modification;  b) will identify in that notice and notification, the good or service to which the measure will be applied, and will include a brief description of the objective and the motivation of the same;  c) provide a copy of the proposed measure to the other Parties and to any interested person who requests it and, where possible, identify the provisions that deviate substantially from relevant international standards;  d) without discrimination, allow the other Parties and interested persons to make comments in writing, discuss them and take them into account, and upon request, let them know the results of the discussions; and  e) ensure that, upon adopting the measure, it is published expeditiously or, in some other way, made available to interested persons of another Party so that they may know its content.
4. Each Party, to the extent possible, shall notify the other Parties that express an interest in the matter, of any modification or adoption of a law or regulation that contains provisions related to technical regulations.  5. When a Party considers it necessary to address an urgent problem related to safety or the protection of human, animal or plant life or health, or safety or environmental protection or practices that may lead to to error or deception of consumers, you may omit any of the steps established in paragraph 3, provided that when adopting the standardization measure:
a) immediately notify the other Parties, in accordance with the requirements established in subparagraph b) of paragraph 3, including a description of the urgent problem;  b) deliver a copy of the measure to the other Parties and to any interested person who requests it;  c) without discrimination, allow the other Parties and interested persons to make comments in writing, discuss them and take them into account, and upon request, let them know the results of the discussions; and  d) ensure that the measure is published expeditiously, or otherwise allow interested persons to know its content;
6. Each Party shall allow an adequate period between the publication of its measures relating to standardization and metrology, and the date on which they enter into force, for interested persons to adapt their goods, services or production methods to these measures. , except when it is necessary to deal with one of the urgent problems indicated in paragraph 5.  7. Each Party shall annually notify the other Parties in writing of its plans and programs for standardization.  8. The Parties designate as competent authorities, responsible for the application of the notification provisions of this chapter, those indicated in annex 15-12. When a Party designates two or more government authorities for this purpose, it must inform the other Party, precisely and completely, of the scope of responsibilities of those authorities.  9. When a Party makes an administrative rejection, it shall promptly inform in writing, the person holding the shipment or the service provider, the justification for the rejection.  10. Once the information referred to in paragraph 9 is generated, the Party shall send it immediately to the information center or centers in its territory, referred to in article 15-13, which, in turn, They will make it known to the information center or centers of another Party.  Article 15-13 Information centers.  1. Each Party shall ensure that it has at least one information center in its territory, responsible for answering and responding to questions and reasonable requests from another Party and interested persons, as well as providing the relevant updated documentation in relation to :
a) any measure relating to standardization, metrological standards or approval procedures, adopted or proposed in its territory by governmental or non-governmental bodies;  b) any standard or conformity assessment process adopted or proposed by non-governmental standardization bodies in its territory;  c) the membership and participation of that Party, its authorities or relevant non-governmental organizations in its territory, in international or regional standardization bodies and conformity assessment systems, in bilateral or multilateral agreements, within the scope application of this chapter, as well as in relation to the provisions of those systems and agreements;  d) the medium, date and location of the notices published pursuant to this chapter, or the place where the information they contain can be obtained; and  e) the Party's risk assessment procedures, the factors it takes into consideration when carrying out the assessment and for establishing the levels of protection it deems appropriate, to achieve its legitimate objectives in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.
2. When a Party designates more than one information center:
a) inform the other Party about the scope of competence of each one of said centers; and  b) ensure that any request sent to the wrong information center is forwarded, in an expedited manner, to the correct information center.
3. Each Party shall ensure that, when the other Party or interested persons, in accordance with the provisions of this chapter, request copies of the documents referred to in paragraph 1, they are provided at the same price as its nationals, except the cost actual shipping.  4. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 3, when the information center of a Party requests copies of documents issued by government agencies from the other Party, these shall be provided to them free of charge, except for the actual cost of shipping.  5. The obligation to answer and respond to the questions and reasonable requests referred to in paragraph 1, will in no way be understood in the sense that the information center is empowered to interpret any measure related to standardization or metrological standards adopted or proposed. in their territory. However, said information center must refer the Party or interested persons to the competent authority or body.  Article 15-14 Committee on Measures Related to Standardization.  1. The Parties establish the Committee for Measures Related to Standardization, which will be made up of specialized representatives of each of them. The Parties, by common agreement, will establish the procedures for determining the number and selection of their representatives. This Committee:
a) meet at least once a year, unless the Parties agree otherwise;  b) will make its decisions by consensus; and  c) will issue its own regulations, which will be approved by the Commission.
2. The Committee will have, among others, the following functions:
a) supervise the application, compliance and administration of this chapter;  b) respond to queries on issues related to measures related to standardization and metrology and formulate to the Commission any recommendations it deems pertinent;  c) submit to the Parties, when appropriate, proposals to resolve in the most expeditious manner, the problems derived from technical barriers to trade;  d) report annually to the Commission on the application of this chapter;  e) create the subcommittees it deems necessary, granting them the corresponding functions; and  f) any other assigned by the Commission.
Article 15-15 Subcommittee on Labeling, Packaging and Packaging.  1. The Parties establish the Labeling, Packaging and Packaging Subcommittee, which reports to the Committee and will be made up of competent representatives of each of them. The Parties, by mutual agreement, will establish the procedures for determining the number and selection of their representatives.  2. The Subcommittee will develop harmonized standards on labeling, packaging and packaging and will have the following functions:
a) make recommendations, among others, on:
i) common systems of symbols and pictograms;  ii) definitions, terminology and warning labeling;  iii) presentation of information, including language, measurement systems, ingredients and sizes; Y
b) any other assigned by the Committee.
3. Until such harmonized standards are adopted, each Party will apply its relevant labeling requirements, in accordance with the provisions of Article 15-06 and the other provisions of this chapter.  Article 15-16 Approval Procedures Subcommittee.  1. The Parties establish the Approval Procedures Subcommittee, which reports to the Committee and will be made up of competent representatives of each of them. The Parties, by mutual agreement, will establish the procedures for determining the number and selection of their representatives.  2. The Subcommittee will have the following functions:
a) develop a directory of representatives of relevant government authorities, who serve as a point of contact and exchange of information on its approval procedures and keep it updated;  b) identify the approval procedures whose adoption or application cause specific problems for the other Party.  c) examine such specific problems with the aim of reaching a mutually satisfactory agreement and make recommendations for their corresponding solution;  d) develop, where appropriate, equivalent approval procedures for goods and services that are subject to those requirements; and  e) any other assigned by the Committee.
Article 15-17 Subcommittee on Measures Related to Telecommunications Standardization  1. The Subcommittee on Measures Related to Telecommunications Standardization will develop, within a period of six months from the entry into force of this treaty, a work program , including a calendar, to make the measures related to standardization compatible with the authorized equipment.  2. The Subcommittee may address other issues related to standards regarding telecommunications equipment or services and any other issues it deems appropriate.  3. The Sub-Committee shall take into account relevant work carried out by the Parties in other forums, as well as that of non-governmental standard-setting entities.  Article 15-18 Technical consultations.  1. When a Party has doubts about the interpretation or application of this chapter, it may request that the Committee meet to seek a mutually satisfactory solution to the difference or resort to the dispute settlement mechanism provided for in Chapter XIX. The Parties may not use both channels simultaneously.  2. When a Party decides to go to the Committee, it shall be notified so that it may consider the matter or refer it to a sub-working group or other competent forum, in order to obtain non-binding technical advice or recommendations.  3. The Committee will consider any matter referred to it in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2, in the most expeditious manner possible and will inform the Parties of any advice or technical recommendation that it develops or receives in relation to that matter. Once the Parties receive the requested technical advice or recommendation from the Committee, they will send to the latter a written response in relation to that technical advice or recommendation, in a period determined by the Committee.  4. In the event that the technical recommendation issued by the Committee does not resolve the difference between the Parties, they may resort to the dispute resolution mechanism established in Chapter XIX. Unless the Parties agree otherwise, the consultations carried out before the Committee or any of the subcommittees created shall constitute technical consultations for the purposes established in the dispute settlement mechanism in accordance with paragraph 2 of article 19-06.  5. The technical information generated in the Committee may be considered in the event that consultations are established under the framework of the dispute resolution mechanism.  6. The Party that asserts that a standardization measure of the other Party is inconsistent with the provisions of this Chapter shall prove the inconsistency.  Article 15-19 Management of hazardous substances and hazardous waste.  1. For the control and management of hazardous substances and hazardous waste, the Parties shall apply the provisions, guides or recommendations of the Charter of the United Nations, the Basel Convention and the international agreements to which they are party, as well as their current legislation.  2. Each Party shall regulate, in accordance with its legislation, the introduction, acceptance, deposit, transportation, and transit through its territory of dangerous substances and dangerous, radioactive, and other wastes of internal or external origin that, due to their characteristics, constitute a danger to public health or the environment.  Article 15-20 Technical cooperation.  1. At the request of a Party, the other Party may provide information or technical assistance, to the extent of its possibilities and in mutually agreed terms, in order to help comply with the provisions of this chapter and strengthen the activities, processes, systems and measures relating to standardization and metrology of that Party.  2. The activities referred to in paragraph 1 include:
a) the development of a mutual accreditation system for verification units and testing laboratories;  b) implementation of intercomparison programs in order to ensure that the optimal conditions of the systems and methods to be used and evaluated are maintained;  c) strengthening of the formal communication systems established in this chapter;  d) exchange of information on technical cooperation programs related to measures related to standardization carried out by a Party; and  e) identification of specific needs, such as:
i) the application of good manufacturing practices in the preparation and approval of medicines, particularly those for human use;  ii) the application of good laboratory practices in the analysis and evaluation systems established in the pertinent international guidelines in force; and  iii) the development of common identification and nomenclature systems for auxiliary goods for health and medical instruments; Y
f) preparation of training programs, training and organization of, among others, a common system for training, continuing education, training and evaluation of sanitary officials and inspectors.
Annex 15-12 Competent authorities
For the purposes of article 15-12, the authority in charge of notification will be:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Ministry of Economy, through the Directorate of Commercial Policy, or its successor;  b) in the case of Guatemala: the Ministry of Economy, through the Guatemalan Standards Commission (COGUANOR), or its successor;  c) in the case of Honduras: the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, through the General Directorate of Consumer Protection, or its successor; and  d) in the case of Mexico: the Ministry of Commerce and Industrial Development, through the General Directorate of Standards, or its successor.
Chapter XVI INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY  Section A General provisions and basic principles
Article 16-01 Definitions.  For the purposes of this chapter, the following shall be understood as:  Berne Convention : the Berne Convention for the Protection of Literary and Artistic Works (1971);  Geneva Convention : the Geneva Convention for the Protection of Producers of Phonograms against Unauthorized Duplication of their Phonograms (1971);  Paris Convention : the Paris Convention for the Protection of Industrial Property (1967);  Rome Convention : the Rome Convention for the Protection of Performers, Producers of Phonograms and Broadcasting Organizations (1961);  Intellectual Property Rights: includes all categories of intellectual property that are protected by this chapter, in the terms indicated therein;  nationals of the other Party : with respect to the relevant intellectual property right, persons who would meet the eligibility criteria for protection under the Rome Convention, the Berne Convention, the Geneva Convention, and the Paris Convention;  public: any group of individuals who are intended to be directed and are capable of perceiving communications or execution of works, regardless of whether they can do so at the same time and place, or at different times and places, provided that this group is larger than one family and immediate circle of acquaintances. However, the public shall not be understood as a group made up of a limited number of individuals who have the same type of close relationships, which has not been formed for the main purpose of receiving these performances and communications of works; and  encrypted program-carrying satellite signal: one that is transmitted in a form by which the auditory or visual characteristics, or both, are modified or altered to prevent the reception of the program carried in that signal by persons who lack the equipment that is designed to eliminate the effects of such modification or alteration.  Article 16-02 Protection of intellectual property rights.  1. Each Party shall grant in its territory to the nationals of another Party adequate and effective protection and defense of intellectual property rights and shall ensure that the measures designed to enforce those rights do not become, in turn, obstacles to trade. legitimate.  2. Each Party may grant in its legislation protection of intellectual property rights that is broader than that required in this chapter, provided that such protection does not infringe the provisions of this chapter.  3. The Parties may freely establish the appropriate procedure to apply the provisions of this chapter, within the framework of their own legal system and practice.  Article 16-03 Provisions on the matter.  In order to grant adequate and effective protection and defense of intellectual property rights, the Parties shall apply, at least, the rules contained in this chapter and the substantive provisions of:
a) the Berne Convention;  b) the Geneva Convention;  c) the Rome Convention; and  d) the Paris Convention.
Article 16-04 National treatment.  1. Each Party shall grant to the nationals of another Party, treatment no less favorable than that granted to its own nationals in matters of acquisition, protection and defense of the intellectual property rights contemplated in this chapter, subject to exceptions and provided for in the Berne Convention, the Rome Convention and the Paris Convention.  2. No Party may require nationals of another Party, as a condition for the granting of national treatment under this article, to comply with any formality or condition to acquire copyright.  Article 16-05 Exceptions.  Each Party may resort to the exceptions indicated in Article 16-04 in relation to judicial and administrative procedures for the protection and defense of intellectual property rights, including the designation of a legal domicile or a representative within the jurisdiction of the Party, provided that such exception:
a) It is necessary to ensure compliance with provisions that are not incompatible with those of this chapter; and  b) is not applied in such a way as to constitute a disguised restriction on trade.
Article 16-06 Most-favoured-nation treatment.  With respect to the protection of intellectual property rights, any advantage, favour, privilege or immunity that a Party grants to the nationals of any other non-Party country shall be granted immediately and without conditions to the nationals of the other Party.  Exempt from this obligation are any advantages, favors, privileges or immunity granted in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights, Annex 1C of the WTO Agreement.  Article 16-07 Control of abusive or anti-competitive practices and conditions.  Provided that they are compatible with the provisions of this chapter, each Party may apply appropriate measures to prevent the abuse of intellectual property rights by their holders or the resort to practices that unreasonably limit trade or are detrimental to international transfers. of technology.  Article 16-08 Cooperation to eliminate trade in infringing goods.  The Parties will cooperate with each other in order to eliminate trade in goods that infringe intellectual property rights. To this end, they will establish information services in their administration and exchange information on trade in infringing goods.
Section B Copyright and Related Rights
Article 16-09 Protection of copyright and related rights.  1. Each Party shall protect the moral and property rights of the authors of the works included in Article 2 of the Berne Convention, including any others that incorporate an original expression in the sense that this Convention confers on this term, such as television programs. computing, or the compilations of data that for reasons of selection, compendium, arrangement or disposition of its content constitute creations of an intellectual nature.  2. The protection conferred on data compilations shall not extend to the data or materials themselves, nor shall it be granted to the detriment of any copyright that exists in such data or materials.  3. Each Party shall grant authors or their successors in title the rights set forth in the Berne Convention, with respect to the works referred to in paragraph 1, including the right to authorize or prohibit:
a) graphic editing;  b) translation into any language or dialect;  c) the adaptation and inclusion in phonograms, videograms, cinematographic films and other audiovisual works;  d) communication to the public;  e) reproduction by any means or in any form;  f) the first public distribution of the original and each copy of the work by sale, lease, loan or any other means;  g) the importation into the territory of a Party of copies of the work made without the authorization of the right holder; and  h) any form of use, process or system known or to be known.
4. At least with respect to computer programs, the Parties shall grant authors and their successors in title the right to authorize or prohibit commercial leasing to the public of originals or copies of their works protected by copyright. The authorization of the author or successor in title will not be necessary when the copy of the computer program does not constitute in itself the essential object of the lease.  5. Each Party shall provide that for copyright and related rights:
a) Any person who acquires or holds economic rights may, freely and separately, transfer them by contract for the purposes of exploitation and enjoyment by the assignee; and  b) any person who acquires and holds these economic rights by virtue of a contract, including employment contracts that imply the creation of any type of work and phonograms, has the capacity to exercise those rights in their own name and to fully enjoy benefits derived from such rights.
6. Each Party shall circumscribe the limitations or exceptions to the rights established in this article to determined special cases that do not impede the normal exploitation of the work, nor cause unreasonable prejudice to the legitimate interests of the right holder.  7. The protection granted by this article will extend during the life of the author. After his death, those who have legitimately acquired rights will enjoy them for a term of at least 50 years. When the duration of the protection of a work is calculated on a basis other than the life of a natural person, that duration will be:
a) not less than 50 years from the end of the calendar year of the publication or authorized disclosure of the work; or  b) in the absence of its publication or authorized disclosure, 50 years from the end of the year in which the work was carried out.
Article 16-10 Performers.
1. Each Party shall grant performers the right to authorize or prohibit:
a) the fixation of their unfixed performances and the reproduction of that fixation;  b) the communication to the public, the transmission and retransmission by wireless means of their interpretations or performances; and  c) any other form of use of their interpretations or performances.
2. Paragraph 1 shall not apply once a performer has consented to their performance being incorporated into a visual or audiovisual fixation.  3. The rights that have not been expressly transmitted will be understood as reserved in favor of the performing artist.  Article 16-11 Producers of phonograms.  1. Each Party shall grant the producer of a phonogram the right to authorize or prohibit:
a) the direct or indirect, total or partial reproduction of the phonogram;  b) the importation into the territory of a Party of copies of the phonogram made without the authorization of the producer; and  c) the first public distribution of the original and each copy of the phonogram by sale, lease or any other means.
2. Each Party shall confer upon producers of phonograms and all other holders of rights over phonograms as determined by its legislation, the right to authorize or prohibit commercial leasing to the public of originals or copies of protected phonograms.  Article 16-12 Broadcasting Organizations.  1. Each Party shall grant broadcasting organizations the right to authorize or prohibit:
a) the fixation and reproduction of the fixations of their broadcasts;  b) the retransmission and distribution by cable, fiber optics or any other means, as well as the communication to the public of their broadcasts; and  c) the reception of their broadcasts in relation to commercial activities.
2. Violations of rights mentioned in paragraph 1 will be cause for civil liability, jointly or not with criminal liability, in accordance with the legislation of each Party.  Article 16-13 Protection of encrypted satellite signals carrying programs.  Each Party shall establish as a cause of civil liability, jointly or not with criminal liability, in accordance with its legislation, the reception in connection with commercial activities, or the subsequent distribution of an encrypted satellite signal carrying programs, which has been received without authorization. from the legitimate signal distributor.  Article 16-14 Term of protection of related rights.  The duration of the protection granted under this chapter to performers and producers of phonograms may not be less than 50 years, counted from the end of the calendar year in which the fixation was made or the fixation took place. interpretation or performance. The duration of the protection granted to broadcasting organizations may not be less than 20 years, counted from the end of the calendar year in which the broadcast took place.  Article 16-15 Limitations or exceptions to related rights.  1. The protection provided for in this chapter with regard to performers, producers of phonograms and broadcasting organizations, will leave intact and will not affect in any way the protection of the moral and patrimonial rights of the authors of the literary or artistic works, nor may they be interpreted in detriment of that protection.  2. With regard to the rights conferred by Articles 16-10, 16-11 and 16-12, each Party may establish limitations or exceptions in the terms permitted by the Rome Convention.
Section C Trademarks
Article 16-16 Matter object of protection.  1. Any sign or combination of signs that make it possible to distinguish the goods or services of one person from those of another may constitute a trademark, since these are considered sufficiently distinctive or capable of identifying the products or services to which they are applied, compared to those of their same species or class. The marks will include the collective ones. Each Party may establish as a condition for the registration of a trademark, that the signs be visually perceptible.  2. The nature of the goods and services to which a trademark is applied will not be, in any case, an obstacle to its registration.  Article 16-17 Publication.  Pursuant to their legislation, the Parties shall publish each trademark before or soon after its registration, offering interested persons a reasonable opportunity to oppose or challenge its registration.  Article 16-18 Rights conferred.  The owner of a registered trademark shall have the exclusive right to prevent any third party, without his consent, from using in the course of business operations identical or similar signs for goods or services that are identical or similar to those for which the trademark has been registered. , when such use gives rise to the likelihood of confusion. In the event that an identical sign is used for identical goods or services, it will be presumed that there is a probability of confusion. The aforementioned rights will be granted without prejudice to previously existing rights and will not affect the possibility of the Parties to recognize rights based on use.  Article 16-19 Well-known marks.  1. The Parties, ex officio, if their legislation allows it, or at the request of the interested party, will refuse or invalidate the registration and will prohibit the use of a trademark for products or services that constitutes the reproduction, imitation or translation, likely to create confusion, of a trademark that the competent authority of the country of registration or use deems to be well known there and used for identical or similar products or services. The same will occur when the essential part of the mark constitutes the reproduction of such a well-known mark or an imitation liable to create confusion with it.  2. It shall be understood that a trademark is well-known when a determined sector of the public or commercial circles of the Party in which the reputation is claimed, knows the trademark as a consequence of the commercial or promotional activities carried out by a person who uses that trademark. brand in relation to its products or services. In order to demonstrate the notoriety of the brand, all the means of proof admitted in the Party in question may be used, including national and foreign ones.  3. The Parties will not register as a trademark those signs that are the same or similar to a well-known trademark that, to be applied to any product or service, their use could indicate a connection with the owner of the well-known trademark, or harm the interests of the owner. of the well-known mark.  4. A minimum period of five years must be granted, from the date of registration, to claim the cancellation of said trademark. The Parties have the power to provide a period in which the prohibition of use must be claimed.  5. No term will be set to claim the cancellation or prohibition of use of trademarks registered or used in bad faith.  Article 16-20 Exceptions.  Each Party may establish limited exceptions to the rights conferred by a trademark, such as the fair use of descriptive terms, provided that such exceptions take into account the legitimate interests of the trademark owner and third parties.  Article 16-21 Duration of protection.  The initial registration of a trademark will last 10 years from the date of filing the application or the date of its registration, according to the legislation of each Party, and may be renewed indefinitely for successive periods of 10 years, provided that the conditions for renewal are met.  Article 16-22 Use Requirement.  1. When a Party does not establish the requirement of use of a mark to maintain its registration, that Party shall establish such requirement in its legislation within a period of five years from the date of entry into force of this treaty. A trademark registration may be declared expired or canceled for non-use only after an uninterrupted period of non-use of at least three years has elapsed, unless the owner of the trademark demonstrates valid reasons supported by the existence of obstacles to use. Valid reasons for non-use will be recognized as circumstances arising, regardless of the will of the owner of the trademark, that constitute an obstacle to its use,  2. It will be understood that a trademark is in use when the goods or services that it distinguishes have been placed on the market or are available on the market, in the quantity and in the manner that normally corresponds, taking into account the nature of the goods or services and the modalities under which their commercialization is carried out.  3. For purposes of maintaining the use requirement, the use of a trademark by a person other than the owner of the same shall be recognized, when such use is subject to the control of the owner.  Article 16-23 Other requirements.  The use of a mark in the course of commercial operations with special requirements, such as, for example, use with another mark, use in a special way, or use in a way that impairs the ability to the mark to distinguish the goods or services of one company from those of other companies. This provision will not prevent the requirement that the name that identifies the company that produces the goods or services be used jointly but not linked to the brand that distinguishes the specific goods or services in question from that company.  Article 16-24 Licenses and assignment of trademarks.  Each Party may establish conditions for the licenses and assignment of trademarks. The owner of a registered trademark will have the right to assign it with or without the transfer of the company to which the trademark belongs. Compulsory licenses will not be allowed.
Section D Patents
Article 16-25 Patentable subject matter.  1. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3, patents shall be granted for inventions, whether of products or procedures, in all fields of technology, provided they are new, result from an inventive activity and are capable of of industrial application.  2. Subject to the provisions of paragraph 3, there shall be no discrimination in the granting of patents, nor in the enjoyment of the respective rights, depending on the field of technology, the territory of the Party in which the invention was made or whether the products were imported or produced locally.  3. Each Party may exclude from patentability inventions whose commercial exploitation in its territory must be prevented to protect public order or morality, including to protect human, animal or plant life or health, or to avoid serious damage to nature. or to the environment, provided that this exclusion is not made merely because the exploitation is prohibited by its legislation.  4. Likewise, each Party may exclude plants and animals from patentability, except for microorganisms and essentially biological processes for the production of plants or animals, which are not non-biological or microbiological processes. However, the Parties shall grant protection to all plant varieties through patents, an effective sui generis system, or a combination thereof. To the extent that it is compatible with its legislation, without this implying any adherence commitment, each Party will consider complying with the current substantive provisions of the International Convention for the Protection of New Varieties of Plants (UPOV).  Article 16-26 Rights conferred.  1. A patent will confer on its owner the following exclusive rights:
a) when the matter of the patent is a product, prevent third parties, without their consent, from carrying out acts of: manufacture, use, offer for sale, sale or import for the purposes of the product object of the patent; or  b) when the matter of the patent is a procedure, prevent third parties, without their consent, from carrying out the act of using the procedure and the acts of: use, offer for sale, sale or import for these purposes, of what less, the product obtained directly by means of said procedure.
2. Likewise, the patent holders shall have the right to assign or transfer the patent by any means and to conclude license contracts.  Article 16-27 Conditions imposed on patent applicants.  1. Each Party shall require the applicant for a patent to disclose the invention in a sufficiently clear and complete manner, so that persons skilled in the art in question can carry out the invention. In addition, each Party may require that the applicant indicate the best way of carrying out the invention known to the inventor on the date of filing of the application or, if priority is claimed, on the priority date claimed in the application. .  2. Each Party may require the applicant for a patent to provide information regarding its applications, and the corresponding grants of patents abroad.  Article 16-28 Exceptions.  Each Party may provide limited exceptions to the exclusive rights conferred by a patent, provided that such exceptions do not unreasonably conflict with a normal exploitation of the patent, nor unreasonably prejudice the legitimate interests of the patent holder, taking into account the legitimate interests of third parties.  Article 16-29 Other uses without authorization of the right holder.  When the legislation of a Party allows other uses of the subject matter of a patent, other than those permitted in accordance with the previous article, without the authorization of the right holder, including use by the government or by third parties authorized by the government, the following provisions:
a) the authorization of those uses will be considered depending on the matter in question;  b) These uses may only be allowed when, before making them, the potential user has tried to obtain authorization from the rights holder under reasonable commercial terms and conditions and these attempts have not been effective within a reasonable period of time. The Parties may exempt from this obligation in case of national emergency or in other circumstances of extreme urgency, or in cases of non-commercial public use. However, in situations of national emergency or other circumstances of extreme urgency, the rights holder will be notified as soon as reasonably possible. In the case of non-commercial public use, where the government or contractor, without doing a patent search, knows or has demonstrable reason to know that a valid patent is or will be used by or for the government,  c) the scope and duration of these uses will be limited to the purposes for which it has been authorized;  d) those uses will not be exclusive;  e) these uses may not be assigned, except together with the part of the company that enjoys those uses;  f) these uses will be authorized mainly to supply the internal market of the Party that authorizes them;  g) the authorization of those uses may be withdrawn subject to the adequate protection of the legitimate interests of the persons who have received authorization for those uses, if the circumstances that gave rise to it have disappeared and are not likely to arise again. The competent authorities will be empowered to examine, upon well-founded request, whether said circumstances continue to exist;  h) the holder of the right will be paid an adequate remuneration according to the circumstances of each case, taking into account the economic value of the authorization;  i) the legal validity of any resolution regarding the authorization of those uses, will be subject to judicial review or to an independent review by a different superior authority;  j) any resolution regarding the remuneration granted for those uses will be subject to judicial review or an independent review by a different authority;  k) The Parties shall not be obliged to apply the conditions established in subparagraphs b) and f), when such uses have been allowed to remedy practices that, as a result of a judicial or administrative process, have been determined to be anticompetitive. The need to correct anti-competitive practices may be taken into account when determining the amount of remuneration in such cases. The competent authorities will have the power to deny the revocation of the authorization, if it is probable that the conditions that gave rise to that authorization will be repeated; Y  l) when these uses have been authorized to allow the exploitation of a patent (second patent), which cannot be exploited without infringing another patent (first patent), the following additional conditions must be observed:
