i) the invention claimed in the second patent must represent an important technical advance of considerable economic relevance with respect to the invention claimed in the first patent;  ii) the holder of the first patent shall be entitled to a cross license, under reasonable conditions, to exploit the invention claimed in the second patent; and  iii) the authorized use of the first patent may not be assigned without the assignment of the second patent.
Article 16-30 Revocation or cancellation.  The possibility of judicial review of any decision to revoke or cancel a patent will be provided. Each Party may revoke or cancel a patent only when there are reasons that would have justified the refusal to grant it.  Article 16-31 Evidence in cases of infringement of patented processes.  1. When the matter of a patent is a procedure to obtain an identical product, the judicial authorities shall be empowered to order the defendant to prove that the procedure to obtain a product is different from the patented procedure. Accordingly, each Party shall provide that, in any infringement proceeding, the respondent bears the burden of proving that the allegedly infringing product was made by a process other than the patented one, at least in the following cases:
a) if the product obtained by the patented procedure is new; or  b) if there is a substantial probability that the identical product was manufactured by the process, and the patentee cannot establish through reasonable efforts which process was actually used.
2. The Parties will be free to establish that the burden of proof indicated in paragraph 1 will correspond to the alleged infringer only if the condition set forth in subparagraph a) is met or only if the condition set forth in subparagraph b) is met.  3. In the presentation of evidence to the contrary, the legitimate interests of the defendants in terms of the protection of their industrial and commercial secrets will be taken into account.  Article 16-32 Duration of protection.  The protection conferred by a patent will not expire before a period of 20 years has elapsed, counted from the filing date of the application.
Section E Utility models
Article 16-33 Protection of utility models.  Each Party shall protect utility models in accordance with its legislation.
Section F Industrial Designs
Article 16-34 Conditions and duration of protection.  1. Each Party shall grant protection to new or original industrial designs that are independently created. Each Party may establish that designs are not considered new or original if they do not differ significantly from known designs or from combinations of characteristics of known designs. Each Party may establish that this protection does not extend to designs based essentially on functional or technical considerations.  2. Each Party shall ensure that the requirements for obtaining industrial design protection, particularly with regard to any cost, examination or publication, do not unreasonably impair a person's opportunity to apply for and obtain such protection. The Parties shall be free to fulfill this obligation through industrial design legislation or through copyright legislation.  3. Each Party shall grant a protection period for industrial designs of at least 10 years from the date of filing of the application.  Article 16-35 Rights conferred.  1. The owner of a protected industrial design shall have the right to prevent third parties without their consent from manufacturing, selling or importing items that display or incorporate a protected design or fundamentally a copy of it, when these acts are carried out for commercial purposes.  2. The Parties may establish limited exceptions to the protection of industrial designs, provided that such exceptions do not unreasonably violate the normal exploitation of protected industrial designs, nor do they cause unreasonable prejudice to the legitimate interests of the owner of the protected design. , taking into account the legitimate interests of third parties.
Section G Undisclosed Information
Article 16-36 Protection of undisclosed information.  1. In ensuring effective protection against unfair competition, the Parties shall protect undisclosed information in accordance with paragraph 2, and data that has been submitted to governments or official bodies, in accordance with article 16-37.  2 Individuals and legal entities will have the possibility to prevent information that is legitimately under their control from being disclosed to third parties, or being acquired or used by third parties without their consent, contrary to honest commercial uses, to the extent that that said information:
a) is secret, in the sense that, as a whole or in the precise configuration and composition of its elements, it is not generally known or easily accessible to the people who are members of the circles that normally handle the type of information in question ;  b) the information has a commercial value because it is secret; and  c) in the given circumstances, has been subject to reasonable measures to keep it secret by the person who legally has control over it.
3. To grant protection, each Party may require that a trade secret be recorded in documents, electronic or magnetic media, optical discs, microfilms, films or other similar instruments.  4. No Party may limit the duration of protection for trade or trade secrets, as long as the conditions described in paragraph 2 exist.  5. No Party may discourage or prevent the voluntary licensing of trade or trade secrets by imposing excessive or discriminatory conditions on such licenses, or conditions that dilute the value of industrial or commercial secrets.  Article 16-37 Data protection of pharmaceutical or agrochemical goods.  Each Party, where it requires, as a condition of approving the marketing of pharmaceutical goods or agricultural chemical goods that use new chemical constituents, the submission of undisclosed test or other data that requires considerable effort to produce, shall protect such data from any commercial use. unfair.  In addition, each Party shall protect such data from disclosure, except as necessary to protect the public or unless measures are taken to ensure the protection of the data from unfair commercial use.
Section H Geographical indications and appellations of origin
Article 16-38 Protection of geographical indications and appellations of origin.  1. Each Party shall protect geographical indications and appellations of origin, in the terms of its legislation.  2. In relation to geographical indications and appellations of origin, each Party shall establish the legal means so that interested persons can prevent:
a) the use of any means that, in the designation or presentation of the product, indicates or suggests that the product in question comes from a territory, region or locality other than the true place of origin, so as to mislead the public as to the geographical origin of the product; and  b) any other use that constitutes an act of unfair competition, within the meaning of Article 10 bis of the Paris Convention. 
3. The Parties, ex officio, if their legislation allows it, or at the request of an interested party, will deny or invalidate the registration of a trademark that contains or consists of a geographical indication or appellation of origin with respect to non-originating goods from the indicated territory, if the use of such an indication in the mark for those goods in that Party is of such a nature as to mislead the public as to the true place of origin.  4. Paragraphs 2 and 3 shall apply to any geographical indication or appellation of origin which, while correctly indicating the territory, region or locality in which the goods originate, gives the public a false idea that the goods originate from another territory, region or locality.  5. In relation to geographical indications and appellations of origin, each Party shall establish the means to prevent the importation, manufacture or sale of a good that uses a geographical indication or appellation of origin protected in another Party, unless it has been produced and certified in that Party, in accordance with the laws, rules and regulations applicable to that good.
Section I Enforcement of Intellectual Property Rights
Article 16-39 General obligations.  1. Each Party shall ensure that its legislation establishes procedures for the enforcement of intellectual property rights, in accordance with the provisions of this section that allow the adoption of effective measures against any action infringing the intellectual property rights referred to. this chapter, including expeditious remedies to prevent infringements and remedies that are an effective means of deterring new infringements. These procedures will be applied in such a way as to avoid the creation of obstacles to legitimate trade, and will provide safeguards against their abuse.  2. Procedures relating to the enforcement of intellectual property rights shall be fair and equitable. Likewise, these procedures will not be unnecessarily complicated or burdensome, nor will they entail unjustified deadlines or undue delays.  3. Decisions on the merits of a case will be formulated in writing and will be reasoned. They shall be made available at least to the parties to the proceedings, without undue delay. They will only be based on evidence about which those parties have been given an opportunity to be heard.  4. The parties to the proceeding will be given the opportunity for a review by a judicial authority of the final administrative decisions and, subject to the jurisdictional provisions provided for in their legislation regarding the importance of a case, of at least minus the legal aspects of all first instance judicial decisions on the merits of the case. However, it will not be mandatory to give them the opportunity to review the acquittals issued in criminal cases.  5. It is understood that this section does not impose any obligation to establish a judicial system for the enforcement of intellectual property rights different from the one already existing for the application of the legislation in general, nor does it affect the ability of the Parties to enforce their rights. laws in general. Nothing in this section creates any obligation with respect to the allocation of resources between IP enforcement and general law enforcement.  Article 16-40 Fair and equitable procedures.  Each Party shall make available to rights holders the civil judicial procedures to obtain the observance of all intellectual property rights referred to in this chapter. Defendants shall have the right to receive timely written notice with sufficient detail, including the basis for the claim. Parties will be authorized to be represented by independent counsel and the proceedings will not impose unreasonably onerous requirements for mandatory personal appearances. All parties to these proceedings will be duly empowered to substantiate their allegations and present all relevant evidence. The procedure must provide means to identify and protect confidential information,  Article 16-41 Evidence.  1. The judicial authorities will be empowered to order that, when a party to the procedure has presented the evidence that it reasonably has and that is sufficient to support its allegations, and has identified any pertinent evidence to substantiate its allegations that is under the control of the opposing party provides said evidence, subject, where appropriate, to conditions that guarantee the protection of confidential information.  2. Where a party to the proceeding voluntarily and unreasonably denies access to necessary information, or otherwise fails to provide such information within a reasonable time, or materially impedes a proceeding relating to an enforcement action, the Parties may authorize the judicial authorities to formulate preliminary and final determinations, affirmative or negative, based on the information that has been presented to them, including the claim or allegation presented by the party unfavorably affected by the denial of access to information, provided that the parties are given an opportunity to be heard regarding the allegations or evidence.  Article 16-42 Court orders.  1. The judicial authorities shall have the power to order a party to the proceedings to desist from the alleged infringement, among other things to prevent imported goods that infringe an intellectual property right from entering the commercial circuits of their jurisdiction, immediately after the their customs clearance. The Parties are not required to grant such power in relation to a protected matter that has been acquired or requested by a person before knowing or having reasonable grounds to know that operating with such matter would entail infringement of an intellectual property right.  2. Notwithstanding the other provisions of this section, and subject to compliance with the provisions of this chapter that specifically refer to use by the government or by third parties authorized by the government, without the consent of the rights holder, the Parties may limit the resources available against such use to the payment of compensation, in accordance with the provisions of literal h) of article 16-29. In all other cases, the remedies provided for in this section will be applied or, when these are incompatible with the legislation, declaratory judgments and adequate compensation may be obtained.  Article 16-43 Damages.  1. The judicial authorities will be empowered to order the infringer to pay the right holder adequate compensation to compensate for the damage that the right holder has suffered due to an infringement of his intellectual property right, when the infringer has been sentenced in the corresponding judicial process. .  2. Likewise, the judicial authorities will be empowered to order the infringer to pay the expenses of the holder of the right, which may include the fees of the lawyers that are appropriate. When appropriate, the Parties may authorize the judicial authorities to grant reparation for previously recognized benefits or damages, even when the infringer did not know or did not have reasonable grounds to know that he was carrying out an infringing activity.  Article 16-44 Other resources.  1. In order to establish an effective means of dissuading infringements, the judicial authorities will be empowered to order that the goods that have been determined to be infringing be, without any compensation, separated from the commercial circuits in such a way as to avoid causing damage to the owner. of law, or that they be destroyed, provided that this is not incompatible with current constitutional provisions.  2. The judicial authorities will also be empowered to order that the materials and instruments that have been used predominantly for the production of the infringing goods, be, without any compensation, separated from the commercial circuits so as to minimize the risks of new infractions. Both the need for a proportion between the seriousness of the infringement and the measures ordered and the interests of third parties will be taken into account when processing the corresponding requests.  3. Regarding counterfeit goods, the mere removal of the illegally adhered mark will not be enough to allow their release into commercial circuits, except in exceptional cases established by the legislation of each Party, such as those in which the authority orders its donation to charitable institutions.  Article 16-45 Right to information.  Except where it is disproportionate to the seriousness of the infringement, each Party may provide that judicial authorities may order the infringer to inform the right holder of the identity of third parties who have participated in the production and distribution of the infringing goods or services, and on their distribution circuits.  Article 16-46 Compensation to the defendant.  1. The judicial authorities shall have the power to order a party to the proceedings, at whose request measures have been taken and who has abused the enforcement procedure, to adequately indemnify the party on whom an obligation or restriction has been unduly imposed, for the damage suffered as a result of such abuse. In addition, the judicial authorities will have the power to order the plaintiff to pay the defendant's expenses, which may include attorneys' fees.  2. In connection with the administration of any laws relating to the protection or enforcement of intellectual property rights, each Party shall exempt both the authorities and their officials from the responsibilities that the appropriate corrective measures give rise to, only in the case of actions carried out or planned in good faith for the administration of said laws.  Article 16-47 Administrative procedures.  To the extent that civil remedies may be brought as a result of administrative proceedings relating to the merits of a case, such proceedings shall follow principles substantially equivalent to those set forth in this section.  Article 16-48 Precautionary measures.  1. The judicial authorities will be empowered to order the adoption of fast and effective precautionary measures aimed at:
a) prevent the infringement of any intellectual property right and, in particular, prevent counterfeit goods from entering the commercial circuits of their jurisdiction, including imported goods, immediately after customs clearance; and  b) preserve the pertinent evidence related to the alleged infringement.
2. The judicial authorities shall be empowered to adopt precautionary measures, when appropriate, without having heard the other party to the proceedings, particularly when there is a probability that any delay will cause irreparable damage to the rights holder, or when there is a verifiable risk of destruction of evidence.  3. The judicial authorities shall be empowered to require the plaintiff to present the evidence reasonably available, in order to establish to their satisfaction with a sufficient degree of certainty that the plaintiff is the owner of the right and that their right is subject to or will be be imminently infringed, and to order the plaintiff to post a bond or equivalent guarantee that is sufficient to protect the defendant and prevent abuse.  4. When precautionary measures have been adopted without having heard the other party in the procedure, these shall be notified without delay to the affected party, no later than immediately after applying them. At the request of the defendant, within a reasonable period of time from that notification, a review will be carried out in which the right to be heard will be recognized, in order to decide whether these measures should be modified, revoked or confirmed.  5. The authority in charge of the execution of the precautionary measures may require the plaintiff to present any additional information necessary for the identification of the goods in question.  6. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraph 4, precautionary measures taken under paragraphs 1 and 2 shall be revoked or otherwise rendered null and void, at the request of the respondent, if the proceedings leading to a decision on the merits of the case The matter does not start within a reasonable period of time, which must be established when national legislation allows it, by determination of the judicial authority that ordered the measures, and which, in the absence of such determination, will not exceed 20 business days or 31 days, if this period were longer.  7. In the cases in which the precautionary measures are revoked or expire by action or omission of the plaintiff, or in those cases in which it is subsequently determined that there was no infringement or threat of infringement of an intellectual property right, the judicial authorities will be empowered to order the plaintiff, upon the defendant's request, to give the defendant adequate compensation for any damage caused by those measures.  8. To the extent that precautionary measures may be ordered as a result of administrative proceedings, those proceedings shall conform to principles substantially equivalent to those set forth in this section.  Article 16-49 Suspension of customs clearance by customs authorities.  Each part:
a) adopt procedures so that the holder of a right, who has valid reasons to suspect that the importation of counterfeit trademark goods or pirated goods that infringe copyright is being prepared, can submit to the competent authorities, a written demand with object that the customs authorities suspend the dispatch of those goods for free circulation, in accordance with articles 16-50 to 16-58;  b) may authorize such a claim to be made with respect to goods that involve other infringements of intellectual property rights, provided that the requirements of this section are met; Y  c) may establish analogous procedures for the customs authorities to suspend the clearance of those goods intended for export from its territory.
Article 16-50 Demand.  Any right holder initiating a proceeding under Article 16-49 will be required to submit sufficient evidence to the satisfaction of the competent authorities that, under the law of the importing country, there is a presumption of infringement of your intellectual property right and provide a sufficiently detailed description of the goods so that they can be easily recognized by customs authorities. The competent authorities will notify the claimant, within a reasonable time, if they have accepted the claim and, when they are the ones who establish it, the term of action of the customs authorities.  Article 16-51 Deposit or equivalent guarantee.
1. The competent authorities shall be empowered to require the plaintiff to provide a bond or equivalent guarantee, which is sufficient to protect the defendant and the competent authorities and prevent abuse. Such a bond or equivalent guarantee shall not unduly discourage recourse to these procedures.
prior deposit of a deposit for an amount that is sufficient to protect the owner of the right in any case of infringement. Payment of said bond shall be understood without prejudice to any other recourse available to the holder of the right. Likewise, it will be understood that the deposit will be returned if the holder does not exercise his right of action within a reasonable period of time.
Article 16-52 Notice of suspension.
The importer and the claimant will be promptly notified of the suspension of customs clearance of the goods, in accordance with article 16-49. Article 16-53 Duration of suspension.
In the event that, within a period not exceeding 10 business days from the notification of the suspension to the plaintiff, the customs authorities have not been informed that a party to the proceeding other than the defendant has initiated the proceeding leading to a decision on the merits of the matter or that the authority duly empowered for this purpose has adopted precautionary measures that prolong the suspension of the customs clearance of the goods, they will be released if all the other required conditions have been met. for import or export; in the cases in which it proceeds, the aforementioned period may be extended for another 10 business days. If the procedure leading to a decision on the merits of the matter has been initiated, at the request of the defendant, a review, including the right of the latter to be heard, shall be carried out within a reasonable period of time in order to decide whether those measures should be modified, revoked or confirmed. However, when the suspension of customs clearance is carried out or continued by virtue of a precautionary judicial measure, the provisions of paragraph 6 of article 16-48 shall apply.
Article 16-53 Duration of suspension.
In the event that, within a period not exceeding 10 business days from the notification of the suspension to the plaintiff, the customs authorities have not been informed that a party to the proceeding other than the defendant has initiated the proceeding leading to a decision on the merits of the matter or that the authority duly empowered for this purpose has adopted precautionary measures that prolong the suspension of the customs clearance of the goods, they will be released if all the other required conditions have been met. for import or export; in the cases in which it proceeds, the aforementioned period may be extended for another 10 business days. If the procedure leading to a decision on the merits of the matter has been initiated, at the request of the defendant, a review, including the right of the latter to be heard, shall be carried out within a reasonable period of time in order to decide whether those measures should be modified, revoked or confirmed. However, when the suspension of customs clearance is carried out or continued by virtue of a precautionary judicial measure, the provisions of paragraph 6 of article 16-48 shall apply.
Article 16-54 Compensation to the importer and the owner of the goods.
The relevant authorities shall have the power to order the plaintiff to pay the importer, the consignee and the owner of the goods adequate compensation for any damage to them caused by the unfounded retention of the goods or by the detention of those that have been dispatched in accordance with with the provisions of article 16-53.
Article 16-55 Right of inspection and information.
Without prejudice to the protection of confidential information, the Parties shall empower the competent authorities to give the right holder sufficient opportunities to have any goods detained by the customs authorities inspected, in order to substantiate their claims. Likewise, the competent authorities will be empowered to give the importer equivalent opportunities to have those goods inspected. When a positive decision on the merits of the matter has been adopted, the Parties may authorize the competent authorities to communicate to the right holder the name and address of the consignor, the importer and the consignee, as well as the quantity of the goods that be concerned.
Article 16-56 Action ex officio.
When the parties to the procedure request the competent authorities to act ex officio and suspend the dispatch of those goods with respect to which they have the presumption that they infringe an intellectual property right:
a) the competent authorities may request, at any time, the holder of the right any information that may be useful to exercise that power;
b) The suspension must be promptly notified to the importer and the right holder. If the importer appeals against it before the competent authorities, the suspension will be subject, mutatis mutandis, to the conditions stipulated in article 16-53; Y
c) The Parties will exempt both the authorities and their officials from the responsibilities that the appropriate precautionary measures give rise to, only in the case of actions carried out or planned in good faith.
Article 16-57 Appeals.
Without prejudice to the other actions that correspond to the holder of the right and subject to the defendant's right to appeal before a judicial authority, the competent authorities will be empowered to order the destruction or removal of the infringing property, in accordance with the principles established in article 16-44. As for counterfeit goods, the authorities will not allow them to be re-exported in the same state, except in exceptional circumstances, nor will they submit them to a different customs procedure.
Article 16-58 Negligible imports.
Each Party may exclude from the application of articles 16-49 to 16-57, small amounts of goods that are not of a commercial nature and are part of the personal baggage of travelers or are sent in small consignments.
Article 16-59 Criminal proceedings.
1. Each Party shall establish criminal procedures and sanctions, at least for cases of willful counterfeiting of trademarks or piracy infringing copyright on a commercial scale, which shall include imprisonment or the imposition of monetary sanctions, sufficiently dissuasive, that are consistent with the level of sanctions applied for crimes of comparable gravity.
2. Where appropriate, available sanctions will also include confiscation, forfeiture and destruction of infringing property and all materials and accessories predominantly used in the commission of the offence. When considering the issuance of such orders, the judicial authorities shall take into account the need for proportionality between the seriousness of the infringement and the measures ordered, as well as the interests of other persons including those of the right holder.
3. Regarding counterfeit goods, the mere removal of the illegally affixed mark will not be sufficient to allow the release of the goods into commercial circuits, except in exceptional cases established by the legislation of each Party, such as those in which the authority arranges your donation to charitable institutions.
Each Party may provide for the application of criminal procedures and sanctions in other cases of infringement of intellectual property rights, in particular when committed with intent and on a commercial scale.
Chapter XVII TRANSPARENCY
Article 17-01 Information Center.
1. Each Party shall designate a unit or office as an information center to facilitate communication between the Parties on any matter covered by this Agreement.
2. When requested by a Party, the information center of another Party shall indicate the agency or official responsible for the matter and shall provide the support required to facilitate communication with the requesting Party.
Article 17-02 Publication.
Each Party shall ensure that its laws, regulations, procedures and administrative resolutions of general application, which refer to any matter included in this Agreement, are published as soon as possible or made available for the knowledge of the Parties and any interested party.
Article 17-03 Notification and provision of information.
1. Each Party shall, to the extent possible, notify the other Parties of any current or proposed measure that the Party considers could affect or substantially affect the interests of the other Parties under the terms of this Agreement. Said notification will be made without prejudging whether or not the measure is compatible with it.
2. Each Party, at the request of another Party, shall provide information and prompt responses to its questions regarding any current or proposed measure.
Article 17-04 Hearing, legality and due process guarantees.
1. The Parties reaffirm the guarantees of hearing, legality and due process contemplated in their respective legislation.
2. Each Party shall maintain judicial or administrative procedures for the review and, when appropriate, the correction of the final acts related to this agreement.
3. Each Party shall ensure that in the judicial and administrative procedures related to any measure that affects the application of this Agreement, the essential formalities of the procedure are observed and the legal cause of the same is founded and motivated.
Chapter XVIII ADMINISTRATION OF THE TREATY
Article 18-01 Administrative Commission.  1. The Parties establish the Administrative Commission, which will be made up of the officials referred to in Annex 18-01(1) or by the persons designated by them.  2. The Commission will have the following functions:
a) ensure compliance and correct application of the provisions of the treaty;  b) evaluate the results achieved in the application of the treaty, monitor its development and recommend to the Parties the modifications it deems appropriate;  c) propose measures aimed at the correct administration and development of the treaty and its annexes;  d) contribute to the solution of controversies that arise regarding its interpretation and application;  e) recommend to the Parties the adoption of the necessary measures to implement their decisions;  f) set the amounts of remuneration and expenses to be paid to the arbitrators, their assistants and the experts, which shall be covered in equal parts by the disputing Parties; Y  g) hear about any other matter that could affect the operation of this treaty, or that is entrusted to it by the Parties.
3. The Commission may:
a) establish ad hoc or permanent committees, working groups and groups of experts, as well as assign powers to them;  b) request the advice of persons or institutions without governmental ties; and  c) adopt any other action for the exercise of its functions.
4. The Commission will establish its rules and procedures and all its decisions will be made by consensus.  5. The Commission shall meet at least once a year in ordinary session and, at the request of any Party, in extraordinary session. The ordinary sessions will be chaired successively by each Party.  Article 18-02 Administrative Subcommittee.  1. The Parties establish the Administrative Subcommittee, which will be made up of the officials referred to in Annex 18-02(1) or by the persons they designate.  2. The Subcommittee will have the following functions:
a) supervise the work of all committees, subcommittees and working groups established under this Agreement and included in Annex 18-02(2);  b) follow up on the decisions and agreements reached by the Commission;  c) prepare and review the technical files necessary for making decisions and agreements within the framework of the treaty;  d) act as technical secretariat in the meetings of the Commission;  e) Designate the information center for each Party, in accordance with Article 17-01; Y
f) hear about any other matter that could affect the operation of the treaty, which is entrusted to it by the Commission.
3. The Subcommittee will meet at least twice a year, alternating the venue between the Parties.  4. The Subcommittee will present an annual work report to the Commission.  Article 18-03 Secretariat  1. The Commission shall establish and supervise a Secretariat made up of national sections.  2. Each Party:
a) establish the permanent office of its national section;  b) will be in charge of:
i) the operation and costs of its section, and  ii) the remuneration and expenses that must be paid to the arbitrators, their assistants and experts appointed in accordance with the chapter;
c) appoint the Secretary of its national section, who will be the official responsible for its administration; and  d) notify the Commission of the address of its national section.
3. The Secretariat will have the following functions:
a) provide assistance to the Commission and the Sub-Commission;  b) provide administrative support to the arbitral tribunals created pursuant to Chapter XIX;  c) on the instructions of the Commission, support the work of the committees, subcommittees and groups of experts established in accordance with this treaty; and  d) the others entrusted to it by the Commission.
Annex 18-01 Officials of the Administrative Commission
The officials that make up the Commission will be:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Minister of Economy or his successor;  b) in the case of Guatemala: the Minister of Economy or his successor;  c) in the case of Honduras: the Secretary of State in the Offices of Industry and Commerce, or his successor; and  d) in the case of Mexico: the Secretary of Commerce and Industrial Development, or his successor.
Annex 18-02 (1) Officials of the Administrative Subcommittee
 
The officials that make up the Subcommittee will be:
a) in the case of El Salvador: the Vice Minister of Economy, or his successor;  b) in the case of Guatemala: the Vice Minister of Economy in Charge of Integration Affairs, or his successor;  c) in the case of Honduras: the Undersecretary of Economic Integration and Foreign Trade, or his successor; and  d) in the case of Mexico: the Head of the Negotiations Office for Latin America, Market Access and the FTAA, or his successor.
Annex 18-02(2) Committees and Subcommittees
Committee on Trade in Goods (article 3-18)  Committee on Agricultural Trade (article 4-10)  Committee on Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures (article 5-10)  Committee on Regional Integration of Inputs (article 6-19)
Origin Committee (article 7-12)  Committee on Cross-Border Trade in Services and Investment (article 10-10)  Professional Services Committee (annex on professional services)  Financial Services Committee (article 11-11)  Committee on Temporary Entry of Persons of Business (article 13-06)
Committee on Measures Related to Standardization (article 15-14)
Subcommittee on Labeling, Packaging and Packaging (article 15-15)
Approval Procedures Subcommittee (article 15-16)
Subcommittee on Measures Related to the Standardization of Telecommunications (article 15-17)
Chapter XIX SETTLEMENT OF DISPUTES
Article 19-01 Cooperation.  The Parties shall always endeavor to reach agreement on the interpretation and application of this Agreement through cooperation and consultation, and shall endeavor to reach a mutually satisfactory solution to any matter that might affect its operation.  Article 19-02 Scope of application.  Except as otherwise provided in this agreement, the procedure of this chapter shall apply:
a) to the prevention or settlement of all disputes between the Parties relating to the application or interpretation of this treaty; or  b) when a Party considers that an existing or proposed measure of another Party is or could be inconsistent with the obligations of this agreement or could cause nullification or impairment within the meaning of Annex 19-02.
Article 19-03 Settlement of disputes under the WTO Agreement.  1. Controversies that arise in relation to the provisions of this treaty and the WTO Agreement or the agreements negotiated in accordance with the latter, may be resolved in one or another forum, at the choice of the complaining Party.  2. Once a dispute settlement procedure has been initiated pursuant to Article 19-06, or one pursuant to Article 6 of the Understanding Concerning Rules and Procedures Governing Dispute Settlement that is part of the of the WTO Agreement, the selected forum will be exclusive of any other.  Article 19-04 Perishable goods.  In controversies relating to perishable goods, the terms established in this chapter will be reduced by half, without prejudice to the fact that the disputing Parties by mutual agreement decide to reduce them even more.  Article 19-05 Consultations.  1. Any Party may request, in writing, consultations with the other Party or Parties regarding any measure adopted or planned, or any other matter that it considers could affect the operation of this Agreement under the terms of Article 19-02.  2. The requesting Party, through its national section of the Secretariat, will deliver a copy of the request to the other Parties.  3. Unless otherwise provided by the Commission, a third Party may participate in the consultations, upon written notification through its national section of the Secretariat to the other Parties.  4. The consulting Parties:
a) they will examine with due diligence the queries made to them;  b) provide the information that allows examining the way in which the adopted or projected measure could affect the operation of this treaty;  c) treat confidential information exchanged during consultations in the same manner as the Party that provided it; and  d) will endeavor to avoid any solution that adversely affects the interests of any other Party under this treaty.
Article 19-06 Intervention of the Commission, good offices, conciliation and mediation.  1. Any consulting Party may request in writing, through its national section of the Secretariat, that the Commission meet whenever a matter is not resolved in accordance with Article 19-05 within 30 days of delivery of the consultation request.  2. A Party may also request in writing, through its national section of the Secretariat, that the Commission meet when technical consultations have been held in accordance with the provisions of Articles 5-13 and 15-18.  3. The requesting Party shall mention in the request the measure that is the subject of the complaint, indicate the provisions of this treaty that it considers applicable, and submit the request, through its national section of the Secretariat, to the other Parties.  4. The Commission will meet within the 10 days following the presentation of the request and in order to achieve a mutually satisfactory solution to the dispute, it may:
a) convene technical advisers or create the working or expert groups that it deems necessary;  b) resort to good offices, conciliation, mediation or other alternative means for dispute resolution; or  c) make recommendations.
5. Unless it decides otherwise, the Commission may combine two or more proceedings that it hears under this article, relating to the same measure. Likewise, it may accumulate two procedures referring to other matters that it knows in accordance with this article, when it deems appropriate to examine them jointly.  Article 19-07 Request for the establishment of the arbitral tribunal.  1. Any consulting Party may request in writing the establishment of an arbitral tribunal when the matter has not been resolved within:
a) 30 days after the meeting of the Commission in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 4 of article 19-06 or, if it has not been held, within 30 days after the request for a meeting of the Commission; or  b) the 30 days following the Commission's meeting to address the most recent matter submitted to its consideration, when several procedures have been accumulated pursuant to paragraph 5 of Article 19-06.
2. The requesting Party shall deliver the request, through its national section of the Secretariat, to the other Parties. Upon submission of the request, the Commission will establish an arbitral tribunal.  3. A third Party shall be entitled to participate as a complaining Party, by delivering its intent, through its national section of the Secretariat, to the disputing Parties. The notification shall be delivered no later than seven days after the date on which a Party has submitted the request for the establishment of the arbitral tribunal.  4. If a third Party decides not to intervene as a complaining Party in accordance with paragraph 3, it shall thereafter refrain from bringing in respect of the same matter, in the absence of a significant change in economic or commercial circumstances:
a) a dispute resolution procedure in accordance with this chapter; or  b) a dispute settlement procedure in accordance with the Understanding on Rules and Procedures Governing Dispute Settlement, which forms part of the WTO Agreement, invoking grounds substantially equivalent to those that said Party could invoke. in accordance with this treaty.
5. Unless otherwise agreed between the disputing Parties, the arbitral tribunal will be integrated and will perform its functions in accordance with the provisions of this chapter.  Article 19-08 List and qualifications of the arbitrators.  1. Upon the entry into force of this agreement, each Party shall designate 10 arbitrators to integrate the "List of arbitrators from Mexico and El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras". Likewise, the Parties, by mutual agreement, will designate five arbitrators from non-Party countries to integrate the "List of arbitrators from non-Party countries".  2. The members of the lists:
a) have specialized knowledge or experience in law, international trade, other matters related to this agreement, or in the settlement of disputes arising from international trade agreements;  b) they will be elected strictly based on their objectivity, reliability and good judgment;  c) they will be independent, will not be linked to the Parties and will not receive instructions from them; and  d) they will comply with the Code of Conduct established in annex 19-08.
3. The persons who have intervened in a controversy, in the terms of paragraph 4 of article 19-06, may not be arbitrators for the same controversy.  Article 19-09 Integration of the arbitral tribunal.  1. The arbitral tribunal will be made up as follows:
a) within 10 days following the request for the integration of an arbitral tribunal, in accordance with article 19-07, each Party shall designate an arbitrator from the "List of arbitrators from Mexico and El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras";  b) by mutual agreement, the Parties will appoint the third arbitrator from the "List of arbitrators from non-Party countries", within 10 days from the date on which the last of the two arbitrators mentioned in subparagraph a was appointed. ). The third arbitrator will preside over the arbitral tribunal;  c) If a Party has not designated its arbitrator within the 10-day period established in subparagraph a), such designation shall be made by lot between the Parties, at the request of the other Party, from among the arbitrators that make up the "List of arbitrators from Mexico and El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras", who are nationals of the Party that has not appointed its arbitrator;  d) likewise, if within the 10 days following the term established in literal b) there is no agreement between the Parties to designate the third arbitrator, any Party may designate it from the "List of arbitrators from non-Party countries" ; and  e) by mutual agreement, the Parties may designate an arbitrator who is not on the lists referred to in article 19-08.
2. In the event that a disputing Party is made up of two or more Parties, one of them, elected by mutual agreement, shall assume the representation of the others regarding the procedure established in paragraph 1.  Article 19-10 Model Rules of Procedure.  1. Unless otherwise agreed between the disputing Parties, the procedure before the arbitral tribunal shall be governed by the Model Rules of Procedure, contained in annex 19-10.  2. The Commission may modify the Model Rules of Procedure.  3. Unless the Parties agree otherwise, the mandate of the arbitral tribunal shall be: "Examine, in light of the applicable provisions of the treaty, the controversy submitted to its consideration in the terms of the request for the meeting of the Commission, and issue the preliminary report and the final report referred to in articles 19-13 and 19-14".  4. If the complaining Party alleges that a matter has been the cause of nullification or impairment within the meaning of Annex 19-02, the mandate shall so indicate.  5. When a disputing Party requests that the arbitral tribunal formulate conclusions on the degree of adverse commercial effects that the measure that XIX - 7 has been deemed to be incompatible with this treaty or has caused nullification or impairment in the sense of annex XIX - 7 has generated for any Party 19-02, the mandate will indicate it.  Article 19-11 Third Party Participation.  A third Party, upon written notification through its national section of the Secretariat to the disputing Parties, shall be entitled to attend all hearings, to submit written and oral submissions to the arbitral tribunal, and to receive written submissions from the disputing Parties.  Article 19-12 Information and technical advice.  Ex officio or at the request of the disputing Party, the arbitral tribunal may request the information and technical advice of the persons or institutions it deems pertinent.  Article 19-13 Preliminary report.  1. The arbitral tribunal shall issue a preliminary report based on the arguments and communications presented by the disputing Parties and on any information it has received pursuant to article 19-12.  2. Unless the disputing Parties decide otherwise, the arbitral tribunal shall submit to said Parties, within 90 days following the appointment of the last arbitrator, a preliminary report containing:
a) findings of fact, including any arising from a request under paragraph 5 of Article 19-10;  b) the determination as to whether the measure in question is or may be inconsistent with the obligations deriving from this treaty, or is cause for nullification or impairment within the meaning of annex 19-02 or in any other determination requested in the mandate; and  c) the draft final report.
3. The arbitrators may issue written opinions on issues for which there is no unanimity.  4. The disputing Parties may make written observations to the arbitral tribunal on the preliminary report within 15 days following its presentation.  5. In this case, and after examining the written observations, the arbitral tribunal may, ex officio or at the request of any disputing Party:
a) request the observations of any disputing Party;  b) carry out any diligence it deems appropriate; or  c) reconsider the preliminary report.
Article 19-14 Final report.  1. The arbitral tribunal shall notify the disputing Parties of its final report, agreed upon by a majority, and, where appropriate, the written opinions on the issues with respect to which there has been no unanimity, within the following 30 days from the presentation of the preliminary report.  2. Neither the preliminary report nor the final report will reveal the identity of the arbitrators who have voted with the majority or with the minority.  3. The disputing Parties shall confidentially communicate to the Commission the final report within five days following the day on which they were notified, together with all written considerations that a disputing Party wishes to attach.  4. The final report shall be published within 15 days of its communication to the Commission in the Official Gazette of each disputing Party.  Article 19-15 Compliance with the final report.  1. The final report shall be binding on the disputing Parties in the terms and within the terms ordered by it, which shall not exceed three months from its communication to the Commission, unless said Parties agree otherwise.  2. When the final report of the arbitral tribunal declares that the measure is incompatible with this treaty, the Party complained against shall refrain from executing the measure or shall repeal it.  3. When the final report of the arbitral tribunal declares that the measure is cause for nullification or impairment within the meaning of Annex 19-02, it will determine the level of nullification or impairment and may suggest adjustments that it considers mutually satisfactory to the disputing Parties.  Article 19-16 Suspension of benefits.  1. The complaining Party may suspend the defendant Party, the application of benefits derived from this treaty that have equivalent effect to the benefits not received, if the arbitral tribunal resolves:
a) that a measure is incompatible with the obligations of this treaty and the Party complained against does not comply with the final report within the term that the arbitral tribunal has set; or  b) that a measure is cause for nullification or impairment within the meaning of Annex 19-02 and the disputing Parties do not reach a mutually satisfactory settlement of the dispute within the time limit set by the arbitral tribunal.
2. The suspension of benefits will last until the Party complained against complies with the final report or until the disputing Parties reach a mutually satisfactory agreement on the controversy, as the case may be. However, if the Party complained against is made up of two or more Parties, and one of them complies with the final report, or reaches a mutually satisfactory agreement with the complaining Party, the latter must lift the suspension of benefits.  3. In considering the benefits to be suspended under this article:
a) The complaining Party shall first seek to suspend the benefits within the same sector or sectors that are affected by the measure, or by another matter that the arbitral tribunal has considered incompatible with the obligations derived from this treaty, or that would have been cause for annulment. or impairment within the meaning of Exhibit 19-02; and  b) if the complaining Party considers that it is not feasible or effective to suspend benefits in the same sector or sectors, it may suspend benefits in other sectors.
4. At the written request of any disputing Party, after notifying the other Parties through its national section of the Secretariat, the Commission shall set up an arbitral tribunal to determine whether the level of benefits that the complaining Party has suspended in accordance with this article. To the extent possible, the arbitral tribunal will be made up of the same members that made up the one that issued the final report referred to in article 19-14.  5. The proceedings before the arbitral tribunal constituted for the purposes of paragraph 4 shall be processed in accordance with the Model Rules of Procedure. The arbitral tribunal will present its final decision within 60 days following the election of the last arbitrator, or in any other term that the disputing Parties agree.  Article 19-17 Judicial and administrative instances.  1. The Commission will endeavor to agree, as soon as possible, on an appropriate non-binding interpretation or response when:
a) a Party considers that a question of interpretation or application of this treaty, arising or to arise in a judicial or administrative proceeding of another Party, merits interpretation by the Commission; or  b) a Party receives a request for an opinion on a question of interpretation or application of this treaty by a court or administrative organ of that Party.
The Party in whose territory the court or administrative body is located shall submit to them the response of the Commission, in accordance with the procedures of that forum.  2. When the Commission is unable to agree on a response, either Party may submit its own opinion to the court or administrative body, in accordance with the procedures of that forum.  Article 19-18 Alternative means for dispute resolution.  1. Each Party shall promote and facilitate the arbitration procedure and other alternative means for the solution of international commercial disputes between individuals.  2. To this end, each Party shall have adequate procedures to ensure compliance with arbitration agreements and the recognition and enforcement of arbitral awards pronounced in those disputes.
Annex 19-02 Nullification and Impairment
1. The Parties may resort to the dispute settlement mechanism of this chapter when, by virtue of the application of a measure that does not contravene the treaty, they consider that the benefits that they could reasonably have expected to receive from the application of the treaty are annulled or impaired. Chapters III, IV, V, VI, VII, VIII, IX, X, XV and XVI.  2. The Parties may not invoke the annulment or impairment of the provisions of chapters XI, XII, XIII and XIV.
Annex 19-08 CODE OF CONDUCT
AIM
This code of conduct is established to ensure respect for the principles of integrity and impartiality that the Parties grant to the procedures of Chapter XIX of the Free Trade Agreement entered into between the United Mexican States and the Republics of El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras.  The fundamental objective of this code of conduct is that all candidates or members must disclose the existence of any interest, relationship or matter that could affect their independence or impartiality or that could reasonably create an appearance of dishonesty or bias. The appearance of dishonesty or bias exists when a reasonable person, with knowledge of all the relevant circumstances that a reasonable investigation might yield, would conclude that the candidate's or member's ability to carry out their duties with integrity, impartiality and fairly is impaired. competent.  However, this principle should not be construed in such a way that the burden of making detailed disclosures makes it impossible for lawyers or business people to agree to serve as members, thus depriving Parties and participants of what may be the best members. . Consequently, candidates and members should not be required to disclose interests, relationships or issues that have a trivial influence on the procedure.  Candidates and members have a continuing obligation to disclose, throughout the proceedings, interests, relationships and issues that may be linked to the integrity or impartiality of the dispute resolution system. This code of conduct does not determine whether, based on the disclosures made, the Parties will challenge or remove a candidate or member of an arbitral tribunal, or under what circumstances they would do so.
DEFINITIONS
1. For the purposes of this code of conduct, the following means:  assistant : a researcher or a person who provides support to a member, according to the conditions of their appointment;  candidate :
a) an individual whose name appears on a list established pursuant to Article 19-08; or  b) an individual who is being considered for appointment as a member of an arbitral tribunal pursuant to article 19-09; member: a member of an arbitral tribunal constituted in accordance with article 19-09;
staff : with respect to a member, persons other than attendees, who are under their direction and control;  procedure :
a) a proceeding before an arbitral tribunal conducted in accordance with Chapter XIX; or  b) a proceeding dealing with a dispute arising out of Chapters V or XV to which Chapter XIX applies; Y
Secretariat : the Secretariat established in accordance with article 18-02; and  2. Any reference in this code of conduct to an article, annex or chapter, means the corresponding article, annex or chapter of the treaty.
Section A Responsibilities regarding the dispute resolution system.
All candidates, members and former members will maintain a high level of conduct, in such a way that the integrity and impartiality of the dispute resolution system are preserved.
Section B Declaration obligations.
1. Every candidate shall disclose any interest, relationship or matter that could affect his independence or impartiality or that could reasonably create an appearance of dishonesty or bias in the procedure. To that end, candidates will make every reasonable effort to learn of any such interests, relationships, and issues.  2. Candidates will disclose such interests, relationships and issues by completing the Initial Declaration which will be provided by the Secretariat, and submitting it to the Secretariat.  3. Without limiting the generality of the foregoing, each candidate will disclose the following interests, relationships, and issues:
a) any financial or personal interest of the candidate:
i) in the procedure or in its result; and  ii) in an administrative proceeding, an internal legal proceeding or other proceeding before an arbitral tribunal, involving issues that may be decided in the proceeding for which the candidate is being considered;
b) any financial interest of the employer, partner, associate or family member of the candidate:
i) in the procedure or in its result; and  ii) in an administrative proceeding, an internal legal proceeding or other proceeding before an arbitral tribunal, involving issues that may be decided in the proceeding for which the candidate is being considered;
c) any relationship, present or past, of a financial, commercial, professional, family or social nature with any party interested in the proceeding, or with their lawyers, or any relationship of that nature that the employer, partner, associate or member of the candidate's family; and  d) any provision of services as a public defender, or as a legal representative, or of any other type, related to any controversial issue in the procedure or that involves the same assets.
4. Once appointed, members shall continue to make all reasonable efforts to learn of and disclose any interests, relationships or matters referred to in paragraph 1. The obligation to disclose is ongoing and requires each member to disclose any such interests, relationships and issues that may arise at any stage of the proceeding.  5. Each member shall disclose such interests, relationships and issues by communicating them in writing to the Secretariat, for consideration by the appropriate Parties.
Section C Performance of the functions of the candidates and members.
1. Any candidate who agrees to be appointed as a member must be available to perform, and will perform, the duties of a member fully and expeditiously throughout the procedure.  2. The members shall ensure that the Secretariat can establish contact with them, at all reasonable times, in order to carry out the functions of the arbitral tribunal.  3. Every member shall perform her duties fairly and diligently.  4. Every member shall comply with the provisions of Chapter XIX and the model rules of procedure.  5. No member shall deprive the others of the right to participate in all aspects of the proceeding.  6. Members will only consider controversial issues that have arisen in the proceedings and are necessary to reach a decision. Unless otherwise provided in the aforementioned rules, no member shall delegate the duty of deciding to another person.  7. Members will take all reasonable steps to ensure that their assistants and staff comply with Sections A, B and F of this code of conduct.  8. No member shall establish ex parte contacts in the proceedings.  9. No candidate or member shall disclose issues related to violations or potential violations of this code of conduct, unless to the Secretariat or as necessary to find out if the candidate or member has violated or may violate the code.
Section D Independence and impartiality of members.
1. Every member shall be independent and impartial. Each member will act fairly and avoid creating an appearance of dishonesty or bias.  2. No member may be influenced by self-interest, external pressure, political considerations, public pressure, loyalty to a Party or fear of criticism.  3. No member may, directly or indirectly, acquire any obligation or accept any benefit that in any way could interfere, or appear to interfere, with the performance of its duties.  4. No member shall use her position in the arbitral tribunal for personal or private benefit. Each member shall avoid creating the impression that others may influence him. Members will make every effort to prevent or discourage others from creating such influence.  5. No member will allow his judgment or conduct to be influenced by relationships or responsibilities, present or past, of a financial, commercial, professional, family or social nature.  6. Every member will avoid establishing any relationship or acquiring any interest, of a financial nature, that is likely to influence its impartiality or that could reasonably create an appearance of dishonesty or partiality.  
Section E
Specific Obligations.

Any former member shall avoid creating the appearance of having been biased in the performance of his duties as a member or that he could benefit from the decision of the arbitral tribunal.

Section F
Confidentiality.


1. Members or former members shall never disclose or use information related to or acquired during the proceedings that is not in the public domain, except for purposes of the proceedings. In no case, members or ex-members will disclose or use such information to benefit themselves, to benefit others or to adversely affect the interests of others.

2. No member shall disclose an order or decision of an arbitral tribunal, prior to its issuance by the arbitral tribunal.

3. No member shall disclose a report of an arbitral tribunal issued pursuant to chapter XIX prior to its publication by the Commission. Members or former members will never reveal the identity of members who have voted with the majority or minority in a procedure carried out in accordance with chapter XIX.

4. Members or former members will never disclose the deliberations of an arbitral tribunal, or any opinion of a member, except when required by law.

Section G
Attendant and Staff Responsibilities.


Sections A, B and F of this code of conduct also apply to assistants and support staff of the arbitral tribunal.

FREE TRADE AGREEMENT BETWEEN THE UNITED MEXICAN STATES AND THE REPUBLIC OF EL SALVADOR, GUATEMALA AND HONDURAS
PROCEDURE (title) (File number assigned by the Secretariat) INITIAL DECLARATION
I have read the CODE OF CONDUCT FOR DISPUTE SETTLEMENT PROCEDURES OF CHAPTER XIX OF THE FREE TRADE AGREEMENT BETWEEN THE UNITED MEXICAN STATES AND THE REPUBLIC OF EL SALVADOR, GUATEMALA AND HONDURAS (Code of Conduct).
I am fully aware that Section B of the code of conduct requires me to disclose interests, relationships and matters that could affect my independence or impartiality or that could reasonably create an appearance of dishonesty or bias in the above procedure.
I have read the request for review by an arbitral tribunal filed in the above-referenced proceeding and have made every reasonable effort to learn of the existence of any such interest, relationship or matter. I make the following statement fully aware of my duties and obligations derived from the code of conduct.
1. I have no financial or personal interest in the above procedure or its outcome, except as follows:
2. I have no financial or personal interest in an administrative proceeding, domestic judicial proceeding or other proceeding before an arbitral tribunal involving issues that may be decided in the above-mentioned proceeding, except as follows:
3. I am not aware that my employer, partner, associate or any member of my family has a financial interest in the above procedure or in its outcome, except as follows:
4. I am not aware that my employer, partner, associate or any member of my family has an interest of a financial nature in an administrative proceeding, an internal legal proceeding or other proceeding before an arbitral tribunal that involves matters that can be decided in the above procedure, except as follows:
5. I have no relationship, present or past, of a financial, commercial, professional, family or social nature with any of the parties interested in the aforementioned procedure, or with their lawyers, nor am I aware that my employer, partner, associate or member of my family have such a relationship, except as follows:
6. I have not rendered my services as a public defender, or as a legal representative, or of any other type, in a disputed matter in the aforementioned procedure or that involves the same assets, except as follows:
7. I have no interests or relationships, other than those described above, nor have I become aware of any matter that might affect my independence or impartiality or that might reasonably create an appearance of dishonesty or bias, except as follows:
I acknowledge that, once appointed, I have an ongoing obligation to make every reasonable effort to become aware of and disclose any interest, relationship or matter within the scope of section B of the code of conduct that may arise during any phase of the above procedure. in writing to the Secretariat when I find out about it. 
__________________________ Signature __________________________ Name (typed name ) __________________________ Date
Annex 19-10 SAMPLE RULES OF PROCEDURE
DEFINITIONS
1. For the purposes of these Rules, it shall be understood as:
adviser : a person retained by a Party to give it advice or assistance in connection with proceedings before an arbitral tribunal;
non- business day : in respect of a Party, all Saturdays and Sundays, and any other day designated by that Party as non-business and notified to the other Parties;
Respondent Party : the Party or Parties against whom the claim is made, in terms of the definition of the complaining Party;
Disputing Parties : the complaining Party and the defending Party;
Parties involved : the disputing Parties and a third Party;
Complaining Party : the Party making a complaint, which may be made up of one or more Parties:
a) in no case may Mexico file the claim jointly with any other Party; Y
b) El Salvador, Guatemala and Honduras, individually or jointly, may only use this dispute resolution procedure to file claims against Mexico;
responsible section of the Secretariat : the national section of the Secretariat of the defendant Party. In case the defendant Party is made up of two or more Parties, one of its national sections of the Secretariat, chosen by lot, will be the section responsible for the Secretariat;
Secretariat : the Secretariat established in accordance with article 18-02; Y
third Party : a Party, other than a disputing Party, that gives written notice pursuant to Article 19-11.
MANDATE
2. The disputing Parties shall deliver, without delay, the mandate to the responsible section of the Secretariat, who shall immediately deliver it to the arbitral tribunal, once it has been established.
3. If the disputing Parties have not agreed on the mandate after 20 days from the date of delivery of the request for the establishment of the arbitral tribunal, at the request of any Party, a mandate will be delivered under the terms of article 19-10, to the disputing Parties and to the third Party, and to the arbitral tribunal, once it has been established.
WRITINGS AND OTHER DOCUMENTS
4. A Party or the arbitral tribunal, respectively, shall deliver any request, notice, and other document related to the proceeding to the responsible section of the Secretariat, who, in turn, shall forward it as expeditiously as possible to the other Parties involved and to the arbitral tribunal.
5. To the extent possible, each Party involved shall attach an electronic copy of all requests, notices, writings and other documents that they deliver to a responsible section of the Secretariat.
6. The Parties involved will deliver to their responsible section of the Secretariat the original and seven copies of each of their writings and, at the same time, will make a copy of them available to the Embassy of each of the other Parties involved.
7. No later than 10 days after the date on which the arbitral tribunal has been established, the complaining Party shall deliver its initial submission to its responsible section of the Secretariat. Within 20 days from the date of delivery of the initial brief, the Party complained against shall deliver its response brief to its responsible section of the Secretariat. The third Party will deliver its brief to its responsible section of the Secretariat, within the same period in which the defendant Party must submit its own.
8. In the case of any request, notice or other document related to the procedure that is not contemplated by rules 6 and 7, the Party involved must deliver a copy to the other Parties involved by any means of electronic transmission.
9. Minor errors in the form contained in an application, notice, writing or any other document related to the procedure, may be corrected by delivering a new document that clearly identifies the modifications made.
10. When the last day to deliver a document to any section of the Secretariat is a non-business day for said section, or if the offices of that section are closed on that day, due to government order or force majeure, the document may be delivered during the next business day. All delivery of documents related to these rules will be made within the normal working hours of the corresponding offices where the delivery must be made.
OPERATION OF THE ARBITRAL COURT
11. The meetings of the arbitral tribunals will be chaired by their president who, by delegation of the members of the arbitral tribunal, will have the power to make administrative and procedural decisions.
12. Except as otherwise provided in these rules, the arbitral tribunal shall perform its duties by any means of communication, including telephone, fax transmission, or computer links.
13. Only the arbitrators may participate in the deliberations of the arbitral tribunal, unless the latter allows the presence, during said deliberations, of assistants, staff of the Secretariat, interpreters or translators.
14. Regarding procedural issues not provided for in these rules, the arbitral tribunal may apply the procedural rules it deems appropriate, provided they are not incompatible with this treaty.
15. If an arbitrator dies, resigns or is dismissed, a substitute will be appointed, in the most expeditious manner possible, following the same selection procedure used for the appointment of the former.
16. The procedural deadlines will be suspended from the date the arbitrator dies, resigns or is dismissed, until the date the substitute arbitrator joins the arbitral tribunal.
17. After consulting the disputing Parties, the arbitral tribunal may modify the procedural deadlines and make any other procedural or administrative adjustment that may be necessary in the proceeding, such as due to the substitution of an arbitrator or when the Parties must respond in writing to the questions that the arbitral tribunal asks them.
AUDIENCES
18. The president of the arbitral tribunal will set the place, date and time of the hearing in consultation with the Parties involved, the other members of the arbitral tribunal and the responsible section of the Secretariat. The responsible section of the Secretariat will notify the Parties involved in writing about the place, date and time of the hearing.
19. The hearing shall be held in the capital of the Party complained against.
20. With the prior consent of the disputing Parties, the arbitral tribunal may hold additional hearings.
21. All arbitrators must be present at the hearings.
22. The following persons may be present at the hearing:
a) the representatives of the Parties involved;
b) the advisors of the Parties involved, provided that they do not address the arbitral tribunal and that neither they nor their employers or bosses, partners, associates or members of their family have any financial or personal interest in the proceeding;
c) the administrative staff of the Secretariat, interpreters, translators and stenographers; Y
d) assistant referees.
23. No later than five days before the date of the hearing, each Party involved shall deliver to the other Parties involved and to the responsible section of the Secretariat, a list of the persons who, on their behalf, will make oral arguments at the hearing, as well as of the other representatives or advisors who will be present at the meeting.
24. The arbitral tribunal will conduct the hearing as follows and will ensure that the complaining Party and the defendant Party enjoy the same time:
oral arguments
a) Allegation of the complaining Party.
b) Allegation of the defendant.
c) Presentation of the third Party.
Replies and counter-replies
d) Reply of the complaining Party.
e) Counter-reply of the defendant.
25. At any time during the hearing, the arbitral tribunal may ask questions of the Parties involved.
26. The responsible section of the Secretariat will adopt the necessary measures so that the hearing is recorded in writing and, as soon as possible, will deliver to the Parties involved, the other sections of the Secretariat and the arbitral tribunal, a copy of the transcript of the audience.
COMPLEMENTARY WRITINGS
27. At any time during the proceedings, the arbitral tribunal may ask written questions to any of the Parties involved. The arbitral tribunal will deliver the written questions to the Party or Parties to whom they are addressed through the responsible section of the Secretariat. In the most expeditious manner possible, the responsible section of the Secretariat will arrange for the copies of the questions to be delivered to the other sections of the Secretariat and to any other Party involved.
28. The Party concerned to which the arbitral tribunal puts written questions shall deliver a copy of its written response to its national section of the Secretariat. In the most expeditious manner possible, that section of the Secretariat will forward said response to the responsible section of the Secretariat. Also in the most expeditious manner possible, the responsible section of the Secretariat will arrange for the delivery of copies of the response to the other sections of the Secretariat and to the other Parties involved. During the five days following the date of delivery, each Party involved will have the opportunity to make written comments on the response document.
29. Within 10 days of the date of the hearing, the Parties involved may submit to their national section of the Secretariat a supplementary brief on any matter that has arisen during the hearing.
BURDEN OF PROOF REGARDING INCOMPATIBLE MEASURES AND EXCEPTIONS
30. A Party that asserts that a measure of another Party is inconsistent with the provisions of the treaty shall bear the burden of proving that inconsistency.
31. The Party that asserts that a measure is subject to an exception under the treaty shall have the burden of proving that the exception is applicable.
AVAILABILITY OF INFORMATION
32. The Parties shall maintain the confidentiality of the hearings before an arbitral tribunal, the deliberations and the preliminary report, as well as all the writings and communications with the arbitral tribunal, in accordance with the procedures periodically agreed between the representatives of the Parties.
EX PARTE CONTACTS
33. The arbitral tribunal shall refrain from meeting with an involved Party and from establishing contact with it in the absence of the other involved Parties.
34. No arbitrator shall discuss with one or more of the Parties involved any matter related to the proceedings in the absence of the other arbitrators.
TECHNICAL ADVICE
35. No arbitral tribunal, either ex officio or at the request of an involved Party, may collect information or request technical advice from the persons or institutions it deems appropriate after 15 days have elapsed from the date of the hearing.
36. Before the date of selection of the persons or institutions referred to in the preceding paragraph, the Parties involved may submit to the arbitral tribunal written observations on the issues of fact regarding which said persons or institutions must give an opinion.
COMPUTATION OF TERMS
37. When, in accordance with the treaty or these rules, it is required to carry out any action, procedure or procedure, or the arbitral tribunal requires it to be carried out, within a specific period after, before or from a specific date or event, it will not include in calculating the term that specific date or the one on which said event occurs.
38. When, as a consequence of the provisions of Rule 10, a Party involved receives a document:
a) on a date other than that on which the same document is received by any other Party involved; either
b) from another Party involved on a date before or after the date on which it receives the corresponding document from a third Party involved; any period that must begin to run with the receipt of said document shall be calculated from the date of receipt of the last of said documents.
ARBITRATION COURTS FOR SUSPENSION OF BENEFITS
39. These rules shall apply to arbitral tribunals established pursuant to paragraph 4 of article 19-16, except for:
a) the Party requesting the establishment of the arbitral tribunal shall deliver its initial brief to its section of the Secretariat within 10 days after the last arbitrator has been appointed;
b) the Party that must respond shall deliver its brief to its section of the Secretariat within 15 days following the date of delivery of the initial brief;
c) Subject to the time limits established in the treaty and in these rules, the arbitral tribunal shall fix the time limit for the delivery of any additional submissions, including written replies, in such a way that each disputing Party has the opportunity to submit an equal number of submissions. ; Y
d) Unless otherwise agreed by the disputing Parties, the arbitral tribunal may decide not to hold hearings.
RESPONSIBLE SECTION OF THE SECRETARIAT
40. The responsible section of the Secretariat:
